# GameHelper2 — Bug Audit (2026-04-27)

**Scope:** `GameHelper/` and `GameOffsets/` projects.
**Out of scope:** `Launcher/`, `Plugins/`.
**Source baseline:** post `chore(net): relax warnings-as-errors post-migration` commit.

**Phase 1 progress (2026-04-28):** Cluster C1 (coroutine try/catch hygiene), C2 (SafeMemoryHandle robustness), and C3 (JsonHelper atomicity + IO error handling) complete — 12 findings fixed. See spec at `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-04-28-fix-all-high-medium-design.md`.

**Phase 2 progress (2026-04-28):** Cluster C4 (UiElementParents lock symmetry), C5 (GameProcess lifecycle), C7 (RemoteObject lifecycle), and C8 (atomic snapshot-then-publish) complete — 17 additional findings fixed. 29 / 51 high+medium fixed (57%). Phases 3-4 pending.

## Summary

| Severity | Count | Fixed (Phases 1+2) |
|----------|-------|--------------------|
| critical | 0 | 0 |
| high     | 17 | 15 |
| medium   | 34 | 14 |
| low      | 104 | 0 |
| nit      | 33 | 0 |
| **Total**| **188** | **29** |

Coverage: 134 / 134 source files audited.

## Index

- F-001 — `KrangledPassiveDetector` "Generate krangled data.json" handler dereferences nullable JTokens with `#pragma warning disable CS8602`; corrupt or unexpected JSON crashes the render coroutine (low, `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:184-218`)
- F-002 — `ToLower()` without `Invariant` in process-name dictionary (low, `GameOffsets/GameProcessName.cs:14-18`)
- F-003 — `static readonly Dictionary` is mutable (low, `GameOffsets/GameProcessName.cs:12-19`)
- F-004 — Default-constructed `Pattern` NPEs in `ToString()` and consumers (low, `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:8-122`)
- F-005 — `Pattern.ToString` string concatenation in loop (nit, `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:104-121`)
- F-006 — Pattern without `^` marker silently sets `BytesToSkip = -1` (medium, `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:73-82`)
- F-007 — Explicit-`bytesToSkip` constructor does not strip `^` from input (low, `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:92-98`)
- F-008 — `byte.Parse` with bad hex input throws uncaught at startup (low, `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:44-64`)
- F-009 — `static readonly Pattern[]` array is mutable (low, `GameOffsets/StaticOffsetsPatterns.cs:8-105`)
- F-010 — `1 << pos` is `int` shift, not `uint` (low, `GameOffsets/Natives/Util.cs:10-15`)
- F-011 — Public static mutable `Func` fields (low, `GameOffsets/Natives/Util.cs:5-16`)
- F-012 — `StdVector.TotalElements` divides by caller-supplied size with no zero check (low, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdVector.cs:18-21`)
- F-013 — `Size` as `int` silently truncates 64-bit length in `StdList`/`StdMap` (low, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdList.cs:13-18`, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdMap.cs:13-18`)
- F-014 — `Length`/`Capacity` as `int` silently truncates 64-bit length in `StdString`/`StdWString` (low, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdString.cs:7-27`, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdWString.cs:11-31`)
- F-015 — `StdTuple3D` missing constructor (asymmetry with `StdTuple2D`) (nit, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdTuple3D.cs:6-16`)
- F-016 — `StdTuple2D`/`StdTuple3D` `ToString()` formatting is culture-dependent for floating `T` (low, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdTuple2D.cs:17-20`, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdTuple3D.cs:12-15`)
- F-017 — `LoadedFilesRootObject.TotalCount` is mutable `public static int` (low, `GameOffsets/Objects/LoadedFilesOffset.cs:8-12`)
- F-018 — `IGNORE_FIRST_X_AREAS` comment "Feel free to set it to 0" misleads — field is `readonly` (nit, `GameOffsets/Objects/LoadedFilesOffset.cs:32-34`)
- F-019 — `[StructLayout(Explicit, Pack = 1)]` — `Pack` is ignored under `Explicit` layout (nit, `GameOffsets/Objects/GameStateOffsets.cs:13,19`, `GameOffsets/Objects/LoadedFilesOffset.cs:22`, `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameStateOffset.cs:7,15`)
- F-020 — `[StructLayout(Sequential, Pack = 1)]` redundant on `[InlineArray]` struct (nit, `GameOffsets/Objects/GameStateOffsets.cs:26-31`)
- F-021 — `AreaChangeOffset.counter` field name violates PascalCase convention (nit, `GameOffsets/Objects/AreaChangeOffset.cs:8`)
- F-022 — `[StructLayout(Explicit, Pack = 1)]` `Pack` is ignored — extension of F-019 across all 32 audited Component/State/UiElement structs (nit, multiple)
- F-023 — `VitalStruct.CurrentInPercent()` divides by `Unreserved` which can be 0 or negative (medium, `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Life.cs:56-64`)
- F-024 — `WorldDataOffset.CameraStructurePtr` is misnamed — embedded struct, not a pointer (low, `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/WorldDataOffset.cs:15`)
- F-025 — Public static mutable `Func` fields across helper classes — extension of F-011 (low, multiple)
- F-026 — Public static mutable fields that should be `const` or `readonly` — extension of F-017 (low, multiple)
- F-027 — Lowercase / mixed-case public field names violate PascalCase convention — extension of F-021 (nit, multiple)
- F-028 — `RenderOffsets.CharactorModelBounds` typo (should be `CharacterModelBounds`) (nit, `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Render.cs:19`)
- F-029 — `StatusEffectStruct.ToString()` and `DeployedEntityStructure.ToString()` use culture-dependent number formatting (low, `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Buffs.cs:33-38`, `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Actor.cs:105-108`)
- F-030 — `ActiveSkillCooldown.TotalActiveCooldowns()` uses magic-number element size `0x10` (nit, `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Actor.cs:70-73`)
- F-031 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadMemoryArray` compares bytes-read to element count, missing partial reads (high, `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:120-153`)
- F-032 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdList` has no upper bound, will infinite-loop on cycle / torn read (medium, `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:366-387`)
- F-033 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdList` zero-pointer guard runs after the read (low, `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:370-380`)
- F-034 — `SafeMemoryHandle` parameterless constructor leaves handle uninitialised with no diagnostic (medium, `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:31-35`)
- F-035 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadMemory` / `ReadMemoryArray` catch base `Exception`, swallowing OOM and ThreadAbortException (low, `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:85-89, 148-152`)
- F-036 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdString` / `ReadStdWString` silently truncate strings >1000 chars (low, `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:160-191, 198-229`)
- F-037 — `PatternFinder.Find` computes `patternMaxLength` but never uses it; chunks have no overlap (medium, `GameHelper/Utils/PatternFinder.cs:63, 78-92`)
- F-038 — `PatternFinder.Find` writes shared bool/int arrays without synchronisation (low, `GameHelper/Utils/PatternFinder.cs:73-74, 106, 144-148, 156`)
- F-039 — `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` non-atomic write — crash mid-write corrupts user settings (high, `GameHelper/Utils/JsonHelper.cs:42-46`)
- F-040 — `JsonHelper.CreateOrLoadJsonFile` does not handle `JsonReaderException` / `IOException` (high, `GameHelper/Utils/JsonHelper.cs:21-35`)
- F-041 — `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` typo — should be `SaveToFile` (nit, `GameHelper/Utils/JsonHelper.cs:42`)
- F-042 — `DisappearingEntity.UpdateActivation` opens a race window where `isActivated` is transiently `false` (medium, `GameHelper/Cache/DisappearingEntity.cs:137-148`)
- F-043 — `DisappearingEntity` mutable `bool` fields written across threads without `volatile` (low, `GameHelper/Cache/DisappearingEntity.cs:39-40, 90, 134, 139-144, 152, 157, 167, 170`)
- F-044 — `UiElementParents.AddIfNotExists` reads `grandparent.cache` without grandparent's lock (high, `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:51`)
- F-045 — `UiElementParents.OnGameClose` / `OnStateChange` clear the cache without holding `lock (this.cache)` (high, `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:120, 145, 157`)
- F-046 — `UiElementParents.ToImGui` iterates `cache` without lock (medium, `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:127-134`)
- F-047 — `UiElementParents.AddIfNotExists` has empty `if` block on line 53 — confusing control flow (nit, `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:51-72`)
- F-048 — `GameHelperEvents.PostPerFrameDataUpdate` is mutable (no `readonly`) — extension of F-017 in host code (low, `GameHelper/CoroutineEvents/GameHelperEvents.cs:59`)
- F-049 — `GgpkAddresses` / `UiElementParents` start coroutines in constructor with no teardown (low, `GameHelper/Cache/GgpkAddresses.cs:29-30`, `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:39-40`)
- F-050 — `ImGuiHelper.Color(Vector4)` casts truncate instead of rounding (nit, `GameHelper/Utils/ImGuiHelper.cs:66-70`)
- F-051 — `ImGuiHelper.EnumComboBox` and `StatsWidget` allocate per frame in render hot path (low, `GameHelper/Utils/ImGuiHelper.cs:177-181, 325-342`)
- F-052 — `MiscHelper.KillTCPConnectionForProcess` ignores first `GetExtendedTcpTable` error code, allocates with potentially-zero buffer (low, `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:148-156`)
- F-053 — `MiscHelper.KillTCPConnectionForProcess` does not free CoTaskMem on `SetTcpEntry` exception (low, `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:177-182`)
- F-054 — `MiscHelper.TryConvertStringToImGuiGlyphRanges` returns `false` if last element is not `0x00`, even though parsing succeeded (low, `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:51-74`)
- F-055 — `MiscHelper.KeyUp` uses non-thread-safe static `Random`; `Task.Run` exception is unobserved (low, `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:20-22, 109-137`)
- F-056 — `GameProcess.AskUserToSelectClient` Done button clears `clientSelected` before `FindAndOpen` consumes it — multi-instance selection is broken on the typical user timing (high, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:146-227`)
- F-057 — `GameProcess.Open()` does not dispose the previous `Handle` on the retry path (high, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:305-317`)
- F-058 — `GameOverlay.Render` has no `try/catch` — a single exception in any coroutine kills the entire render loop (high, `GameHelper/GameOverlay.cs:85-98`)
- F-059 — `GameProcess.Pid` getter swallows all exceptions and conflates "no game" with "access denied" (medium, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:46-59`)
- F-060 — `GameProcess.Monitor` accesses `HasExited` without try/catch; race with `Close()` throws `InvalidOperationException` (medium, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:245-265`)
- F-061 — `Program.Main` UnhandledException handler calls `Environment.Exit(1)` — skips `using` Dispose, leaks process handle (medium, `GameHelper/Program.cs:22-32`)
- F-062 — `GameProcess.Close` raises `OnClose` *before* disposing the handle — coroutines that wake on `OnClose` can race the still-open handle (medium, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:126-137`)
- F-063 — `GameProcess.Address` has an empty `private set { }` — confusing dead code (nit, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:74-95`)
- F-064 — `GameProcess.FindAndOpen` calls `Process.GetProcesses()` every 2 s — heavy enumeration of all OS processes (low, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:148-185`)
- F-065 — `MainWindowTitle.ToLower()` culture-sensitive comparison — extension of F-002 in host code (low, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:156`)
- F-066 — `Core.cs:166` `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(property.Value, null)` masks a contract violation; `?.` should be `!` (low, `GameHelper/Core.cs:166`)
- F-067 — Win32 P/Invokes (`GetForegroundWindow`, `GetClientRect`, `ClientToScreen`) declared without `SetLastError = true` (low, `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:347-351`)
- F-068 — `Program.Main` writes `Error.log` to a relative path that depends on CWD (low, `GameHelper/Program.cs:25`)
- F-069 — `MiscHelper.GenerateRandomString` allocates a fresh `new Random()` per call; output is the overlay window title — predictability + low entropy (low, `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:80-100`)
- F-070 — `Core.version` is `null!`; `GetVersion().Trim()` NREs if `Initialize()` is skipped (low, `GameHelper/Core.cs:30, 129-132`)
- F-071 — `Core.RemoteObjectsToImGuiCollapsingHeader` reflects over `Core` properties every frame the Debug widget is open (low, `GameHelper/Core.cs:159-169`)
- F-072 — `Core` is `static class`; testability and lifecycle footgun (nit, `GameHelper/Core.cs:25`)
- F-073 — `Core.Overlay = new GameOverlay(...)` happens before `Core.Initialize()` — `version` is null while overlay coroutines are starting (nit, `GameHelper/Program.cs:29`, `GameHelper/Core.cs:102-123, 137-146`, `GameHelper/GameOverlay.cs:24-50`)
- F-074 — `PluginAssemblyLoadContext` is not collectible — plugin DLLs cannot be unloaded for the process lifetime (high, `GameHelper/Plugin/PluginAssemblyLoadContext.cs:6-25`)
- F-075 — `PManager.UnloadPlugin` (DEBUG) does not unload the assembly; method name is misleading (medium, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:75-89`)
- F-076 — `PManager.DrawPluginUiRenderCoroutine` has no per-plugin `try/catch` — a single plugin `DrawUI` exception kills the entire plugin render loop (high, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:253-277`)
- F-077 — `PManager.SavePluginSettingsCoroutine` has no per-plugin `try/catch` — a single plugin `SaveSettings` exception kills the save coroutine (medium, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:241-251`)
- F-078 — `PManager.Plugins` list iterated by render + save coroutines, mutated by DEBUG `LoadPlugin` / `UnloadPlugin` without synchronisation (medium, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:33, 75-116, 207, 246, 268`)
- F-079 — `Parallel.ForEach(Plugins, EnablePluginIfRequired)` calls plugin `OnEnable` from worker threads — plugin authors typically assume single-threaded init (medium, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:45, 219-225`)
- F-080 — `PManager.ReadPluginFiles` catches base `Exception`, swallowing OOM / `BadImageFormatException` distinction (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:125-148`)
- F-081 — `PManager.LoadPlugin(Assembly, ...)` catches base `Exception` around `assembly.GetTypes()` — `ReflectionTypeLoadException` lost (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:164-202`)
- F-082 — DEBUG `PManager.LoadPlugin(string name)` uses `Contains` substring match — picks wrong plugin when names share prefixes (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:91-116`)
- F-083 — `PManager.ReadPluginFiles` glob `{DirName}*.dll` plus `FirstOrDefault` can pick wrong DLL; rename of dir without DLL silently fails (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:129-138`)
- F-084 — `PManager.LoadPluginMetadata` / `SavePluginMetadata` use `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` — non-atomic, no exception handling (high, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:204-217, 227-230, 232-239`)
- F-085 — `PManager.LoadPlugin` derives plugin root via `string.Replace(PluginsDirectory.FullName, PluginsDirectory.Name)` — fragile if any path component duplicates the substring (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:151-162`)
- F-086 — `PCore<TSettings>.DllDirectory` and `.Settings` are public mutable fields, not properties — violates encapsulation; external mutation possible (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PCore.cs:11-22`)
- F-087 — `IPCore` defines no lifecycle hook for game close, render-loop teardown, or `IDisposable` — plugins cannot reliably release native resources (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/IPCore.cs:10-50`)
- F-088 — `PluginMetadata` has no schema version field — future schema changes will fail silently or break user metadata (nit, `GameHelper/Plugin/PluginMetadata.cs:6-12`)
- F-089 — `PManager.UnloadPlugin` (DEBUG) calls `Plugins.Remove(plugin)` inside `foreach (var plugin in Plugins)` — works only because of immediate `return true`; brittle (nit, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:75-89`)
- F-090 — `PManager.LoadPlugin(Assembly, ...)` requires plugin entry class to be `sealed`; missing `sealed` silently rejects plugin with confusing log (low, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:176-184`)
- F-091 — `Activator.CreateInstance(iPluginClasses[0])` requires a parameterless constructor; a plugin with a parameterized ctor fails with no targeted log (nit, `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:187-192`)
- F-092 — `RemoteObjectBase.cs:114` `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(...)` masks contract violation; `?.` should be `!` (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:112-117`)
- F-093 — `RemoteObjectBase` parameterless constructor throws `NotImplementedException` — dead code with no diagnostic value (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:29-32`)
- F-094 — `RemoteObjectBase.GetToImGuiMethods` reflects via `Type.GetProperties` + `Type.GetMethod` per call — extension of F-071 at the base layer (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:144-180`)
- F-095 — `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter holds `updateLock` for the entire `UpdateData` call — readers blocked for the duration of an arbitrary memory-read sequence (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:62-94`)
- F-096 — `RemoteObjectBase.ToImGui` reads `this.address` field directly without lock at line 109 — race with `Address` setter (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:105-119`)
- F-097 — `GameStates.UpdateData(false)` reads/writes `myStaticObj` and `currentStateAddress` without holding `updateLock` while `CleanUpData` clears them inside the lock — torn-read race on game-close (high, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:90-138`)
- F-098 — `GameStates.UpdateData` magic constant `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 0x10` assumes 8-byte pointer (x64-only) (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:108`)
- F-099 — `GameStates.UpdateData` reads `data.States[i]` for `i < 12` then accesses `States[0]` and `States[4]` by hard-coded index — fragile coupling to enum ordering (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:97-103`)
- F-100 — Coroutine bodies in 5 RemoteObject classes have no `try/catch` — extension of F-058 / F-076 at the data-update layer (high, multiple)
- F-101 — `LoadedFiles` debug UI uses `ToLower()` (current culture) on file paths and search text — extension of F-002 (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:89, 103`)
- F-102 — `LoadedFiles.ToImGui` Save button uses `File.WriteAllText` with no atomicity / try-catch — extension of F-039 (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:74-76`)
- F-103 — `LoadedFiles.ToImGui` Save button uses user-controlled `filename` field with no path-traversal sanitization (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:64, 74-76`)
- F-104 — `GameWindowScale.UpdateData` writes 6 floats one-by-one — non-atomic; concurrent reader can see partial state (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameWindowScale.cs:89-100`)
- F-105 — `GameWindowScale.UpdateData` redundant `- 0` and `Cull.Value - Cull.Value` instead of `2 * Cull.Value` (nit, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameWindowScale.cs:92-93`)
- F-106 — `TerrainHeightHelper.UpdateData` replaces the `Values` array reference rather than copying in place — concurrent readers may iterate stale length (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/TerrainHeightHelper.cs:51`)
- F-107 — `TerrainHeightHelper.ToImGui` `string.Join(' ', this.Values)` allocates a string proportional to terrain-height data per render frame (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/TerrainHeightHelper.cs:35`)
- F-108 — `EntitySubtypes.ChestWithRareRarity` doc comment is a copy-paste of `ChestWithMagicRarity` (nit, `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/Entity/EntitySubtypes.cs:32-40`)
- F-109 — `EntityFilterType` member names use ALLCAPS — violates PascalCase + serializes to JSON in that form via `StringEnumConverter` (nit, `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/Entity/EntityFilterType.cs:11-18`)
- F-110 — `GameStats` enum members use snake_case — violates PascalCase, generated by sed pipeline; cast `(GameStats)newStat.key` relies on a fragile +1 offset contract documented only in a NOTE comment (low, `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/GameStats.cs:16-24884`)
- F-111 — `InventoryName` mixes real slots, `DONOTUSE5`, `UNUSED1` placeholders — silent index alignment to .dat file with no compile-time enforcement of the off-by-one comment-documented invariant (low, `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/InventoryName.cs:13-124`)
- F-112 — `ComponentBase.CleanUpData` throws `Exception` unconditionally — propagates out of `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter (high, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ComponentBase.cs:36-39`)
- F-113 — Component `UpdateData` methods never wrap memory reads in try/catch — extension of F-100 across all 22 components (high, multiple)
- F-114 — `MinimapIcon.UpdateData` empty `catch {}` blocks swallow all exceptions silently (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:37-51, 62-74`)
- F-115 — `Mods` and `ObjectMagicProperties` `UpdateData` append to mod lists without clearing — list grows forever on re-update (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Mods.cs:62-69`, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ObjectMagicProperties.cs:79-87`)
- F-116 — `Actor.UpdateData` never clears `ActiveSkills` / `ActiveSkillCooldowns` dictionaries — stale entries persist across skill swaps (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Actor.cs:166, 173-221`)
- F-117 — `MinimapIcon.IconName` never reset when read fails — stale value retained when icon disappears or read errors (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:26, 55-75`)
- F-118 — `Animated.UpdateData` only reads `Path`/`Id` when `hasAddressChanged` — stale data if AnimatedEntityPtr changes at the same component address (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Animated.cs:46-63`)
- F-119 — `Chest.UpdateData` only reads `IsStrongbox`/`IsLabelVisible` when `hasAddressChanged` — strongbox/label-visibility transitions invisible to consumers (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Chest.cs:56-62`)
- F-120 — `StateMachine.UpdateData` has no upper bound on `statesCount` — torn read of StdVector triggers a 2 M-element loop and list allocation (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/StateMachine.cs:34-53`)
- F-121 — `MinimapIcon` performs ad-hoc offset arithmetic (`Address + 0x20`) instead of using a typed offset struct (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:62-72`)

- F-126 — `Stats.IsInShapeshiftedForm = data.ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr != 0x00` compares `IntPtr` to integer literal — should be `IntPtr.Zero` (nit, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Stats.cs:63`)
- F-127 — Component public mutable fields (`Stats.StatsChangedByItems`, `ObjectMagicProperties.Mods`/`ModNames`/`ModStats`) — encapsulation hole + invites unsynchronized iteration (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Stats.cs:22, 27, 32, 37`, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ObjectMagicProperties.cs:38, 43, 48`)

- F-129 — `Buffs.UpdateData` chains `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id` four levels deep with no null guards — NRE if any link is mid-mutation (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Buffs.cs:79`)
- F-130 — `Inventory.UpdateData` `throw new Exception` inside `Parallel.ForEach` worker propagates as `AggregateException`, killing the inventory coroutine (high, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Inventory.cs:182-186`)
- F-131 — `WorldData.UpdateData` writes 64-byte `Matrix4x4 worldToScreenMatrix` non-atomically — concurrent `WorldToScreen` reads can observe a torn matrix (high, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/WorldData.cs:165, 38-115`)
- F-132 — Coroutine bodies in 5 InGameStateObjects + AreaLoadingState classes have no `try/catch` — extension of F-100 / F-113 across this batch (medium, multiple)
- F-133 — `Entity.TryCalculateEntitySubType` throws bare `new Exception` on `Unidentified` and default cases from a `Parallel.ForEach` entity-update worker (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:615-616, 697, 725-726`)
- F-134 — `Entity.TryGetComponent` non-atomic check-then-write on `componentCache` — two parallel callers can race to insert different `T` instances (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:173-202`)
- F-135 — `Entity.TryCalculateEntitySubType` chains `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id` from a parallel entity-update worker (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:653`)
- F-136 — `UiElementBase.this[int i]` allocates a fresh `UiElementBase` per indexer call; combined with recursive `GetUnScaledPosition`, total allocations are O(depth²) (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/UiElement/UiElementBase.cs:144-156, 252-282`)
- F-137 — `UiElementBase.GetUnScaledPosition` unbounded recursion through `parents.GetParent(...)` chain (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/UiElement/UiElementBase.cs:252-282`)
- F-138 — `AreaInstance.GetSubTerrainHeight` `throw new Exception` from inside a `Parallel.For` worker — propagates out of terrain-height build path (medium, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:535-538`)
- F-139 — `Entity.consecutiveInvalidFrames` is a non-atomic `int`, incremented from `Parallel.ForEach` entity loop (low, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:42, 138, 143`, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:296, 308-309`)

## Findings

### Concurrency / coroutine sync

### F-044 — `UiElementParents.AddIfNotExists` reads `grandparent.cache` without grandparent's lock

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 58eaa96
- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:51`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `if (this.grandparent != null && this.grandparent.cache.ContainsKey(address))` reads the grandparent's `Dictionary<IntPtr, UiElementBase>` without acquiring `lock (this.grandparent.cache)`. Grandparent's own `AddIfNotExists` synchronises mutation under `lock (this.cache)`, but the read here does not participate in that synchronisation.
- **Why it's a bug:** `Dictionary<,>` is documented as not thread-safe even for concurrent reader-during-write. A reader during a `Dictionary.Add` (which may grow & rehash internally) can observe a half-built bucket array and either return a wrong answer, throw `IndexOutOfRangeException`, or in rare cases enter an infinite loop in `FindEntry`. `AddIfNotExists` is called per UI element from `UiElementBase.UpdateData`, which runs in `Parallel.ForEach` (`UpdateAllParentsParallel`, line 107). Two parallel adds on a child cache plus a concurrent grandparent read across a single `_buckets` resize is the classic dictionary-corruption case.
- **Suggested fix:** Take the grandparent's lock when reading, or — preferred — switch the underlying storage to `ConcurrentDictionary<IntPtr, UiElementBase>` and drop the manual locking. Today's lock is asymmetric (write under lock, read without), which is the worst pattern.
- **Risk if left:** Crash or stuck thread under load (boss arenas with many UI elements). Symptoms intermittent and hard to repro.

### F-045 — `UiElementParents.OnGameClose` / `OnStateChange` clear the cache without holding `lock (this.cache)`

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 58eaa96
- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:120, 145, 157`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `Clear()` (line 120) and the two coroutine teardown paths (`OnGameClose` line 145, `OnStateChange` line 157) all call `this.cache.Clear()` directly. None of them takes `lock (this.cache)`. Meanwhile `AddIfNotExists` and `UpdateAllParentsParallel` mutate `this.cache` under that lock from parallel threads.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same root cause as F-044. `Dictionary.Clear()` resets internal `_buckets`/`_entries` arrays, and a concurrent `Add`/`TryGetValue` will observe inconsistent state. State-change events fire on the render thread; `AddIfNotExists` fires on parallel entity-reader / UI-element-update threads. This is the live race.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap each `cache.Clear()` in `lock (this.cache) { this.cache.Clear(); }` — minimum change. Better: move to `ConcurrentDictionary` and remove the lock entirely. Same change in `UiElementParents.Clear()` (line 120).
- **Risk if left:** Hard-to-repro crash/hang on area transition (state change), specifically when the UI parent cache is being filled by parallel updaters at the same instant the state-change coroutine fires.

### F-097 — `GameStates.UpdateData(false)` reads/writes `myStaticObj` and `currentStateAddress` without holding `updateLock` while `CleanUpData` clears them inside the lock — torn-read race on game-close

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit c76ccc0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:90-138`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `GameStates` has three private mutable fields: `currentStateAddress`, `currentStateName`, `myStaticObj`. `UpdateData(true)` writes `myStaticObj` (line 95) inside the lock (because it's called from the Address setter). `UpdateData(false)` reads `myStaticObj` (line 107) and writes `currentStateAddress` (line 111). `OnPerFrame` (line 128-138) calls `this.UpdateData(false)` directly *outside* the Address setter — no lock. `CleanUpData` (line 118-126) writes `myStaticObj = default; currentStateAddress = IntPtr.Zero;` inside the lock (called from the Address setter when value transitions to Zero, e.g., on game close).
  
  Concrete race:
  1. `OnPerFrame` coroutine fires `UpdateData(false)`. About to read `myStaticObj.GameState` at line 107.
  2. Concurrently, game-close event sets `Address = IntPtr.Zero`. The setter takes the lock, writes `address = IntPtr.Zero`, calls `CleanUpData`, which assigns `myStaticObj = default;` (struct field write — non-atomic for struct >8 bytes; `GameStateStaticOffset` is 8 bytes (one IntPtr), atomic on x64; OK).
  3. `OnPerFrame` continues reading the now-zeroed `myStaticObj.GameState` (= IntPtr.Zero). `reader.ReadMemory<GameStateOffset>(IntPtr.Zero)` returns `default(GameStateOffset)`.
  4. Then `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 0x10` = `IntPtr.Zero - 0x10` = a large bogus address.
  5. `reader.ReadMemory<IntPtr>(bogus)` returns `default(IntPtr)` = Zero — survives.
  6. The check `cStateAddr != IntPtr.Zero` filters out — no state change recorded. OK by accident.

  But: in the time window between step (1) and step (2), if `OnPerFrame` reads `myStaticObj` (still pointing to valid game state), then the setter swaps in a NEW non-zero address (game restarted, different process), `CleanUpData` doesn't run (only fires for Zero transition). Then `UpdateData(false)` continues using the *old* `myStaticObj` (cached from prior `UpdateData(true)`). Stale `myStaticObj.GameState` is dereferenced in the new process — a foreign address. `ReadMemory` returns garbage, parsed as `GameStateOffset`, leads to `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 0x10` pointing to a random kernel address. Final read returns whatever (or `default`). The state wiring may briefly point to invalid addresses, propagated to `AreaLoading.Address` and `InGameStateObject.Address` on the next `UpdateData(true)`.
  
  The bug surface increases on game-restart (PoE crash → relaunch with no overlay reattach). The `Address` setter only fires `UpdateData(true)` when the address *changes*, but `myStaticObj` is only refreshed when `hasAddressChanged` is true. The `forceUpdate` flag could mitigate, but `GameStates` is constructed with `forceUpdate = false` (the default).
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) take `updateLock` inside `UpdateData(false)` — minimum change but trades F-095 throughput for safety; (b) snapshot `myStaticObj` to a local at the top of `UpdateData(false)` so the read is internally consistent — doesn't fix the cross-process staleness; (c) re-read `myStaticObj` from `this.Address` in `UpdateData(false)` — defeats the cache purpose; (d) split the Address setter so `UpdateData` always runs under the lock for both `hasAddressChanged` and the periodic case — most defensive. Recommend (a) — `OnPerFrame` already yields per render frame, lock contention is bounded.
- **Risk if left:** Intermittent stale-state reads during process re-attach; the symptom is "GameStates briefly reports incorrect state after game restart". Plausibly the source of long-tail user reports of "overlay shows wrong state after I relaunched PoE".

### F-131 — `WorldData.UpdateData` writes 64-byte `Matrix4x4 worldToScreenMatrix` non-atomically — concurrent `WorldToScreen` reads can observe a torn matrix

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit f7ea257
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/WorldData.cs:165, 38-115`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Line 165: `this.worldToScreenMatrix = data.CameraStructurePtr.WorldToScreenMatrix;` — assigns a 16-element `Matrix4x4` (16 × 4 bytes = 64 bytes) field. C# struct assignment to a field is *not* atomic for any struct larger than 8 bytes on x64. Public methods `WorldToScreen(StdTuple3D<float>, float)` (lines 47-77) and `WorldToScreen(Vector2, float)` (lines 85-115) read the field 16 times each (`this.worldToScreenMatrix[j, i]` inside the inner loop, line 63 / 101) — a concurrent reader can observe an arbitrary mix of "old half" and "new half" of the matrix. `UpdateData` is invoked from the `OnPerFrame` coroutine (line 168-178), driven by `GameHelperEvents.PostPerFrameDataUpdate` — render thread. `WorldToScreen` is consumed by *every* radar/overlay plugin, every `ImGuiHelper.DrawText(eRender.WorldPosition, ...)` call (e.g., `AreaInstance.cs:886, 889`) — those calls run on the same render thread, so on the surface synchronous. **However**, plugin host coroutines that subscribe to `GameHelperEvents.OnRender` may run *before* `WorldData.UpdateData` fires on `PostPerFrameDataUpdate` of the same frame, and the order between coroutines yielded on `PerFrameDataUpdate` (which fires before `PostPerFrameDataUpdate`) and `WorldData.OnPerFrame` is sensitive. More importantly, the `Parallel.ForEach` entity-update path in `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` (line 284) runs from worker threads and may indirectly trigger `WorldToScreen`-equivalent computations through plugin code that captures `WorldData` references.
- **Why it's a bug:** Even if today's call graph doesn't expose a parallel reader, the *guarantee* that `WorldToScreen` is consistent rests on accidental sequencing. A torn matrix produces a `WorldToScreen` projection that combines values from camera angle T0 and camera angle T1 — for a moving camera, the result can be wildly off-screen (e.g., a near-zero divisor in the perspective division at line 69 / 107: `tmpResult[i] /= tmpResult[3]`). One-frame UI element jumps; for tools that snap-target based on `WorldToScreen` (radar overlay click-to-target plugins), the click lands at the wrong screen coordinate. Same defect family as F-104 (`GameWindowScale.UpdateData` writes 6 floats one-by-one) and F-124 (`Render.UpdateData` writes `gridPos2D.X/Y` non-atomically) but with much higher per-tear amplification because the matrix is the load-bearing input to a perspective-divide.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) make `worldToScreenMatrix` a reference-type wrapper (`private MatrixBox cache;` where `MatrixBox` is a class with the matrix as a field) — assignment of a class reference is atomic on x64; (b) volatile-write a record-substitution: `private record MatrixSnap(Matrix4x4 M); private MatrixSnap snap = new(Matrix4x4.Identity); ... Volatile.Write(ref this.snap, new MatrixSnap(data.CameraStructurePtr.WorldToScreenMatrix));`; or (c) take a lock around the matrix assignment and the `WorldToScreen` reads. Option (b) is cleanest and matches the suggestion in F-104.
- **Risk if left:** Visible single-frame UI jumps for camera-moving content (boss arenas with rotating cameras, area transitions with camera blends). Click-to-target plugins occasionally click the wrong spot. Severity is high because the failure is user-visible — an entity tracker that points to an off-screen ghost for one frame is exactly the kind of "the overlay glitches sometimes" report that's hard to root-cause.

### F-042 — `DisappearingEntity.UpdateActivation` opens a race window where `isActivated` is transiently `false`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/DisappearingEntity.cs:137-148`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `UpdateActivation` writes `this.isActivated = false;` (line 139), then loops over `environments` and writes `this.isActivated = true;` (line 144) only if a matching env key is found. The bool field is read by `TryAddParallel` (line 90) on parallel entity-reader threads.
- **Why it's a bug:** Between line 139 and the subsequent assignment, `TryAddParallel` running concurrently sees `isActivated == false` and skips caching. For a Breach/Delirium environment that *should* be active across the whole frame, a fraction of entities seen during that window get dropped from the cache and miss the disappearing-entity cleanup downstream. Worst case: when the env is leaving (so the loop never sets `true` again), the field correctly ends as `false` — but on every other frame a parallel reader can intermittently see the transient `false`.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute the new value into a local first, then assign once: `var active = false; foreach (...) if (...) { active = true; break; } this.isActivated = active;`. Also mark the field `volatile` (or use `Volatile.Write`/`Read`) for cross-thread visibility — see F-043.
- **Risk if left:** Intermittent under-caching of disappearing entities — they leak past the cleanup that this class exists to perform, exactly the problem the class was created to solve.

### F-046 — `UiElementParents.ToImGui` iterates `cache` without lock

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 58eaa96
- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:127-134`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `foreach (var (key, value) in this.cache)` iterates the Dictionary directly from the render-thread debug UI. `AddIfNotExists` and `UpdateAllParentsParallel` mutate the same dictionary from parallel threads.
- **Why it's a bug:** Foreach over a Dictionary that mutates concurrently throws `InvalidOperationException("Collection was modified")` from the enumerator. Unlike F-045 (Clear with corruption), this throws cleanly — but the debug UI tab containing this widget will crash or stop rendering whenever a UI element is added during that tab's render frame.
- **Suggested fix:** Snapshot under lock before iterating: `KeyValuePair<IntPtr, UiElementBase>[] snap; lock (this.cache) { snap = this.cache.ToArray(); } foreach (var (k, v) in snap) ...`. Same pattern as `UpdateAllParentsParallel`.
- **Risk if left:** Periodic `InvalidOperationException` whenever the user opens the UI Element Parents debug widget while the game is mutating UI.

### F-062 — `GameProcess.Close` raises `OnClose` *before* disposing the handle — coroutines that wake on `OnClose` can race the still-open handle

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 44c314d
- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:126-137`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `Close()`:
  ```csharp
  CoroutineHandler.RaiseEvent(GameHelperEvents.OnClose);   // line 128
  this.WindowArea = Rectangle.Empty;
  this.Foreground = false;
  this.Handle?.Dispose();                                   // line 131
  this.Information?.Close();                                // line 132
  ```
  `RaiseEvent(OnClose)` synchronously dispatches all yield-on-OnClose coroutines (`Core.GameClosedActions` is the main one, line 271-288 of `Core.cs`). Those coroutines clear the addresses on `States`, `CurrentAreaLoadedFiles`, etc., which triggers `RemoteObjectBase.CleanUpData` paths. *Some of those `CleanUpData` paths can themselves perform reads through `Core.Process.Handle`* (e.g. ImportantUiElements children clean-up that iterates a snapshot read from memory). At the moment `OnClose` fires, `this.Handle` is still open and valid, so the reads succeed but reference about-to-be-stale memory.
  
  More subtle: Coroutines that did not yield on `OnClose` but do hold a reference to `Core.Process.Handle` and run on the next tick after `Close()` — for example any per-frame data update — see `Handle.IsInvalid == true` after line 131 disposes. The window between `OnClose` returning and `Handle.Dispose()` is short (a few statements) but real.
- **Why it's a bug:** The fix is straightforward — dispose the handle *first*, then raise the event. After Dispose, `Handle.IsInvalid == true` and every read primitive in `SafeMemoryHandle` early-returns harmlessly. Subscribers to `OnClose` then see a clean teardown state.
- **Suggested fix:**
  ```csharp
  this.Handle?.Dispose();
  this.Information?.Close();
  this.WindowArea = Rectangle.Empty;
  this.Foreground = false;
  CoroutineHandler.RaiseEvent(GameHelperEvents.OnClose);
  if (monitorForNewGame) CoroutineHandler.Start(this.FindAndOpen());
  ```
- **Risk if left:** `CleanUpData` running with a still-live handle is mostly harmless today, but the inverse — an unsubscribed coroutine running while Handle disposes mid-call — is exactly the source of intermittent "ReadProcessMemory failed" errors during area transitions or game-exit sequences.

### F-078 — `PManager.Plugins` list iterated by render + save coroutines, mutated by DEBUG `LoadPlugin` / `UnloadPlugin` without synchronisation

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:33, 75-116, 207, 246, 268`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `internal static readonly List<PluginContainer> Plugins = new();` is a plain `List<>`. Coroutines `DrawPluginUiRenderCoroutine` (line 253) and `SavePluginSettingsCoroutine` (line 241) iterate it via `foreach`. DEBUG `UnloadPlugin` (line 83) calls `Plugins.Remove(plugin)`, and DEBUG `LoadPlugin(string)` (line 103) goes through `LoadPluginMetadata` (line 207) which calls `Plugins.AddRange(...)`. All paths run on the coroutine/render thread — but the design relies on coroutines being cooperatively scheduled, and the DEBUG path doesn't yield between iteration and mutation.
- **Why it's a bug:** Today the saving grace is that `CoroutineHandler.Tick` is single-threaded and DEBUG `LoadPlugin`/`UnloadPlugin` are presumably triggered from a render-thread debug menu, so no real interleaving occurs. But: (a) `Parallel.ForEach(Plugins, EnablePluginIfRequired)` at line 45 mutates plugin state across threads while the list itself isn't being mutated (safe today, fragile if init code grows), and (b) any future caller that invokes `LoadPlugin` from a worker thread (e.g., a "watch for new plugin DLLs" file watcher) would crash with `InvalidOperationException`. The lack of any synchronisation primitive is a footgun.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) document "Plugins must only be mutated from the render thread, between coroutine yields" via XML doc, (b) replace with `ConcurrentBag<PluginContainer>` or guard with a lock, or (c) move all mutations to a dedicated coroutine that yields on a queue of operations. Minimum-risk fix: add `lock (Plugins) { ... }` around all mutations and snapshots before iteration.
- **Risk if left:** Latent — works today, breaks the moment plugin loading goes async or a debug feature triggers from a non-render thread.

### F-079 — `Parallel.ForEach(Plugins, EnablePluginIfRequired)` calls plugin `OnEnable` from worker threads — plugin authors typically assume single-threaded init

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:45, 219-225`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** During `InitializePlugins`, line 45 runs `Parallel.ForEach(Plugins, EnablePluginIfRequired)`, which calls `container.Plugin.OnEnable(...)` from `ThreadPool` worker threads. `OnEnable` is documented as "Called when the plugin is enabled by the user or when GameOverlay starts and plugin is already enabled" — no documentation that it may be called concurrently with itself for different plugins, and no guarantee that the calling thread is the same one that later calls `DrawSettings`/`DrawUI` (which always run on the render thread).
- **Why it's a bug:** Plugin authors typically initialise ImGui-related state, register event handlers on `GameHelperEvents`, allocate native resources, or load settings from disk in `OnEnable`. Specific defects this opens:
  1. Two plugins both touching `Core.GgpkStringCache` in `OnEnable` may race the cache's coroutine startup if it hasn't run yet.
  2. A plugin that registers a coroutine in `OnEnable` calls `CoroutineHandler.Start` from a worker thread — `CoroutineHandler` documentation isn't checked here, but most coroutine libraries are not thread-safe for registration.
  3. A plugin that reads a settings file via `JsonHelper.CreateOrLoadJsonFile` in `OnEnable` triggers `File.ReadAllText` on a worker — fine, but if two plugins share a settings dir and one creates it (`file.Directory?.Create()`), there's a race window where both call `Create()`.
  4. ImGui state set in `OnEnable` (theme tweaks, font registration) is fundamentally main-thread-only.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop the `Parallel`; use plain `foreach`. The performance saving is negligible — `OnEnable` is called once at startup, not per frame, and total plugin count is small (<20 typical). Replace line 45 with:
  ```csharp
  foreach (var container in Plugins)
  {
      EnablePluginIfRequired(container);
  }
  ```
  Same change inside `LoadPlugins()` is fine to keep parallel — that's just file IO and reflection, no plugin-author code.
- **Risk if left:** Plugin authors hit threading bugs that manifest only at startup, only on multi-core machines, only when the user has multiple plugins enabled. Reproducibility is poor.

### F-095 — `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter holds `updateLock` for the entire `UpdateData` call — readers blocked for the duration of an arbitrary memory-read sequence

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:62-94`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** The `Address` setter takes `lock (this.updateLock)` at line 74, then calls `this.UpdateData(hasAddressChanged)` at line 90 inside the same lock. Derived `UpdateData` implementations perform arbitrary memory reads — `GameStates.UpdateData` (lines 90-115) reads the static offset, the GameStateOffset, then iterates `TOTAL_STATES` reads and sets two child Addresses (each of which acquires *its own* `updateLock` and runs *its own* `UpdateData`); `LoadedFiles.UpdateData` is a no-op (the work is in `OnAreaChange`); but `AreaInstance.UpdateData` and similar do dozens of native reads. The `Address` *getter* (line 64-70) also acquires `updateLock`, so every reader of the property blocks for the entire write+UpdateData duration.
- **Why it's a bug:** Three concrete concerns: (a) Throughput — coroutines that just want to read `Address` (e.g., the `OnPerFrame` coroutines in this batch all start with `if (this.Address != IntPtr.Zero)`) wait on the slowest UpdateData. With `Parallel.ForEach`-based UI tree updates running concurrently with state changes, this is a real serialization point. (b) Recursion footgun — when `GameStates.UpdateData` sets `this.AreaLoading.Address = data.States[0].X`, the AreaLoading lock is acquired *while holding GameStates' lock*. There's no defined lock ordering, so a future change that introduces a reverse-direction set (e.g., AreaLoading triggers GameStates re-read) would deadlock. (c) Liveness — if `UpdateData` throws (no try/catch in the setter), the lock is correctly released by `lock`'s unwind, but the address has been written before the exception — leaving `address = value` but the derived state half-updated. Subsequent readers see an inconsistent object.
- **Suggested fix:** Reduce the lock scope to address-mutation only:
  ```csharp
  set {
      bool hasAddressChanged;
      lock (this.updateLock) {
          hasAddressChanged = this.address != value;
          if (!(hasAddressChanged || this.forceUpdate)) return;
          this.address = value;
      }
      if (value == IntPtr.Zero) { this.CleanUpData(); }
      else {
          using var _ = PerformanceProfiler.Profile(GetType().FullName ?? string.Empty, "UpdateData");
          this.UpdateData(hasAddressChanged);
      }
  }
  ```
  But note this trades lock duration for a fresh race: another writer could set `Address` again while `UpdateData` is mid-execution, producing torn derived state. The proper fix is a queue-of-pending-updates pattern, or — simpler — keep the current lock scope and document "Address setter is serialized; readers block for the duration of UpdateData". Either way, F-097 is a related concern that depends on this design choice.
- **Risk if left:** Latent deadlock potential on any future cross-object Address dependency; throughput cost during state changes; half-updated state if UpdateData throws.

### F-104 — `GameWindowScale.UpdateData` writes 6 floats one-by-one — non-atomic; concurrent reader can see partial state

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit f7ea257
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameWindowScale.cs:89-100`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `UpdateData` writes `this.Values[0..5]` via 6 separate assignments at lines 94-99. The `Values` array is exposed via `public float[] Values { get; }` and consumed by `UiElementBase.Position` / `Size` getters (lines 65, 82, 272 in `UiElementBase.cs`) which call `Core.GameScale.GetScaleValue(scaleIndex, multiplier)` (line 45-66). `GetScaleValue` reads two adjacent slots based on `index` — e.g., `index == 1` reads `Values[0]` and `Values[1]`. The consumer code may run from `UiElementParents.UpdateAllParentsParallel` (a `Parallel.ForEach`-driven update path; see F-044/F-045 for the related cache-mutation race in the same parallel loop). `OnGameMove` / `OnGameForegroundChange` events fire on the render thread but their coroutines write `Values` cooperatively — except the parallel UI updater runs on `ThreadPool` workers concurrently with the cooperative scheduler.
- **Why it's a bug:** `float` writes are atomic on x86/x64 (4-byte aligned), so individual `Values[i]` reads are not torn — but a *consumer* reading `Values[0]` and `Values[1]` in succession can observe a mix of old and new values when an `UpdateData` interleaves between the two reads. Concrete scenario: window resize → `UpdateData` writes `Values[0] = newV1` (old aspect's `Values[1]` still in place) → parallel UI thread reads `Values[0] = newV1, Values[1] = oldV2` → computes a `GetScaleValue` with mismatched X/Y axes → UI element jumps to a wildly wrong position for one frame. Visual flicker on resize. Worse on concurrent foreground change events that invalidate the parallel UI iteration.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) compute new values into 6 locals first, then write all six in a synchronization block (e.g., `lock (this.Values) { ... }` plus the same lock in `GetScaleValue`); (b) replace the array with a `Vector3 widthScales` + `Vector3 heightScales` and write each `Vector3` atomically (Vector3 writes are not atomic either — same problem); or (c) bundle into an immutable record `record ScaleValues(float V1W, float V1H, float V2W, float V2H, float V3W, float V3H)` and replace `Values` field with a single `Volatile.Write(ref _scaleValues, newRecord)` / `Volatile.Read` pair, guaranteeing atomic substitution. (c) is the cleanest.
- **Risk if left:** Intermittent UI element flicker / mispositioning during resize and foreground transitions, particularly visible on the parallel UI tree updater's frames.

### F-124 — `Render.UpdateData` writes `gridPos2D.X`/`Y` non-atomically — concurrent reader can observe torn (newX, oldY) coordinate

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit f7ea257
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Render.cs:76-77`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `UpdateData` writes `this.gridPos2D.X = data.CurrentWorldPosition.X / WorldToGridRatio;` (line 76) then `this.gridPos2D.Y = data.CurrentWorldPosition.Y / WorldToGridRatio;` (line 77). The field `gridPos2D` is `StdTuple3D<float>` (12 bytes — three `float`s). The public `GridPosition` getter returns the field by value (struct copy). A concurrent reader on another thread that copies `gridPos2D` between line 76 and line 77 sees `(newX, oldY, oldZ)` — a torn coordinate. Same defect family as F-104 (`GameWindowScale.UpdateData` writes 6 floats one-by-one).
- **Why it's a bug:** Components are updated from `Entity.UpdateData`, which is invoked from `AreaInstance.UpdateData` running on `Parallel.ForEach` worker threads (`AreaInstance.cs:UpdateData`'s parallel entity loop). Render-thread consumers (radar overlay, position-based filters) read `Render.GridPosition` per frame. A frame that catches the writer mid-`UpdateData` plots the entity at a position with the *new* X coordinate but the *old* Y — visible as a single-frame jitter on radar / pathing for entities that just moved. Worse for entities making large jumps (e.g., teleporting bosses), where the visual jump amplifies the artifact. Also: `gridPos2D.Z` is never written (the property exposes 3D but only X/Y are populated) — Z always reads default `0f`, which the docstring doesn't disclose.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute the new tuple into a local first, then assign once: `this.gridPos2D = new StdTuple3D<float> { X = data.CurrentWorldPosition.X / WorldToGridRatio, Y = data.CurrentWorldPosition.Y / WorldToGridRatio, Z = 0f };`. C# struct assignment to a field is not atomic for a 12-byte struct on x64 either, so a paranoid fix uses `Interlocked.Exchange` on a reference type or moves to per-component locking. The local-then-assign at minimum eliminates the two-step torn-write window. Same shape as F-104's record-substitution suggestion.
- **Risk if left:** Single-frame coordinate jitter on radar/pathfinding consumers; visible for moving entities, especially during teleports.

### F-129 — `Buffs.UpdateData` chains `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id` four levels deep with no null guards — NRE if any link is mid-mutation

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Buffs.cs:79`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Line 79 reads `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id`. Each of the four hops (`Core.States` → `InGameStateObject` → `CurrentAreaInstance` → `Player` → `.Id`) crosses an `RemoteObjectBase` instance whose `Address` setter holds `updateLock` for the duration of `UpdateData` (see F-095). Buffs is a *component on an entity*, so `Entity.UpdateData` calls into `Buffs.UpdateData` from a parallel entity-update worker; concurrently `GameStates.OnPerFrame` (or a state transition coroutine on the render thread) may set `InGameStateObject.Address` to a new value, which clears `CurrentAreaInstance` via `CleanUpData`/`UpdateData`, which clears `Player`, etc.
- **Why it's a bug:** Property accessors on `RemoteObjectBase`-derived classes are typically C#-`internal set { ... }` so null-check is not strictly possible at the type level — but the *initialization sequence* matters. During state changes, a worker thread reading `Core.States.InGameStateObject` sees the new InGameStateObject reference (object refs are atomic on x64), but `.CurrentAreaInstance` may still point to the old AreaInstance whose `Player` field has been zero-cleared. The chain `.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id` then reads `Id` from a Player whose `Address` is `IntPtr.Zero` — `CleanUpData` may have left `Id = 0` or some stale value. Comparing `Player.Id != statusEffectData.SourceEntityId` then proceeds with stale data, may falsely set `FlaskSlot = -1` (line 81) for the local player's own flask buffs.
- **Suggested fix:** Snapshot `Player.Id` once at the top of `UpdateData`: `var playerId = Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id;` — this avoids re-traversing the chain on every iteration, and an exception during the chain traversal at the top of the method (vs mid-loop) is at least localised. For full correctness, wrap in try/catch and bail on null/exception (combine with F-113). Better yet: pass `playerId` to `Buffs.UpdateData` as a parameter from `Entity.UpdateData`, eliminating the cross-state coupling.
- **Risk if left:** Flask-buff misclassification on state changes; rare in practice but a contributing factor to "flask state shows wrong on area transition" reports. NRE not directly observed because `RemoteObjectBase`-derived instances are never null (they exist as long-lived fields), but the deep coupling is fragile and the per-loop cost (4 lock acquisitions) is non-trivial in the StatusEffects iteration loop.

### F-134 — `Entity.TryGetComponent` non-atomic check-then-write on `componentCache` — two parallel callers can race to insert different `T` instances

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:173-202`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `TryGetComponent<T>` does: (1) `componentCache.TryGetValue(name, out var comp)` — return cached if present; (2) `componentAddresses.TryGetValue(name, out var compAddr)` — read the address; (3) `Activator.CreateInstance(typeof(T), compAddr)` — allocate + run constructor (which calls `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter, which calls `UpdateData`); (4) `if (shouldCache) this.componentCache[name] = component;` — write back. `componentCache` is `ConcurrentDictionary<string, ComponentBase>` so step (1) and step (4) are individually thread-safe — but the compound "miss → construct → write" is not. `TryGetComponent` is called from `Entity.UpdateData` (line 419 → `UpdateComponentData` line 339-346), which is invoked from `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` running in `Parallel.ForEach`. It is also called from plugin code that may fan out into its own parallelism.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two parallel callers on the same `Entity` instance both miss step (1), both read the same `compAddr`, both call `Activator.CreateInstance` (allocating two `ComponentBase` instances), and the *last* `componentCache[name] = component` write wins. The other instance is orphaned. The `ComponentBase` constructor calls `Address` setter which acquires its own `updateLock` — but the *two separate instances* have *two separate locks*, so both run `UpdateData` against the same memory simultaneously, racing each other. For components that mutate dictionaries (e.g., `Actor.ActiveSkills`, `Buffs.StatusEffects`), the two parallel UpdateDatas can corrupt their own derived fields. The orphaned instance is GC'd eventually but its internal state may have been partially written before being abandoned.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `componentCache.GetOrAdd(name, n => Activator.CreateInstance(typeof(T), compAddr) as ComponentBase)` — atomic get-or-add. Or hold a per-Entity lock around the miss path. The `GetOrAdd` form may still race the lambda invocation if the dictionary's internal logic invokes the factory more than once — `ConcurrentDictionary.GetOrAdd` documents this as possible. The strict fix is per-name lock with a `Lazy<ComponentBase>` value type, which guarantees single-construction.
- **Risk if left:** Intermittent component-state corruption when the same entity is queried from parallel paths simultaneously. Symptoms: dropped buff updates, missing skill counts on parallel-called entities. Hard to repro because the race is narrow.

### F-135 — `Entity.TryCalculateEntitySubType` chains `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id` from a parallel entity-update worker

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:653`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Line 653: `this.EntitySubtype = this.Id == Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id ? EntitySubtypes.PlayerSelf : EntitySubtypes.PlayerOther;`. Same chain shape as F-129 (`Buffs.UpdateData` Player.Id chain) but in `Entity.TryCalculateEntitySubType`, which is called from `Entity.UpdateData` (line 436), invoked from `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` `Parallel.ForEach` (line 284). Each property hop goes through `RemoteObjectBase.Address` getter (line 64-70), which acquires `updateLock` — four lock acquisitions per Player.Id read.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same race conditions as F-129. During a state transition (`InGameStateObject.Address` being reassigned, `CurrentAreaInstance.Address` cleared via `CleanUpData`, `Player.Address` cleared), a parallel worker reading the chain mid-transition sees an inconsistent state — most commonly `Player.Id == 0` (post-CleanUpData), so any entity whose own Id happens to also be 0 (e.g., torn read returning `default(uint)`) is misclassified as `PlayerSelf`. Plugin UI then highlights a wrong entity as "you". Combined with F-129, every Player.Id lookup in this batch is fragile.
- **Suggested fix:** Snapshot `Player.Id` once at the top of `Entity.UpdateData` (before `TryCalculateEntitySubType`): `var localPlayerId = Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.Id;` and pass it as a parameter to `TryCalculateEntitySubType`. Combined with F-129's fix, this eliminates the deep-chain pattern in two of the three high-frequency call sites in this batch.
- **Risk if left:** Same family as F-129 — rare misclassification of entities as `PlayerSelf` during state transitions; visible as "the overlay highlights the wrong character as me for one frame after I entered the area".

### F-137 — `UiElementBase.GetUnScaledPosition` unbounded recursion through `parents.GetParent(...)` chain

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/UiElement/UiElementBase.cs:252-282`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync (recursion-on-shared-state)
- **Description:** `GetUnScaledPosition` recursively walks the parent chain: `myParent.GetUnScaledPosition()` (line 260). The terminating condition is `TryGetParent` returning `false` or `null` — i.e., reaching the UI tree root. The parent lookup goes through `UiElementParents.GetParent(addr)`, which reads from `Dictionary<IntPtr, UiElementBase>` (locked, see F-044/F-045) — the lookup *can* return a child UiElement whose own parent address points back into the chain. A torn read of UiElement parent pointers from game memory (combined with the `UiElementParents.AddIfNotExists` race in F-044) can produce a cycle in the cached parent chain. `GetUnScaledPosition` recurses through it indefinitely, exhausting the render thread's stack. Render thread default stack is 1 MB on Win64; each `GetUnScaledPosition` frame consumes ~128 bytes (4 locals + return address + this), so ~8000 levels triggers SO. UI trees in PoE rarely exceed 50 levels deep, so a 16x cycle still triggers SO.
- **Why it's a bug:** The render thread's StackOverflowException is uncatchable in C# (the CLR aborts the thread). With F-058 (no try/catch in `Render`), this kills the overlay outright. The bug surface increases with the parent-cache races in F-044/F-045. Independent of those races, a torn `UiElementBase.UpdateData` `data.ParentPtr` read returning a stale value pointing back at this element produces the same cycle.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a depth bound: pass an `int depth` argument to `GetUnScaledPosition` and bail with `relativePosition` after, say, 64 levels (logging once). Or maintain a visited set per call: `HashSet<IntPtr>` of addresses already traversed; if we re-enter, bail. The depth-bound approach is cheaper. Realistic UI trees are < 30 levels.
- **Risk if left:** Hard-to-repro overlay crash on UI tree corruption. With F-058 unfixed, the symptom is "overlay vanishes silently" with no log. With F-058 fixed, a logged StackOverflow is at least diagnosable.

### F-179 — `NearbyVisualization` chains `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.TryGetComponent<Render>` and `.GridHeightData` and `.CurrentWorldInstance.WorldToScreen` from a render-thread coroutine with no null guards

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/NearbyVisualization.cs:41-72`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `NearbyVisualizationRenderCoRoutine` (line 33) on every `OnRender` event:
  - Line 41-42: `if (Core.States.GameCurrentState == GameStateTypes.InGameState && Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.Player.TryGetComponent<Render>(out var r))` — four levels of property chaining (`Core.States` → `InGameStateObject` → `CurrentAreaInstance` → `Player`). Each `RemoteObject` getter goes through `RemoteObjectBase.Address` (acquires `updateLock`).
  - Line 68: `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.GridHeightData[...]` — same chain plus a jagged-array indexer.
  - Line 72: `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentWorldInstance.WorldToScreen(points[i] * gridToWorld, height)` — chains through `CurrentWorldInstance` and reads the `worldToScreenMatrix` (per F-131, this matrix can be torn at the moment a parallel area-change worker is rewriting it).
  
  The `GameCurrentState == InGameState` check at line 41 races against `RemoteEvents.AreaChanged` (which clears `CurrentAreaInstance` via `CleanUpData` before the next `UpdateData` reassigns it). Same family as F-129 (`Buffs.UpdateData` Player.Id chain), F-135 (`Entity.TryCalculateEntitySubType`), F-180 below.
- **Why it's a bug:** During an area transition or game close, any of `InGameStateObject`, `CurrentAreaInstance`, `Player`, `CurrentWorldInstance` can be momentarily reset to a default-valued instance with `Address == IntPtr.Zero`. The coroutine has no `try/catch` (extension of F-100 / F-058), so an NRE here kills the entire `NearbyVisualization` render coroutine. The radar's nearby circles silently disappear and never come back until the user toggles "Nearby Monster Config" Visible off and on (which doesn't actually restart the coroutine — only a process restart fixes it).
- **Suggested fix:** Snapshot the chain into local variables under `try { var inGame = Core.States.InGameStateObject; if (inGame == null) continue; var area = inGame.CurrentAreaInstance; ... }`. Wrap the whole loop body in `try/catch` and log + continue. For the matrix tear (F-131), no fix from this side — must be addressed at `WorldData.UpdateData`.
- **Risk if left:** During a heavy area-change burst (e.g., entering a new map, hideout, town), nearby-circle rendering crashes its coroutine and the user sees no visual indication of inner/outer range until restart.

### F-182 — `PerformanceProfiler.ProfileData.AddFrameSample` mutates `sumFrameNs` (`double`) with raw `+=`/`-=` from worker threads — torn 64-bit double write under contention

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceProfiler.cs:232-243`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `AddFrameSample(double ns)`:
  ```csharp
  recentFrameNs.Enqueue(ns);
  sumFrameNs += ns;       // (B) raw double add
  while (recentFrameNs.Count > WindowSize) {
      if (recentFrameNs.TryDequeue(out double old))
          sumFrameNs -= old;  // (C) raw double subtract
  }
  ```
  `sumFrameNs` is a plain `double` field on the `ProfileData` instance. There is **no `Interlocked.Add(ref double, double)` and no `lock`** here, unlike `AddSample` (F-181) which at least uses `Interlocked.Add(ref long, ...)`. `EndFrame()` (line 168) iterates `CurrentFrameNs` and calls `AddFrameSample` from whatever thread `EndFrame` was invoked on — the render thread (line 71). But `Profile().Dispose()` (line 269) updates `CurrentFrameNs` from instrumented call sites that may run on parallel entity-reader threads or plugin workers.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two concurrent `AddFrameSample` invocations on the same `ProfileData` instance both do read-modify-write on `sumFrameNs` without atomicity. Lost-update window is wider than F-181 because the read-modify-write is not even Interlocked. Worse, `double` is 64-bit; on x86 the CLR does not guarantee atomic 64-bit reads/writes (.NET 10 is x64-only per the migration plan, so 64-bit alignment makes the *single* read or write atomic, but the read-modify-write is still racy). Lost samples mean `AverageFrameNs` slowly drifts away from the true average until the WindowSize cycle dequeues them.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `Interlocked.Add(ref sumFrameNs, ns)` and `Interlocked.Add(ref sumFrameNs, -old)` — `.NET 5+` supports `Interlocked.Add(ref double, double)`. Or hold a per-`ProfileData` lock around the whole Enqueue+Sum mutation.
- **Risk if left:** Profiler "Avg (Frame)" column drifts under contention; profiler is debug-only.

### F-043 — `DisappearingEntity` mutable `bool` fields written across threads without `volatile`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/DisappearingEntity.cs:39-40, 90, 134, 139-144, 152, 157, 167, 170`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `isActivated` is written by render-thread coroutines (`UpdateActivation`, `Clear`) and read by parallel entity-reader threads (`TryAddParallel`, `IsActive`). `isCleanUpTriggered` is written and read inside the same render-thread family but the InvokeLater callback re-enters via the coroutine scheduler. Neither field is `volatile` and neither is fenced.
- **Why it's a bug:** Without a memory fence, parallel readers may keep seeing a stale value from CPU cache for an unbounded period. JIT may also hoist the read out of a loop (`while (!isActivated) { ... }` patterns are unaffected here, but the property `IsActive()` returning `this.isActivated` is consumed by external coroutines that could loop on it).
- **Suggested fix:** Mark both `bool`s as `volatile`, or replace with `int` + `Interlocked.CompareExchange`/`Volatile.Read`/`Write`. ConcurrentDictionary already handles `cache` correctly.
- **Risk if left:** Same family as F-042 — race-induced under-caching, plus latent livelock on any future external poll of `IsActive()`.

### F-049 — `GgpkAddresses` / `UiElementParents` start coroutines in constructor with no teardown

- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/GgpkAddresses.cs:29-30`, `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:39-40`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Both classes call `CoroutineHandler.Start(this.OnGameClose())` and a second coroutine in their constructors. There is no `Dispose`/`Stop` API and no way to unregister these coroutines. The coroutines capture `this` via the iterator method, so each instance keeps itself alive forever (the coroutine handler holds the strong ref).
- **Why it's a bug:** Today, `GgpkAddresses<string>` and `<object>` are static singletons (`Core.GgpkStringCache`/`GgpkObjectCache`) and `UiElementParents` instances are static-readonly or owned by long-lived `ImportantUiElements` — so no live leak. But the API design is a footgun: a future caller that constructs one of these per-area or per-stash inadvertently leaks coroutines and dictionaries forever. The eternal coroutine also means `CoroutineHandler` never reclaims them at shutdown — minor process-exit cleanliness only.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) document "this class must only be constructed as a long-lived singleton" via XML doc, or (b) make the class implement `IDisposable` and store the `CoroutineHandle` returned by `CoroutineHandler.Start` so `Dispose` can stop them, or (c) take an external coroutine-driver argument so the host owns lifetime.
- **Risk if left:** Latent leak if a future refactor instantiates these classes more dynamically.

### F-096 — `RemoteObjectBase.ToImGui` reads `this.address` field directly without lock at line 109 — race with `Address` setter

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:105-119`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Line 109: `ImGuiHelper.IntPtrToImGui("Address", this.address);`. The bare `this.address` field is read directly, bypassing the `Address` property's `lock (this.updateLock)` acquisition. Same field is mutated from the setter under the lock. `ToImGui` runs on the render thread; the setter can run from any coroutine that triggers an Address change.
- **Why it's a bug:** `IntPtr` reads are atomic on x64 (8-byte aligned), so the value read is internally consistent. But under the locking discipline established by the property accessor, the bypass communicates "I don't need a consistent view with concurrent writers" — yet the *reason* the property uses a lock is that derived objects' state may be coupled to `address`. A reader that races a write may display an Address that doesn't match the derived state shown immediately after in the same TreeNode (the `foreach (var property in properties)` block at line 110-118 is independently iterated; a writer could change `address` between line 109 and the property iteration, producing visual inconsistency in the debug widget — the displayed Address belongs to the previous state but the children are from the new state, or vice versa). Same family as F-046 (UI iteration without lock), albeit benign here (no exception, just visual stale-vs-fresh inconsistency).
- **Suggested fix:** Use the property: `ImGuiHelper.IntPtrToImGui("Address", this.Address);`. The minor lock overhead is negligible compared to the ImGui draw cost. Or, if the lock is genuinely too expensive, snapshot at the top of `ToImGui`: `var addrSnap = this.Address;` and use the snapshot consistently.
- **Risk if left:** Cosmetic inconsistency in the debug widget when state changes mid-render; not user-visible in production usage.

### F-106 — `TerrainHeightHelper.UpdateData` replaces the `Values` array reference rather than copying in place — concurrent readers may iterate stale length

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/TerrainHeightHelper.cs:51`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `this.Values = reader.ReadMemoryArray<byte>(this.Address, this.Values.Length);` — replaces the array reference. The new array is sized identically to the old one (length argument is `this.Values.Length`), so the *length* is consistent. But the `Values` property has only a public getter (line 29: `public byte[] Values { get; private set; }`); consumers iterating `Values` may have an old reference for the duration of their loop. Not torn — they see a fully-consistent old snapshot. Just stale.
- **Why it's a bug:** Behavior is actually safe-by-accident: replacing the reference is more atomic than overwriting in place would be (an in-place overwrite would produce torn reads). The concern is the API surface: `public byte[] Values` exposes the underlying array, so a consumer holding an old reference doesn't see updates until they re-read the property. This is silent — a reader expecting "always-fresh" data gets the snapshot at the moment they first dereferenced. Combined with the consumer pattern of `var v = TerrainHeightHelper.Values; for (var i = 0; i < v.Length; i++) ...`, this is fine. But `for (var i = 0; i < TerrainHeightHelper.Values.Length; i++) ...` would iterate the new array's length while indexing the old one — potential OutOfBounds on shrink (which today doesn't happen because `Values.Length` is set in the ctor and never resized; lifetime is process-attach to game-detach).
- **Suggested fix:** Document the snapshot semantic in XML: "Returns a snapshot of terrain height data; subsequent updates do not affect a previously returned reference." Alternatively, expose as `IReadOnlyList<byte>` to discourage direct array reuse, or copy into a caller-provided buffer. Lowest-risk fix: docstring only.
- **Risk if left:** Latent. Today's consumers re-read every frame so staleness is bounded to one frame. A future caller that captures a long-lived reference would observe stale data indefinitely.

### F-125 — `Targetable.cache` 12-byte struct field written in `UpdateData` from worker threads, read from render-thread `ToImGui` without synchronization

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Targetable.cs:17, 53, 36-44`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `private TargetableOffsets cache;` is set inside `UpdateData` (line 53: `this.cache = data;`). `TargetableOffsets` is a 12-byte struct (header + several bools + flags at offsets 0x51-0x5A). The `ToImGui` method reads `this.cache.IsHighlightable`, `this.cache.IsTargetable`, etc. (lines 37-44) without a memory barrier. `UpdateData` runs on parallel entity-update workers; `ToImGui` runs on the render thread.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-124 — non-atomic struct field write/read across threads. Render-thread reads of `cache` while `UpdateData` is mid-write can observe a half-updated struct, producing visually inconsistent flag values in the debug widget (e.g., `IsTargetable=true, HiddenfromPlayer=true` simultaneously, which never actually occurs in-game). Less impactful than F-124 because the values are bools used only by debug UI, but the pattern is the same.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) lock around `this.cache = data;` and the reads, (b) replace `cache` with a reference-type wrapper so the assignment is reference-atomic on x64 (`private TargetableSnapshot cache;` where `TargetableSnapshot` is a class), or (c) drop the cache field entirely and re-read on demand inside `ToImGui` (since `ToImGui` is render-thread-only and can call `Core.Process.Handle.ReadMemory<TargetableOffsets>(this.Address)` itself). Option (c) is the cleanest since the cache exists only for the debug widget.
- **Risk if left:** Cosmetic inconsistency in the debug widget; not user-visible in production usage.

### F-153 — `MapUiElement.UpdateData` writes `shift.X/.Y` and `defaultShift.X/.Y` component-by-component non-atomically

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/UiElement/MapUiElement.cs:70-74`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Lines 70-74:
  ```csharp
  this.shift.X = data.Shift.X;
  this.shift.Y = data.Shift.Y;
  this.defaultShift.X = data.DefaultShift.X;
  this.defaultShift.Y = data.DefaultShift.Y;
  ```
  Same defect family as F-104 (`GameWindowScale.UpdateData` writes 6 floats one-by-one) and F-124 (`Render.UpdateData` writes `gridPos2D.X/Y` non-atomically). `Vector2` is 8 bytes — a *whole-vector* assignment is atomic on x64 (8-byte aligned), but the per-component assignment splits it into two 4-byte writes, each of which is atomic individually but not as a pair. The public `Shift` / `DefaultShift` properties (lines 32-37) return the field by value (struct copy). A render-thread reader copying `shift` between line 70 and line 71 sees `(newX, oldY)`.
- **Why it's a bug:** `MapUiElement.UpdateData` is called from `UiElementBase.UpdateData` which fires per UI element per render frame (driven by parent UpdateData chain). Render-thread radar/minimap consumers read `MiniMap.Shift` / `LargeMap.Shift` to position the player marker on the minimap. A torn shift produces a one-frame jitter: player marker at `(newX, oldY)` instead of `(newX, newY)`. With camera moving rapidly (running through area transitions), the visual jitter is visible. Same shape as F-124.
- **Suggested fix:** Whole-vector assignment: `this.shift = new Vector2(data.Shift.X, data.Shift.Y);` and `this.defaultShift = new Vector2(data.DefaultShift.X, data.DefaultShift.Y);`. The 8-byte aligned `Vector2` write is atomic on x64.
- **Risk if left:** One-frame minimap-marker jitter on map-shift events. Cosmetic.

### F-180 — `OverlayKiller` chains `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentWorldInstance.AreaDetails.IsBattleRoyale` four levels deep on every render frame with no null guards

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/OverlayKiller.cs:37`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `OverlayKillerCoRoutine` (line 32) reads `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentWorldInstance.AreaDetails.IsBattleRoyale` on every `OnRender` (line 37). `AreaDetails` is a `WorldAreaDat` instance whose `UpdateData` may be running on the data-update coroutine concurrently. Each property hop traverses `RemoteObjectBase.Address` getter under `updateLock`. Same chain shape as F-129 / F-135 / F-179.
- **Why it's a bug:** During game-close or `OnAreaChange` (line 57), any of `InGameStateObject`, `CurrentWorldInstance`, `AreaDetails` can be in a transient cleaned-up state with `Address == IntPtr.Zero`, returning default `WorldAreaDat` whose `IsBattleRoyale` is `false`.
