The semantics of "false on transient null" are correct here (we don't want to kill the overlay during area change), so the bug surface is narrower than F-179, but it's still a torn-read producing a one-frame stale boolean. If the *previous* frame correctly identified PvP and started the 20-second countdown, but a frame-by-frame torn `IsBattleRoyale = false` happens to coincide with `OnAreaChange` (line 62 calls `Sw.Restart()`), the countdown silently resets. This is a defensive-programming gap rather than a hard bug.
- **Suggested fix:** Same as F-179 — snapshot the chain, null-check each step, default to "no kill" on torn read but log it so a later audit can correlate the missed countdowns.
- **Risk if left:** Anti-cheat-warning countdown can be silently extended during chaotic area transitions; subtle and arguably *desired* behavior (avoids false PvP detection). No live impact.

### F-181 — `PerformanceProfiler.ProfileData.AddSample` Enqueue then Interlocked.Add(ref sumTicks) is non-atomic — concurrent reader can compute brief inconsistent average

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceProfiler.cs:218-230`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** `AddSample(long ticks)`:
  ```csharp
  Interlocked.Increment(ref totalCount);
  recentTicks.Enqueue(ticks);          // (A) queue grows
  Interlocked.Add(ref sumTicks, ticks); // (B) sum updated
  while (recentTicks.Count > WindowSize) {
      if (recentTicks.TryDequeue(out var old))
          Interlocked.Add(ref sumTicks, -old); // (C) sum decremented
  }
  ```
  Steps (A) → (B) and step (C) are individually atomic, but the compound is not. `AverageTicks` (line 215) computes `sumTicks / recentTicks.Count`. A concurrent reader between (A) and (B) sees `Count` already incremented but `sumTicks` not yet updated — average drops by ~1/Count. Between (C)'s dequeue and the `Interlocked.Add(ref sumTicks, -old)`, sum still includes a value already removed from the queue — average inflates by old/Count. Same family as F-104 / F-124 / F-153 (multi-step writes to fields read concurrently).
- **Why it's a bug:** `Profile()` is called from instrumented call sites (most often at hot loops); `Dispose()` runs on whatever thread the using-block ran. Render-thread `RenderWindow()` (line 48) reads `pd.AverageTicks` and `pd.AverageFrameNs` once per 500 ms. A reader landing in the race window sees a single brief inconsistent sample, which is then averaged into the user-visible "Avg (Call)" / "Avg (Frame)" columns. Since the table is recomputed every 500 ms (line 74), the artifact is short-lived. Cosmetic.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) protect `recentTicks` + `sumTicks` with a single lock (lose lock-free property), or (b) compute `Average = sum / count` with a snapshot copy of both under a brief spin: `var s = Interlocked.Read(ref sumTicks); var c = recentTicks.Count;` — still not perfectly synchronized, but the Interlocked.Read at least guarantees the 64-bit read is not torn.
- **Risk if left:** Occasional one-frame inflated/deflated profiler value; profiler is a debug feature, severity bounded.

### F-183 — `PerformanceProfiler.ProfileData.AverageTicks/AverageFrameNs` checks `!IsEmpty` then divides by `Count` — race-window dequeue produces `Infinity`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceProfiler.cs:215-216`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Concurrency / coroutine sync
- **Description:** Lines 215-216:
  ```csharp
  public double AverageTicks   => !recentTicks.IsEmpty   ? (double)sumTicks   / recentTicks.Count   : 0.0;
  public double AverageFrameNs => !recentFrameNs.IsEmpty ? sumFrameNs         / recentFrameNs.Count : 0.0;
  ```
  The `IsEmpty` check is a snapshot. By the time `recentTicks.Count` is read on the next line, a concurrent `TryDequeue` (from the same `AddSample` while-loop, line 225) may have emptied the queue. `recentTicks.Count == 0` → division `(double) sumTicks / 0` returns `double.PositiveInfinity` (no exception, IEEE 754).
- **Why it's a bug:** The render thread reads `AverageTicks` once per 500 ms (line 97-98) and stores the value into `cachedRows`. A reader landing in this race produces an `Infinity` row, then `FormatTime(Infinity)` (line 193) returns `Infinity ns` (the `>= 1000000000.0` branch evaluates `true` for `Infinity`, divides by 1e9, prints `Infinity s`). The UI shows a corrupt row for 500 ms.
- **Suggested fix:** Snapshot count once: `var c = recentTicks.Count; return c > 0 ? (double)sumTicks / c : 0.0;`. Same for `AverageFrameNs`.
- **Risk if left:** Rare "Avg: Infinity s" cell in the profiler table; profiler is debug-only.


### Process / memory handle lifecycle

### F-057 — `GameProcess.Open()` does not dispose the previous `Handle` on the retry path

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 44c314d
- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:305-317`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Process / memory handle lifecycle
- **Description:** `Open()` writes `this.Handle = new SafeMemoryHandle(this.Information.Id)` (line 307) unconditionally. If a previous attach failed (e.g. user-pick-and-open failure on first try, then a second attempt) or `Open()` is called twice (the multi-instance path: `FindAndOpen` calls `Open()` from line 166 and again from line 177 in different iterations of the same `while (true)`), the previous `SafeMemoryHandle` instance is overwritten without `Dispose()`. The unmanaged Win32 process handle leaks until SafeHandle's finalizer runs (non-deterministic, possibly process-lifetime).
- **Why it's a bug:** SafeMemoryHandle wraps a Win32 `HANDLE` from `OpenProcess(PROCESS_VM_READ | PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION, ...)`. Each leak holds an OS kernel object. Standard idiom for any `IDisposable` field: `this.Handle?.Dispose(); this.Handle = new SafeMemoryHandle(...)`. Same omission applies to the `Information` field — `Open()` doesn't `Information.Close()` the previous one (the previous Process object's wait handle stays open).
  
  Note that `Close()` (line 126-137) does dispose both — it's only the *replacement* path inside `Open()` that's missing the dispose.
- **Suggested fix:**
  ```csharp
  private bool Open()
  {
      this.Handle?.Dispose();
      this.Handle = new SafeMemoryHandle(this.Information.Id);
      if (this.Handle.IsInvalid) return false;
      ...
  }
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Per-failed-attach handle leak. Cumulative under "PoE crashes during play, GameHelper auto-reattaches": each crash leaks one process handle. Over a long session this exhausts OS handle quota or wedges the kernel object table.

### F-034 — `SafeMemoryHandle` parameterless constructor leaves handle uninitialised with no diagnostic

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 9744426
- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:31-35`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Process / memory handle lifecycle
- **Description:** The parameterless constructor `SafeMemoryHandle() : base(true)` writes `"Opening a new handle."` to console but never assigns `this.handle`. The base class default-initialises `handle = invalidHandleValue` (zero) so `IsInvalid` returns true.
- **Why it's a bug:** Every Read* method early-returns silently when `this.IsInvalid`, returning `default(T)` / `Array.Empty<T>()` with no error. If a caller accidentally constructs `new SafeMemoryHandle()` (no PID) instead of `new SafeMemoryHandle(pid)`, every memory read silently returns garbage default values for the lifetime of the process — torn entity reads, missing offsets, blank UI — with no visible error and no exception. The console message says "Opening a new handle" which is actively misleading because no handle was opened.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) make the parameterless constructor `private` so only the framework SafeHandle infrastructure can call it, or (b) throw `InvalidOperationException` from it, or (c) drop it and require a PID. The XML doc gives no caller hint.
- **Risk if left:** A typo or refactor that accidentally bypasses the PID-based ctor produces a zombie reader that swallows everything. Currently no caller invokes this ctor directly, but it's exposed `internal` so anyone in the assembly can.

### F-060 — `GameProcess.Monitor` accesses `HasExited` without try/catch; race with `Close()` throws `InvalidOperationException`

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 44c314d
- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:245-265`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Process / memory handle lifecycle
- **Description:** `Monitor()` is the long-lived per-attach coroutine started in `Open()`. Its body reads `this.Information.HasExited`, `this.Information.MainWindowHandle`, then calls `UpdateIsForeground()` and `UpdateWindowRectangle()` (both of which also touch `Information.MainWindowHandle`). After `this.Information.Close()` is called by `Close()` (line 132), accessing `HasExited` throws `InvalidOperationException("No process is associated with this object.")` and `MainWindowHandle` throws the same. Coroutine startup ordering: `Close()` calls `RaiseEvent(OnClose)` *first* (line 128) which does NOT terminate `Monitor` — `Monitor`'s while-loop only breaks on `HasExited || MainWindowHandle <= 0`. Then `Information.Close()` (line 132) disposes the Process. The next time `Monitor` wakes (after its `yield Wait(1d)`), `HasExited` throws.
- **Why it's a bug:** `Monitor` does not catch the exception. The exception propagates into `Render()` (see F-058) which has no catch either, killing the render loop. The race window is "between `Close()` running and `Monitor`'s 1 s tick firing once more" — expected to fire once in ~1 s, virtually guaranteed.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a short-circuit at the top of `Monitor`:
  ```csharp
  while (true)
  {
      try
      {
          if (this.Information == null || this.Information.HasExited || ...) { ... break; }
          ...
      }
      catch (InvalidOperationException) { break; }
      yield return new Wait(1d);
  }
  ```
  Or, before `RaiseEvent(OnClose)` in `Close()`, signal Monitor to stop via an internal flag. The cleaner fix is to subscribe Monitor to `OnClose` and break.
- **Risk if left:** `InvalidOperationException` propagates up; combined with F-058, the overlay dies silently every time the game exits cleanly via `Close()`.

### F-035 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadMemory` / `ReadMemoryArray` catch base `Exception`, swallowing OOM and ThreadAbortException

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:85-89, 148-152`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Process / memory handle lifecycle
- **Description:** Both methods wrap the read in `try { ... } catch (Exception e) { Console.WriteLine(...); return default; }`. The catch is unfiltered, so `OutOfMemoryException`, `StackOverflowException` (at least the catchable variant), and `ThreadAbortException` (legacy) are all swallowed and the call returns a zeroed result.
- **Why it's a bug:** Standard guidance is "do not catch `System.Exception`; catch the specific exceptions you can recover from." For a memory-read primitive that runs at high frequency, swallowing OOM means the process continues to allocate empty arrays into a half-recovered heap, masking the root cause. The legitimate failure modes here are an internally-thrown `Exception("Failed To Read the Memory ...")` (from the same method) and possibly `AccessViolationException` from the unmanaged read; both could be caught explicitly.
- **Suggested fix:** Catch only `Exception` types this code intentionally throws (or limit to `AccessViolationException`/`Win32Exception`/the local exception class). Re-throw critical exceptions.
- **Risk if left:** OOM diagnosis is harder when memory-read failures are the most frequent log output.

### F-036 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdString` / `ReadStdWString` silently truncate strings >1000 chars

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:160-191, 198-229`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Process / memory handle lifecycle
- **Description:** Both methods early-return `string.Empty` when `Length > 1000` or `Capacity > 1000`. The constant has no XML-doc rationale and no log when the limit is exceeded.
- **Why it's a bug:** Long strings (e.g., a future entity path or buff metadata that grows with patches) are silently dropped to empty. The caller can't distinguish "string was empty" from "string was too long". For a bounded sanity check, 1000 is fine for current POE — but the silence is the bug. A torn read can also produce huge `Length` values and would correctly hit this guard, but again with no signal.
- **Suggested fix:** Log once (rate-limited) when the cap fires; or expose the cap as a `const` with a clear name and call site comment. Optionally accept an out-bool to distinguish empty from truncated.
- **Risk if left:** Silent data loss when the game adds a long path; debugging requires reading source to understand why the string disappeared.


### Exception handling

### F-040 — `JsonHelper.CreateOrLoadJsonFile` does not handle `JsonReaderException` / `IOException`

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit e2a91a3
- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/JsonHelper.cs:21-35`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `CreateOrLoadJsonFile` reads the file and calls `JsonConvert.DeserializeObject<T>(content)`. If the file is corrupt (truncated by a prior crash mid-write — see F-039), unparseable, or the schema has changed, `JsonConvert` throws `JsonReaderException`/`JsonSerializationException`. There is no `try/catch`. The caller (`Core.GHSettings`, plugin settings, etc.) propagates the exception out of `Core` static initialisation and the application fails to start.
- **Why it's a bug:** The user's settings file can be corrupted by:
  1. A power loss / OS crash during `SafeToFile` — file is half-written (see F-039).
  2. A user editing the JSON file by hand and making a syntax error.
  3. A plugin DLL change that renames a property and old data fails to deserialize.
  In all three cases, the user-visible failure is "GameHelper won't start" with a stack trace they can't act on. The defensive behaviour is to fall back to a fresh `new T()` (the same path the file-doesn't-exist branch uses), and ideally rename the bad file aside (e.g., `<file>.corrupt-<timestamp>.json`) so the user can inspect it.
- **Suggested fix:**
  ```csharp
  try { return JsonConvert.DeserializeObject<T>(content) ?? new T(); }
  catch (JsonException) {
      // rename file aside, log, fall through to fresh defaults
      try { file.MoveTo(file.FullName + $".corrupt-{DateTime.UtcNow:yyyyMMdd-HHmmss}.json"); } catch {}
      var fresh = new T(); SafeToFile(fresh, file); return fresh;
  }
  ```
- **Risk if left:** A single power-loss during settings save bricks the user's GameHelper installation until they manually delete the file.

### F-058 — `GameOverlay.Render` has no `try/catch` — a single exception in any coroutine kills the entire render loop

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit a2748a0
- **File:** `GameHelper/GameOverlay.cs:85-98`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `Render()` calls `CoroutineHandler.Tick(...)` then four `RaiseEvent` calls (`PerFrameDataUpdate`, `PostPerFrameDataUpdate`, `OnRender`, `OnPostRender`). The Coroutine library does not catch user-coroutine exceptions internally — a `MoveNext()` that throws propagates back to `Tick`/`RaiseEvent`. Any exception thrown by *any* coroutine yielded on any of these events propagates up through `Render()` into `Overlay.RunMessagePump` (the upstream library's render thread). The base `Overlay` class also does not catch — the exception kills the render thread and the overlay closes silently.
- **Why it's a bug:** Render is called per frame. Coroutines that subscribe to `PerFrameDataUpdate` include the entire entity reader, every plugin's update path, etc. Any one of them throwing — a torn memory read, a `null` deref in plugin code, an `InvalidOperationException` from a Dictionary mutation race (see F-046) — takes down the entire overlay with no log, no recovery, no notification to the user. The user sees the overlay vanish for "no reason".
  
  Additionally, the four `RaiseEvent` calls are not isolated: if `PerFrameDataUpdate` throws, `PostPerFrameDataUpdate`, `OnRender`, `OnPostRender` are *all* skipped that frame. Plugins that rely on `OnRender` to draw UI miss frames every time a sibling plugin throws.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap each event invocation in its own `try/catch`:
  ```csharp
  protected override void Render()
  {
      PerformanceProfiler.StartFrame();
      try { CoroutineHandler.Tick(ImGui.GetIO().DeltaTime); }
      catch (Exception ex) { Console.WriteLine($"[Render] Tick: {ex}"); }
      foreach (var evt in new[] { PerFrameDataUpdate, PostPerFrameDataUpdate, OnRender, OnPostRender })
          try { CoroutineHandler.RaiseEvent(evt); } catch (Exception ex) { Console.WriteLine($"[Render] {evt}: {ex}"); }
      ...
  }
  ```
  Plus log to `Error.log` (see F-068) so users can report the cause.
- **Risk if left:** Any coroutine bug — including ones outside this code's control, e.g. a third-party plugin — silently kills the overlay. The user has no diagnostic.

### F-076 — `PManager.DrawPluginUiRenderCoroutine` has no per-plugin `try/catch` — a single plugin `DrawUI` exception kills the entire plugin render loop

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit a2748a0
- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:253-277`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** The coroutine is `while (true) { yield return new Wait(GameHelperEvents.OnRender); ... foreach (var container in Plugins) { ... container.Plugin.DrawUI(); } }`. The plugin's `DrawUI()` is invoked directly with no exception handler. If any plugin throws (e.g., null deref on a missing entity, divide-by-zero on a stat, ImGui state mismatch), the coroutine bubbles the exception. `CoroutineHandler.Tick()` will surface this to the caller (most likely caught in `GameOverlay.Render`'s outer scaffolding — see F-058 — which currently has no `try/catch` either). The "[PManager] Draw Plugins UI" coroutine name is registered with `CoroutineHandler.Start`; once it throws, that named coroutine is dead and **no plugin UI renders again** until the host restarts.
- **Why it's a bug:** A single buggy plugin permanently disables all other plugins' UI for the rest of the session. Same defect family as F-058 (`GameOverlay.Render` no try/catch around coroutine ticks), but at the plugin-loop level this is more impactful because plugins are user-installed third-party code with much higher defect probability than core code. The performance profiler `using var _ = PerformanceProfiler.Profile(...)` would also leak its `IDisposable` if the throw came from inside `Profile`.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the per-plugin call in `try/catch`, log to console (with plugin name), and continue:
  ```csharp
  foreach (var container in Plugins)
  {
      if (!container.Metadata.Enable) continue;
      try
      {
          using var _ = PerformanceProfiler.Profile(container.Plugin.GetType().FullName ?? string.Empty, "DrawUI");
          container.Plugin.DrawUI();
      }
      catch (Exception ex)
      {
          Console.WriteLine($"Plugin {container.Name} DrawUI threw: {ex}");
          // optional: auto-disable plugin after N consecutive throws
      }
  }
  ```
  Optionally combine with rate-limited error throttling so an exception every frame doesn't flood the console.
- **Risk if left:** Any plugin defect causes total plugin UI blackout. Users see one plugin "stop working" but actually all plugins silently stopped — UX nightmare for support and for plugin authors trying to repro.

### F-100 — Coroutine bodies in 5 RemoteObject classes have no `try/catch` — extension of F-058 / F-076 at the data-update layer

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit a2748a0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/AreaChangeCounter.cs:57-67` (`OnAreaChange`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:128-138` (`OnPerFrame`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameWindowCull.cs:57-79` (`OnGameMove`, `OnGameForegroundChange`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameWindowScale.cs:102-124` (`OnGameMove`, `OnGameForegroundChange`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:168-200` (`OnAreaChange`)
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Each coroutine body is `while (true) { yield return new Wait(...); ... this.UpdateData(...); }` (or equivalent) with no `try/catch` around the work. `UpdateData` reads memory through `Core.Process.Handle`, which has its own internal exception swallowing (F-035) — but anything outside that primitive (struct accessors, property/getter chains, `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.AreaHash` chain in `LoadedFiles.OnAreaChange`) can throw NullReferenceException, InvalidCastException, or similar. The throw propagates out of the iterator's `MoveNext`, into `CoroutineHandler.Tick`, up into `GameOverlay.Render` (where F-058 documents no catch). The coroutine is dead for the rest of the session.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same defect family as F-058 (overlay-level no try/catch) and F-076 (plugin DrawUI no try/catch), but at a different layer. Concrete impact: an `AreaChanged` event with a transiently-bad memory state — common during area transition — can throw inside `LoadedFiles.OnAreaChange` (e.g., `Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentWorldInstance.AreaDetails.IsHideout` evaluates four chained property reads on objects that may be in mid-update). Once `LoadedFiles.OnAreaChange` dies, *no preload data is ever scanned again* until the user restarts the overlay. Same cascade for `GameStates.OnPerFrame` (no current-state tracking), `AreaChangeCounter.OnAreaChange` (counter frozen at int.MaxValue or last value), and `GameWindowCull/Scale` (overlay positioning frozen at last computed values, leading to UI elements rendered at wrong coordinates after a window resize). Combined with F-058, the entire render loop also dies if the throw happens inside the Tick rather than inside an event handler — same cascade as F-076.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the body of each `while (true) { ... }` in `try { ... } catch (Exception ex) { Console.WriteLine($"[{nameof(ClassName)}.{nameof(MethodName)}] {ex}"); }` so a single bad iteration doesn't kill the coroutine. The `yield return` must be outside the try (Coroutine library limitation: yield-in-catch is illegal). Standard pattern:
  ```csharp
  while (true) {
      yield return new Wait(EventName);
      try {
          if (this.Address != IntPtr.Zero) this.UpdateData(false);
      } catch (Exception ex) {
          Console.WriteLine($"[{className}.{methodName}] {ex}");
      }
  }
  ```
  Apply uniformly to all 5 classes.
- **Risk if left:** Same defect family as F-058 — a single bad memory read silently disables an entire subsystem (preload tracking, state tracking, area-change tracking, or window-size tracking) until the user restarts the overlay. Symptoms: "preloads stopped working" / "current state always reports old value" / "UI elements off-screen after I resized" with no diagnostic.

### F-112 — `ComponentBase.CleanUpData` throws `Exception` unconditionally — propagates out of `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit c76ccc0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ComponentBase.cs:36-39`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `protected override void CleanUpData() { throw new Exception("Component Address should never be Zero."); }`. `CleanUpData` is invoked by `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter (line 85 of `RemoteObjectBase.cs`) when `value == IntPtr.Zero`. The setter holds `updateLock` while calling `CleanUpData`. Throwing here propagates out through the lock (lock unwinds correctly) and continues up the stack — typically into `Entity.UpdateData`'s `UpdateComponentData` loop (line 339-346 of `Entity.cs`: `kv.Value.Address = kv.Value.Address;`), or into wherever else a component's address transitions to zero.
- **Why it's a bug:** The exception type is `Exception` (the base type) — Microsoft guidance says never throw the base `Exception` type. The message "should never be Zero" is a developer-debug-only assertion masquerading as runtime behavior. In practice, an entity's component can transition to `Zero` legitimately when:
  1. The entity is being recycled by the game (component swap during enemy phase change, transition between alive/dead states, vendor-trashing items).
  2. A torn memory read returns a `Zero` for `componentAddresses[name]` mid-update (the game patches the array; happens near area transitions).
  3. A plugin or test instantiates a `ComponentBase` directly with a zero address (no compile-time gate prevents this — the public ctor accepts any IntPtr).
  In all three cases, the exception kills the `Entity.UpdateData` coroutine (combined with F-100/F-113, the entity reader dies for the rest of the session). The intended behavior is "if my address went to zero, clean up" — but the implementation is "no, that's an error".
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) override `CleanUpData` as `{ this.OwnerEntityAddress = IntPtr.Zero; }` — actual cleanup of the only mutable field in the base — and let derived classes override to clean their own state; or (b) make it a no-op `{ }` and add a `Debug.Assert` if the developer wants the diagnostic in debug builds. Option (a) is the correct default. Each derived component then optionally overrides for additional cleanup (Buffs.StatusEffects.Clear(), Actor.ActiveSkills.Clear(), etc.).
- **Risk if left:** Any component whose address legitimately transitions to zero kills the entity reader coroutine. Combined with F-113, no further entity updates happen until restart. Symptom: "entities stop refreshing after I entered area X".

### F-113 — Component `UpdateData` methods never wrap memory reads in try/catch — extension of F-100 across all 22 components

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 7dc2cb9
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Actor.cs:160-233`, `Animated.cs:46-63`, `Buffs.cs:63-119`, `Charges.cs:44-54`, `Chest.cs:51-63`, `ComponentBase.cs:49-53`, `Life.cs:71-80`, `MinimapIcon.cs:55-75`, `Mods.cs:55-70`, `ObjectMagicProperties.cs:72-89`, `Player.cs:50-63`, `Positioned.cs:46-53`, `Render.cs:68-78`, `Shrine.cs:38-44`, `Stack.cs:20-26`, `StateMachine.cs:28-54`, `Stats.cs:57-75`, `Targetable.cs:48-56`, `Transitionable.cs:40-46`, `TriggerableBlockage.cs:38-44` (DiesAfterTime, NPC have no UpdateData)
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Every component's `UpdateData` reads memory via `Core.Process.Handle.ReadMemory<T>`/`ReadStdVector`/`ReadStdString` and dereferences pointers without `try/catch`. The primitive `ReadMemory` itself catches and returns `default(T)` (see F-035), so most read failures are silent — but downstream code can still throw:
  - `MiscHelper.ActiveSkillGemDataParser` is called in `Actor` and `Buffs` and may throw on malformed data;
  - `Core.GgpkObjectCache.AddOrGetExisting` invokes a producer lambda that itself reads memory;
  - `(Rarity)data.Details0.Rarity` casts an int to enum — out-of-range values throw on enum-validation paths;
  - Dictionary `Add`/`AddOrUpdate` can throw on null keys (if `effectName` ever becomes null due to a torn read returning empty string + ConcatString of unknownId producing null);
  - `reader.ReadStdWString` (in Animated, Player) returns `string.Empty` on torn reads, but if the StdWString header itself is partially garbage, `Marshal.PtrToStructure` may throw `AccessViolationException`.
  Any throw propagates up to `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter, releases the lock, and continues into `Entity.UpdateData`/`AreaInstance.UpdateData`. Under F-100/F-058, that coroutine dies for the rest of the session.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same root concern as F-100 (5 RemoteObject classes lack try/catch around UpdateData) but at the component layer — and components fire much more frequently (per-entity per-frame vs. per-state). One torn read on one entity's component → entity reader is dead → no entity updates until restart. The components fan-out is wider than F-100's classes, so the probability of a throw per session is correspondingly higher.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap each `UpdateData` body in a single try/catch that logs and swallows. Better: add a single `try` at the call site in `Entity.UpdateComponentData` / `Activator.CreateInstance(...)` so that one component-throw doesn't break the entity, while another component still receives its update. Even better: make `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter's `UpdateData` call try-catch-and-log, so all 30+ derived classes inherit safety. Same fix as F-100 but at the parent layer.
- **Risk if left:** Same impact family as F-100 — a single bad memory read kills the entity reader. Symptoms vary by which component throws: "buffs stop updating", "skills stop updating", "items missing mods", etc.

### F-130 — `Inventory.UpdateData` `throw new Exception` inside `Parallel.ForEach` worker propagates as `AggregateException`, killing the inventory coroutine

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Inventory.cs:182-186`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Lines 182-186:
  ```csharp
  if (!this.Items.TryAdd(invItemPtr, item))
  {
      throw new Exception("Failed to add item into the Inventory Item Dict.");
  }
  ```
  This `throw` happens inside the body of `Parallel.ForEach(this.itemsToInventorySlotMapping.Distinct(), invItemPtr => { ... })` (line 168). `Parallel.ForEach` aggregates worker exceptions into an `AggregateException` and rethrows from the calling thread when the iteration completes. The throw is reached when `TryAdd` returns false, which happens whenever two parallel workers attempt to insert the same `invItemPtr` (legitimate race on duplicate item pointers — `Distinct()` runs over a snapshot, but a separate snapshot in the next 50 Hz tick may see the same pointer in transit). It also fires if `ConcurrentDictionary` rejects the add for any internal reason.
- **Why it's a bug:** The `OnTimeTick` coroutine (line 200-210) has no try/catch. The thrown `AggregateException` propagates up through `Parallel.ForEach` → `UpdateData` → `OnTimeTick`'s while-loop, into `CoroutineHandler.Tick` (driven from `GameOverlay.Render` which itself has no try/catch — see F-058). The end result: the Inventory coroutine *and* the entire render loop die on a single TryAdd-returns-false event. The user's flask UI freezes; manual restart required.
  
  Same defect family as F-100 (no try/catch in coroutines), but at the data-update layer, and worse because `Parallel.ForEach` aggregates and rethrows. The thrown `Exception` is also bare base `Exception` — Microsoft guidance says never throw the base type. The condition itself ("TryAdd returned false") isn't even fatal — it just means the item was already added by another worker, which is a legitimate concurrent state, not an error.
- **Suggested fix:** Two changes. (a) Replace the throw with a no-op or a debug-log: `if (!this.Items.TryAdd(invItemPtr, item)) { /* already added by another worker — fine */ }`. The `TryAdd`-returns-false branch is non-fatal. (b) Wrap the body of `OnTimeTick` in try/catch per F-100 pattern. Even if (a) is applied, future reads/writes inside `Parallel.ForEach` may still throw.
- **Risk if left:** Inventory updates intermittently kill the entire overlay's render loop on a duplicate-item-ptr race. User sees "overlay vanished after I picked up a stack of currency" with no diagnostic. Compound with F-058 (overlay no try/catch) — the entire process becomes brittle.

### F-059 — `GameProcess.Pid` getter swallows all exceptions and conflates "no game" with "access denied"

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 44c314d
- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:46-59`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `Pid` returns `(uint)this.Information.Id` inside a bare `try { ... } catch { return 0; }`. The `Information` field is `null!` until first `FindAndOpen` succeeds; accessing `.Id` on null throws `NullReferenceException`. Once `Information` is populated, `.Id` can throw `InvalidOperationException` ("Process has exited") or `Win32Exception` (access denied). All three are caught and reported as `0`.
- **Why it's a bug:** A caller checking `if (Pid == 0) { /* no game */ }` cannot distinguish:
  1. **No game running** — first `FindAndOpen` hasn't set `Information` yet. Recoverable, just wait.
  2. **Game crashed during read** — `Information.Id` throws `InvalidOperationException`. Not recoverable from the same `Information` reference; needs `Close()` and re-attach.
  3. **Permission lost** — game restarted as admin, current GameHelper instance can no longer read. Recoverable by relaunching as admin or releasing.
  
  All three become "Pid = 0" and the caller's heuristic — typically retry — is wrong for case (2) and (3). The Win32-exception case is particularly bad because every read attempt swallows the error.
- **Suggested fix:** Either:
  - Return nullable `uint?` and let `null` mean "unavailable", with a separate diagnostic API; or
  - Rethrow `InvalidOperationException` (game exited) so callers can re-attach; or
  - Add an internal `LastPidError` field with the exception, and log it on first observation.
- **Risk if left:** Diagnostic black hole — bugs caused by access-denied or process-already-exited states manifest only as "everything reads zero", with no exception to chase.

### F-077 — `PManager.SavePluginSettingsCoroutine` has no per-plugin `try/catch` — a single plugin `SaveSettings` exception kills the save coroutine

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit a2748a0
- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:241-251`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Same shape as F-076 but for the periodic settings save: `while (true) { yield return new Wait(GameHelperEvents.TimeToSaveAllSettings); foreach (var container in Plugins) container.Plugin.SaveSettings(); }`. No try/catch. If one plugin throws on save (e.g., `IOException` writing to read-only disk, `JsonSerializationException` on a malformed settings field), the coroutine dies. Subsequent `TimeToSaveAllSettings` events fire to no listeners — **no plugin saves settings anymore** until restart.
- **Why it's a bug:** Silent permanent-data-loss. The user shuts down the overlay believing settings auto-saved; instead, every plugin's in-memory settings are lost. Combined with F-076, an unhandled plugin exception cascades: `DrawUI` throws → render coroutine dies → `SaveSettings` then can't run via the "save on shutdown" path either.
- **Suggested fix:** Same pattern as F-076: per-plugin try/catch, log with plugin name, continue. Note this coroutine is not registered in `Core.CoroutinesRegistrar` so there's no list-based diagnostic that it died.
- **Risk if left:** Loss of all plugin settings across all plugins after one misbehaving plugin throws once during save.

### F-114 — `MinimapIcon.UpdateData` empty `catch {}` blocks swallow all exceptions silently

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit c76ccc0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:37-51, 62-74`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `TryReadUtf16String` (line 36-52) and the offset-arithmetic block in `UpdateData` (lines 62-74) both use `try { ... } catch { }` with no log, no rethrow, no error category check. The `TryReadUtf16String` catch is at line 50; the `UpdateData` outer catch is at line 74. An `OutOfMemoryException`, `AccessViolationException`, or any other exception is silently dropped.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two issues. (a) The empty-catch-everything pattern is the strongest form of F-035 / F-080 — even base `Exception` is too narrow compared to a bare `catch`. `OutOfMemoryException` and `StackOverflowException` (the catchable variant) are masked. (b) The first catch-all (`TryReadUtf16String`) returning `null` and the outer catch-all (`UpdateData`) leaving `IconName` un-updated means `MinimapIcon` silently fails forever for any entity whose memory is unreadable — combined with F-117 (no reset of `IconName`), the field reads as the previous value or null permanently. Plugin authors using `MinimapIcon.IconName` to identify breach/expedition icons will see false positives/negatives for affected entities.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) drop the empty catches and let exceptions propagate (the Address setter unwinds the lock; combined with F-113's outer try/catch, the symptom is logged and the component is skipped for that frame), or (b) catch only `AccessViolationException` and rethrow other types, with a single console log per occurrence. Note: the rest of the codebase consistently lets `Core.Process.Handle.ReadMemory<T>` swallow read failures internally; this file's defensive try/catch duplicates that logic.
- **Risk if left:** Silent failures in minimap icon detection. No diagnostic. Combined with F-117, the icon name "sticks" to whatever was first read.

### F-132 — Coroutine bodies in 5 InGameStateObjects + AreaLoadingState classes have no `try/catch` — extension of F-100 / F-113 across this batch

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit a2748a0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/AreaLoadingState.cs:82-92` (`OnPerFrame`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameState.cs:87-98` (`OnPerFrame`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:901-911` (`OnPerFrame`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/ImportantUiElements.cs:221-234` (`OnPerFrame`), `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Inventory.cs:200-210` (`OnTimeTick`)
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Same defect pattern as F-100 (coroutines in 5 RemoteObject classes lack try/catch) and F-113 (component UpdateData methods lack try/catch). Each `while (true) { yield return new Wait(...); if (Address != Zero) UpdateData(false); }` body has no try/catch around `UpdateData(false)`. `UpdateData` for these classes performs:
  - `AreaLoadingState`: reads `data.CurrentAreaDetailsPtr`, dereferences a string pointer, raises `RemoteEvents.AreaChanged`. A torn read of `CurrentAreaDetailsPtr` returning a bogus pointer causes `ReadUnicodeString` to silently return empty, but `lastCache = data` still updates — minor self-corruption.
  - `InGameState`: writes addresses on three child RemoteObjects (`CurrentAreaInstance`, `CurrentWorldInstance`, `GameUi`); each setter fires through `RemoteObjectBase.Address` which calls `UpdateData(hasAddressChanged)` recursively. A throw inside any child UpdateData (per F-113) propagates here.
  - `AreaInstance`: reads parallel-entity loops, terrain height computation, environment vector — large surface for throws. `GetTerrainHeight` (line 428-502) has explicit `throw new Exception` (line 536, F-138). `UpdateEntities` calls into `Entity.UpdateData` which can throw (per F-113 / F-133).
  - `ImportantUiElements`: reads `MapParentStruct`, `UiElementBaseOffset`, recursive `AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive` (F-152). Recursion stack-overflow is uncatchable.
  - `Inventory`: `Parallel.ForEach` with `throw new Exception` (F-130) propagates as AggregateException.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same root cause as F-100, but for the 5 coroutines in this batch. Any throw kills the per-class update coroutine for the rest of the session, plus cascades into `GameOverlay.Render` (F-058). The cascading impact is worse here because these are higher-frequency coroutines (`InGameState.OnPerFrame` runs at 60 Hz, `Inventory.OnTimeTick` runs at 50 Hz, `AreaInstance.OnPerFrame` at 60 Hz) and their failure produces immediate user-visible symptoms (entity tracking stops, area name freezes, inventory display freezes).
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap each `UpdateData(false)` call in try/catch; same standard pattern as F-100:
  ```csharp
  while (true) {
      yield return new Wait(EventName);
      try { if (this.Address != IntPtr.Zero) this.UpdateData(false); }
      catch (Exception ex) { Console.WriteLine($"[{className}.OnPerFrame] {ex}"); }
  }
  ```
  Apply uniformly across all 5 coroutines.
- **Risk if left:** Same family as F-100 — a single torn memory read or a child-class throw silently disables an entire subsystem until restart. Symptoms: "area name stuck", "entity list frozen", "inventory display empty after I picked up an item". With F-058 unfixed, also kills the entire overlay.

### F-133 — `Entity.TryCalculateEntitySubType` throws bare `new Exception` on `Unidentified` and default cases from a `Parallel.ForEach` entity-update worker

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:615-616, 697, 725-726`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Three throw sites in `TryCalculateEntitySubType`:
  - Line 616: `case EntityTypes.Unidentified: throw new Exception($"Entity with path ({this.Path}) and Id (${this.Id}) is unidentified.");`
  - Line 697: `_ => throw new Exception($"EntityFilterType {filtertype} added but not handled in Entity file.")`
  - Line 726: `default: throw new Exception($"Please update TryCalculateEntitySubType function to include {this.EntityType}.");`
  
  Two are developer-assertion guards (line 697 — switch-expression default; line 726 — switch default), one is a "should never happen" runtime check (line 616 — Unidentified is filtered out earlier in `Entity.UpdateData` line 424-432, but a torn read could leave `EntityType` as `Unidentified` past that filter). All three throw the bare `Exception` base type — Microsoft guidance says never throw the base type. All three propagate from `TryCalculateEntitySubType` → `Entity.UpdateData` → `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` `Parallel.ForEach` → `AggregateException` rethrow → `OnPerFrame` (no try/catch per F-132) → `Render` (no try/catch per F-058) → render thread death.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-130 (Parallel.ForEach + throw cascade) plus F-112 (bare base Exception). For line 697 and 726, the assertion is legitimate during *development* but should be a `Debug.Assert` not a runtime throw — production code shouldn't crash on enum extension; it should silently skip the unrecognized case. For line 616, the "Unidentified should never reach here" invariant is enforced by an earlier filter in `Entity.UpdateData` — but a torn read or a state transition between `TryCalculateEntityType` and `TryCalculateEntitySubType` can leave `this.EntityType == Unidentified` if `TryCalculateEntityType` returned false but `unresolvedRetryCount` had already incremented past `MaxUnresolvedRetries` and the early-return at line 426-432 was bypassed by a hasAddressChanged reset. Edge case, but real.
- **Suggested fix:** (a) Convert lines 697 and 726 to `Debug.Assert` + return false: `default: Debug.Fail($"Please update TryCalculateEntitySubType for {this.EntityType}"); return false;`. The caller already handles `false` as "skip this entity for this frame". (b) Convert line 616 to a return: `case EntityTypes.Unidentified: return false;` — same handling. (c) For all three, use a more specific exception type if the throw is truly desired (`InvalidOperationException`, `ArgumentOutOfRangeException`).
- **Risk if left:** Adding a new `EntityFilterType` or `EntityTypes` enum value crashes the overlay until the developer updates this switch. A torn read producing `Unidentified` past the guard kills the entity reader. Cascade with F-132 → F-058 means the entire overlay dies on the throw.

### F-138 — `AreaInstance.GetSubTerrainHeight` `throw new Exception` from inside a `Parallel.For` worker — propagates out of terrain-height build path

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:535-538`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Lines 535-538:
  ```csharp
  default:
      if (arrayLength > index) return subterrainheightarray[index];
      else throw new Exception($"SubterrainHeightArray Length {arrayLength} less-than index {index}");
  ```
  `GetSubTerrainHeight` is invoked from a `Parallel.For` body inside `GetTerrainHeight` (line 452-499). The throw propagates as `AggregateException` from `Parallel.For`, out of `GetTerrainHeight`, out of `AreaInstance.UpdateData` (line 231: `this.GridHeightData = this.GetTerrainHeight();` — only on `hasAddressChanged`, i.e., area transition). Same cascade as F-130 / F-132 / F-133 — kills the area-instance update coroutine on area transition.
- **Why it's a bug:** The `arrayLength > index` check on line 530 already returns the value when `index` is in range; the `else` branch fires only when `index >= arrayLength`. That happens when the SubTile's height array has fewer entries than the (gridY, gridX) position computed for it — which can happen when:
  1. Game patch reduces the grid resolution but the SubTile struct hasn't been re-read.
  2. Torn read of `subterrainheightarray.Length` returns a small value momentarily.
  3. The hardcoded special cases at lines 521-528 (`0x01, 0x45, 0x89, 0x119`) don't cover a new compressed-height format added in a future patch.
  
  In all three cases, the right behavior is "skip this tile, return 0" — not crash the entire area-loading. Same family as F-133 (developer-debug throw masquerading as runtime).
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the throw with `return 0;` and log once per area-load: `Console.WriteLine($"[GetSubTerrainHeight] OOR: len={arrayLength}, index={index} — returning 0");`. Terrain-height-of-zero is a graceful degradation (radar shows player at sea-level on the affected tiles).
- **Risk if left:** A single new compressed-height format on a game patch crashes area transitions. Cascade with F-132 → F-058 means the overlay dies on every area change after the patch.

### F-001 — `KrangledPassiveDetector` "Generate krangled data.json" handler dereferences nullable JTokens with `#pragma warning disable CS8602`; corrupt or unexpected JSON crashes the render coroutine

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:184-218`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** The button handler at line 184 wraps lines 191-217 in `#pragma warning disable CS8602 / restore CS8602` to silence "Dereference of a possibly null reference." The disabled block contains a deep `JObject` access chain that assumes the on-disk `data.json` (Path-of-Building tree data) has a specific shape: top-level `"nodes"` key, every per-skill object with `"skill"`, `"group"`, `"orbit"`, `"orbitIndex"`, `"out"`, `"in"` children. Each of `dataReader["nodes"]`, `dataWriter["nodes"][...]["skill"]`, `skillStruct.Value["skill"]`, `dataReader["nodes"][krangledSkillId.ToString()]`, etc. is annotated nullable by Newtonsoft.Json — the suppression hides the nullability rather than handling it. The call site has no `try/catch`; the method's parent `KrangledPassiveDetectorCoRoutine` (line 36) also has no top-level `try/catch` (extension of F-100 / F-058). A pragma-disabled CS8602 site that lacks a try/catch is a deferred-warning timebomb: any user-supplied data.json that does not conform to the assumed shape — missing `nodes` key, a node missing one of the expected children, an empty array where an object was expected — produces an `NullReferenceException` that propagates out of the button handler.
- **Why it's a bug:** Three concrete failure modes:
  1. **User points at the wrong JSON file** (e.g. a `tree.json` instead of `data.json`, an arbitrary JSON document, an empty array `[]`): the chain `dataReader["nodes"]` returns null; `foreach (JProperty skillStruct in dataReader["nodes"])` throws NRE. With no try/catch around the handler, the entire `KrangledPassiveDetectorCoRoutine` dies — the Krangled Passive Detector window vanishes silently and stays gone until process restart. Same family as F-176 (no try/catch on `File.ReadAllText`/`File.WriteAllText`).
  2. **Path of Building schema change** (a future POB version reshapes the tree-data file): one of the assumed children (`"orbit"`, `"orbitIndex"`, `"out"`, `"in"`) goes missing for some node, returning null on the indexer. `null.DeepClone()` NREs. The user has no diagnostic — same coroutine death.
  3. **Concurrent file mutation** (POB writes the file while GameHelper reads it): `JObject.Parse` may either throw `JsonReaderException` (caught by no one — kills coroutine) or succeed with a partial tree where some keys are missing (then NRE on indexer access). The pragma suppresses what would otherwise be a compile-time hint to add `?.` chaining, masking the runtime failure path.

  The pragma was introduced during the .NET 10 migration cleanup loop (Task 4) as a minimal disruption to ship the build; the proper fix was deferred to this audit pass. The disabled warning is at the only suppressed CS8602 site in the in-scope codebase.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the pragma-disabled block with explicit null-checked access using `?.` and `TryGetValue`. Wrap the entire handler body in `try/catch` and surface the failure to the user via `messageToDisplay`:
  ```csharp
  try {
      var dataReader = JObject.Parse(File.ReadAllText(dataJsonFilePath));
      var dataWriter = dataReader.DeepClone().ToObject<JObject>() ?? throw new InvalidDataException("Failed to clone JSON tree.");
      var sourceNodes = dataReader["nodes"] as JObject ?? throw new InvalidDataException("Missing 'nodes' object.");
      var targetNodes = dataWriter["nodes"] as JObject ?? throw new InvalidDataException("Missing 'nodes' object in clone.");
      foreach (var skillStruct in sourceNodes.Properties()) {
          if (skillStruct.Name == "root") continue;
          if (!int.TryParse(skillStruct.Name, out var skillId)) continue;
          if (!skillConvertor.TryGetValue(skillId, out var krangledSkillId)) continue;
          var krangledValue = sourceNodes[krangledSkillId.ToString()];
          if (krangledValue == null) continue;
          var clonedNode = (JObject)krangledValue.DeepClone();
          foreach (var key in new[] { "skill", "group", "orbit", "orbitIndex", "out", "in" }) {
              var src = skillStruct.Value[key];
              if (src != null) clonedNode[key] = src.DeepClone();
          }
          targetNodes[skillStruct.Name] = clonedNode;
      }
      var outPath = Path.Combine(Path.GetDirectoryName(dataJsonFilePath) ?? string.Empty,
                                 Path.GetFileNameWithoutExtension(dataJsonFilePath) + "_krangled.json");
      File.WriteAllText(outPath, dataWriter.ToString(Newtonsoft.Json.Formatting.Indented));
      messageToDisplay = $"{outPath} generated.";
  } catch (Exception ex) {
      messageToDisplay = $"ERROR: {ex.GetType().Name}: {ex.Message}";
  }
  ImGui.OpenPopup("KrangledPassiveDetectorPopUp");
  ```
  This also subsumes F-175 (substring-replace path corruption) and F-176 (no try/catch around the file IO). Once the explicit null-checks are in place, the `#pragma warning disable CS8602` and `restore CS8602` lines can be deleted along with the comment marker `// TODO: see audit F-001`.
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only feature (the whole class is `#if DEBUG`), so user impact is bounded to plugin/tool developers. Within that population, the failure mode is "Krangled Passive Detector window dies silently with no log on any non-conforming data.json", and the cause is genuinely opaque because the pragma hides what would otherwise be a useful nullability hint. Combined with F-058 (overlay no top-level try/catch), the NRE could escalate beyond just the one window dying.

### F-008 — `byte.Parse` with bad hex input throws uncaught at startup

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:44-64`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `ParseArrayOfHexBytes` calls `byte.Parse(hexByte, NumberStyles.HexNumber)` on every non-`?`/`^` token with no surrounding `try` and no validation. Both `Pattern` constructors call this from a field initializer path that runs at type init for `StaticOffsetsPatterns`.
- **Why it's a bug:** A typo in any pattern string (e.g. `"ZZ"`, `"123"` (more than 2 hex digits without `0x`), an empty token between commas) raises a `FormatException` or `OverflowException` during static constructor of `StaticOffsetsPatterns`, manifesting as a `TypeInitializationException` on first use. There is no log of which pattern is malformed.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap `byte.Parse` in a `try` and rethrow with the offending pattern name and token, or validate the token format up-front and produce a clearer error.
- **Risk if left:** Adding a new pattern with a typo produces an obscure type-init exception with no hint at which pattern failed.

### F-080 — `PManager.ReadPluginFiles` catches base `Exception`, swallowing OOM / `BadImageFormatException` distinction

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:125-148`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `ReadPluginFiles` wraps the entire DLL discovery + load in `try { ... } catch (Exception e) { Console.WriteLine($"Failed to load plugin {pluginDirectory.FullName} due to {e}"); return null; }`. The catch is unfiltered — `OutOfMemoryException`, `BadImageFormatException` (DLL is not a valid PE), `FileLoadException` (signature/strong-name issue), `TypeLoadException` are all flattened to the same log line.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same defect family as F-035 (`SafeMemoryHandle`). Standard guidance is to catch only the exceptions you can recover from. For `ReadPluginFiles`, the recoverable cases are `BadImageFormatException` (skip non-DLL), `FileLoadException` (corrupt or version-mismatched), and possibly `IOException`. OOM during plugin load is a critical condition that should propagate.
- **Suggested fix:** Catch specific types, log with category, and let `OutOfMemoryException` propagate:
  ```csharp
  catch (BadImageFormatException e) { Console.WriteLine($"Plugin {pluginDirectory.FullName} is not a valid .NET assembly: {e.Message}"); return null; }
  catch (FileLoadException e) { Console.WriteLine($"Failed to load plugin assembly {pluginDirectory.FullName}: {e}"); return null; }
  catch (IOException e) { Console.WriteLine($"IO error loading plugin {pluginDirectory.FullName}: {e}"); return null; }
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Diagnostic noise on plugin load failures — the user can't tell from the log whether the problem is "wrong .NET version" vs "corrupt DLL" vs "missing dependency". OOM masked.

### F-081 — `PManager.LoadPlugin(Assembly, ...)` catches base `Exception` around `assembly.GetTypes()` — `ReflectionTypeLoadException` lost

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:164-202`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** `assembly.GetTypes()` (line 168) throws `ReflectionTypeLoadException` when one or more types in the assembly fail to load (most commonly: missing dependency, version mismatch, type loader error). The exception's `LoaderExceptions` array contains the actual root causes. The catch block at line 197 swallows it as `Exception e` and logs only `assembly.FullName + e`. The per-type loader exceptions are lost.
- **Why it's a bug:** When a plugin fails to load due to a missing dependency, the user/developer needs to see *which* types failed and *why*. The current log gives only the outer message which typically reads "Unable to load one or more of the requested types." — useless for diagnosis. This is a well-known reflection footgun.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an explicit catch:
  ```csharp
  catch (ReflectionTypeLoadException e)
  {
      Console.WriteLine($"Plugin {assembly.FullName}: type load failed.");
      foreach (var le in e.LoaderExceptions ?? Array.Empty<Exception?>())
          if (le != null) Console.WriteLine($"  - {le.Message}");
      return null;
  }
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Plugin load failures with missing dependencies produce log lines that don't tell anyone what to fix. Same operational impact as F-080.

### F-143 — `AreaInstance.EntitiesWidget` Dump button uses `File.WriteAllText("entity_dumps/...")` with CWD-relative path and no try/catch

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:868-872`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Line 868-869: `Directory.CreateDirectory("entity_dumps"); var outPath = Path.Join("entity_dumps", safeName + ".json");` — relative path, depends on CWD (same defect family as F-068). Line 870: `File.WriteAllText(outPath, json);` — no try/catch, no atomicity (same defect family as F-039 / F-102). Same line also calls `ImGui.SetClipboardText(json)` (line 871) which has its own failure modes (clipboard locked by another process).
- **Why it's a bug:** This is a debug button (Dump) inside the AreaInstance debug widget, which only renders when the user expands the entity tree. Three concrete failure modes:
  1. CWD-relative path lands in different folders for different launchers (F-068).
  2. `File.WriteAllText` to a read-only or full disk throws `IOException` / `UnauthorizedAccessException`. The throw propagates from the Dump button click handler, up through `EntitiesWidget` → `AreaInstance.ToImGui` → `Core.RemoteObjectsToImGuiCollapsingHeader` → `Render` (F-058 cascade).
  3. The `safeName = path.Replace("/", "_")` (line 646) doesn't strip backslashes, colons, or other Windows-illegal chars (`<>:"/\|?*`). A path containing `\` or `:` (legal in PoE Metadata paths? unlikely, but defensively) crashes `File.WriteAllText` with `ArgumentException`.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap in try/catch and log; resolve path against `AppContext.BaseDirectory`:
  ```csharp
  try {
      var dumpDir = Path.Combine(AppContext.BaseDirectory, "entity_dumps");
      Directory.CreateDirectory(dumpDir);
      var sanitized = string.Join("_", safeName.Split(Path.GetInvalidFileNameChars()));
      var outPath = Path.Combine(dumpDir, sanitized + ".json");
      File.WriteAllText(outPath, json);
  } catch (Exception ex) { Console.WriteLine($"[EntityDump] {ex.Message}"); }
  ImGui.SetClipboardText(json);
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Click on Dump for an entity with an unusual path crashes the render loop. Cascade with F-058. Even without crash, dump files land in unpredictable folders.

### F-161 — `SettingsWindow.ChangeFontWidget` "Apply Changes" calls `Core.Overlay.ReplaceFont(...)` with no try/catch

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/SettingsWindow.cs:208-224`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Lines 208-224 in `ChangeFontWidget` (called from `DrawCoreSettings` line 160). When the user clicks "Apply Changes", the code branches on `MiscHelper.TryConvertStringToImGuiGlyphRanges`:
  - Custom-glyph path: `Core.Overlay.ReplaceFont(FontPathName, FontSize, glyphranges)`
  - Language path: `Core.Overlay.ReplaceFont(FontPathName, FontSize, FontLanguage)`
  
  `ReplaceFont` is a `ClickableTransparentOverlay` API that opens the font file. If `FontPathName` is invalid (e.g., default `C:\Windows\Fonts\msyh.ttc` missing on a clean Windows install — see F-163), or the file is locked, ReplaceFont throws (typically `FileNotFoundException` or `IOException`). There is no try/catch around either call.
- **Why it's a bug:** The settings render coroutine (`SettingsWindow.RenderCoroutine` line 677) has no top-level try/catch (extension of F-058 / F-100). An exception in `ReplaceFont` propagates up to the coroutine handler and silently kills the entire settings UI. From the user's perspective, the settings window vanishes mid-edit and never returns until process restart. The user's invalid `FontPathName` is still saved in JSON (per F-039 / F-159), so the next launch repeats the failure on first font-load attempt elsewhere in startup.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap both `ReplaceFont` calls in try/catch, surface the error in the UI (`messageToDisplay = ex.Message; ImGui.OpenPopup(...)`), and revert `FontPathName` to last-known-good or the default.
- **Risk if left:** A single typo in the font path field deletes the entire settings window for the rest of the session. Recoverable only by editing JSON manually.

### F-171 — `GameUiExplorer.CreateUiElement` calls `element[i]!` on an indexer that can return null on torn read

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/GameUiExplorer.cs:46-62`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Line 58: `eleStruct.Children.Add(element[i]!);`. The `UiElementBase` indexer (`UiElementBase.this[int i]`) can return `null` when a child pointer is zero or torn-read returns an invalid address (the indexer is documented as nullable per F-136's discussion of `UiElementBase` allocations). The null-forgiving `!` operator silently asserts non-null and adds `null` to `Children` if the indexer does return null. Subsequent iteration over `Children` (line 197-247 the dropdown render) accesses `child.Address` and `child.IsVisible` on a possibly-null `UiElementBase`.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-066 / F-092 — null-forgiving operator masks a contract violation. If a torn read returns a null child mid-frame, the next render pass hits `child.Address` (line 201, 208, 211) and NPEs out of the GameUiExplorer render coroutine. Per F-058 / F-100, the coroutine has no try/catch. The Game UiExplorer window silently vanishes and cannot be reopened without restart.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `element[i]!` with explicit null-check: `var child = element[i]; if (child == null) continue; eleStruct.Children.Add(child);`. Same pattern in line 154's `current.Children[current.CurrentChildIndex]` and line 200's `current.Children[j]` should also be defensive against null entries.
- **Risk if left:** During heavy UI-tree mutation in-game (e.g., chat opening, panel transitions), the GameUiExplorer window can vanish silently from a single null child read.

### F-176 — `KrangledPassiveDetector` uses `File.ReadAllText` / `File.WriteAllText` with no try/catch and no atomicity

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:191, 217`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Line 191: `var dataReader = JObject.Parse(File.ReadAllText(dataJsonFilePath));` — bad path or insufficient permissions throws `FileNotFoundException`/`UnauthorizedAccessException`/`IOException`. Line 217: `File.WriteAllText(dataJsonFilePath.Replace(".json", "_krangled.json"), ...)` — non-atomic write (extension of F-039). The "Generate krangled data.json" coroutine has no try/catch (extension of F-100); the parent `KrangledPassiveDetectorCoRoutine` (line 36) also has no top-level try/catch (extension of F-058).
- **Why it's a bug:** A user typing a wrong path (or pasting a path with quotes, or pointing at a directory) crashes the entire Krangled Passive Detector coroutine. Same pattern as F-176's sibling F-130 / F-143. Compounded by F-175 — even on a *correct* path, the output filename derivation can corrupt paths containing ".json" elsewhere.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the entire button-handler body in try/catch, log to `messageToDisplay`, and reopen the popup so the user sees the error. For atomicity, write to `tmp` then `File.Move(tmp, target, overwrite: true)` (extension of F-039 fix).
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only feature (the whole class is `#if DEBUG`), so user-impact is bounded to developers using the Krangled tool, but in that population the failure mode is "tool dies silently with no log".

### F-178 — `NearbyVisualization.DrawNearbyRange` empty `try { ... } catch { }` swallows `IndexOutOfRangeException` from `GridHeightData[Y][X]`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/NearbyVisualization.cs:66-70`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Exception handling
- **Description:** Lines 66-70:
  ```csharp
  try {
      height = Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.GridHeightData[(int)points[i].Y][(int)points[i].X];
  } catch { }
  ```
  Empty catch block — same pattern as F-114 (`MinimapIcon.UpdateData`). Catches `IndexOutOfRangeException` (when the projected circle point falls outside the area's grid), `NullReferenceException` (when `GridHeightData` is being rebuilt mid-area-change), `OverflowException` (when `(int)points[i].Y` overflows from a NaN), and `Exception` (anything else).
- **Why it's a bug:** Two concerns:
  1. **Hides legitimate bugs**: a `NullReferenceException` on the chain to `GridHeightData` indicates a torn area-change read (F-179) — the empty catch swallows it instead of surfacing.
  2. **Falls back to stale `height`**: the catch block does not reset `height`, so the previous loop iteration's `height` (or the function's parameter `height` from the player's terrain at i=0) leaks into all subsequent points. The drawn circle bobs along the terrain at the player's height instead of the actual terrain at each point.
- **Suggested fix:** Bounds-check explicitly: `var gx = (int)points[i].X; var gy = (int)points[i].Y; var gh = Core.States.InGameStateObject.CurrentAreaInstance.GridHeightData; if (gh != null && gy >= 0 && gy < gh.Length && gx >= 0 && gx < gh[gy].Length) height = gh[gy][gx];`. Drop the empty catch.
- **Risk if left:** Inner/outer circles draw at wrong terrain heights when the player is near the edge of the area; cosmetic.


### Resource lifecycle / Dispose

### F-074 — `PluginAssemblyLoadContext` is not collectible — plugin DLLs cannot be unloaded for the process lifetime

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PluginAssemblyLoadContext.cs:6-25`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Resource lifecycle / Dispose
- **Description:** The class derives from `AssemblyLoadContext` but its constructor `public PluginAssemblyLoadContext(string assemblyLocation)` calls the base `AssemblyLoadContext()` parameterless ctor, which defaults `isCollectible: false`. There is no override of `Unload()` and no field that retains the ALC instance — `PManager.ReadPluginFiles` instantiates it inline (`new PluginAssemblyLoadContext(dllFile.FullName).LoadFromAssemblyPath(...)`). Once the assembly is loaded, the ALC instance is reachable via the loaded `Assembly`'s context but cannot be unloaded.
- **Why it's a bug:** A non-collectible ALC anchors the assembly, all its types, all JIT-compiled code, and all static fields for the lifetime of the host process. The DEBUG-only `PManager.UnloadPlugin` (line 75) cannot in practice unload anything — it only removes the plugin from the manager's list (see F-075). For developer iteration, this means rebuilding a plugin requires restarting GameHelper. For end users, every plugin that's been loaded — even after the user disables it — keeps consuming memory and pinning native resources (file handles to the DLL on disk on Windows, until process exit).
- **Suggested fix:** Pass `isCollectible: true` to the base ctor: `public PluginAssemblyLoadContext(string assemblyLocation) : base(isCollectible: true) { ... }`. Have `PManager` retain the ALC reference (e.g., add it to `PluginContainer`) and call `alc.Unload()` from `UnloadPlugin`. Note: collectible ALCs have constraints — no static reflection caches that pin types, no NGen — but for a plugin scenario this is the standard pattern. Document the constraint in `IPCore` so plugin authors don't accidentally pin the ALC via static `Type` references.
- **Risk if left:** Plugin development workflow requires full process restart for any plugin change. Users with many disabled plugins still pay full memory/handle cost. DLL replacement on disk is blocked while GameHelper is running (Windows holds an exclusive lock on the loaded DLL).

### F-061 — `Program.Main` UnhandledException handler calls `Environment.Exit(1)` — skips `using` Dispose, leaks process handle

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 44c314d
- **File:** `GameHelper/Program.cs:22-32`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Resource lifecycle / Dispose
- **Description:** The `AppDomain.CurrentDomain.UnhandledException` handler logs to `Error.log` then calls `Environment.Exit(1)`. `Environment.Exit` does **not** unwind the stack — the `using (Core.Overlay = new GameOverlay(...))` block on line 29 never executes its `Dispose()`, which means `Core.Dispose()` (line 151-154 of `Core.cs`) never runs, which means `Process.Close(false)` never runs, which means the SafeMemoryHandle wrapping `OpenProcess` never disposes, the `Information.Close()` never disposes the Process object, and `OnClose` event is never raised so coroutines that depend on it never tear down state.
- **Why it's a bug:** Compounds with F-057 and F-074 — an unhandled exception is exactly the case where teardown matters most (the last chance to flush logs, release handles, save settings). `Environment.Exit(1)` calls only finalizers (best-effort), not `Dispose`. On Windows, OS reclaims the handles eventually, but:
  - The settings file (if a save was in flight) is left half-written (see F-039).
  - Any plugin's `Dispose` that flushes its own data is skipped.
  - The game process retains the foreign `OpenProcess` handle until process teardown's handle-table sweep — racy with whatever holds onto the same target.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) drop `Environment.Exit(1)` and let the runtime terminate normally (which still skips `using`-Dispose because the stack is already unwound past `Main`), but at least lets finalizers/AppDomain.ProcessExit fire; or (b) before `Environment.Exit`, explicitly call `Core.Dispose()` and any plugin-manager teardown. Option (b) is the robust fix.
- **Risk if left:** Resource and settings hygiene gaps on every crash; not visible to the user except as "settings reset" or "stuck game handle" symptoms after crashes.

### F-075 — `PManager.UnloadPlugin` (DEBUG) does not unload the assembly; method name is misleading

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:75-89`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Resource lifecycle / Dispose
- **Description:** `UnloadPlugin(string name)` does the following: `plugin.Plugin.SaveSettings(); plugin.Plugin.OnDisable(); Plugins.Remove(plugin); return true;`. There is no call to unload the assembly's `AssemblyLoadContext`. The plugin's types, code, and static state remain in memory; only the manager's reference is removed.
- **Why it's a bug:** The name promises a tear-down semantics that the method doesn't deliver. A subsequent `LoadPlugin(name)` (DEBUG, line 91) will call `Activator.CreateInstance` on the **same Type instance** still cached in the original `AssemblyLoadContext` — i.e., the "reload" actually reuses the old code. Edits to the plugin DLL on disk are not picked up unless the host process restarts. Compounded with F-074 (ALC not collectible), genuine unload is not even possible.
- **Suggested fix:** Rename to `RemovePlugin` to reflect the true semantics. To enable real unload, combine with F-074's collectible ALC change, store `WeakReference<PluginAssemblyLoadContext>` in `PluginContainer`, call `alc.Unload()` here, and follow up with `GC.Collect()`/`GC.WaitForPendingFinalizers()` until the weak reference drops. This is the documented .NET pattern for plugin hot-reload.
- **Risk if left:** Developers iterating on plugins (the only consumers of this DEBUG path) believe their changes were reloaded when they were not — silent stale code execution, hard-to-debug behavior. Combined with F-074, hot-reload simply doesn't work despite the API claiming it does.

### F-053 — `MiscHelper.KillTCPConnectionForProcess` does not free CoTaskMem on `SetTcpEntry` exception

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:177-182`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Resource lifecycle / Dispose
- **Description:** `Marshal.AllocCoTaskMem` (line 178) → `Marshal.StructureToPtr` → `SetTcpEntry(ptr)` → `Marshal.FreeCoTaskMem(ptr)`. There is no `try/finally` around the unmanaged-memory lifetime. If `Marshal.StructureToPtr` or the P/Invoke throws (rare but possible — e.g., access denied surfaces as `Marshal.GetExceptionForHR`), the unmanaged memory leaks for the process lifetime.
- **Why it's a bug:** Standard CoTaskMem hygiene requires `try/finally`. The same function correctly does this for `buffTable` (`Marshal.AllocHGlobal` at line 149-171) but forgets it here.
- **Suggested fix:** `var ptr = Marshal.AllocCoTaskMem(...); try { Marshal.StructureToPtr(...); _ = SetTcpEntry(ptr); } finally { Marshal.FreeCoTaskMem(ptr); }`.
- **Risk if left:** Tiny per-call leak (sizeof(MibTcprowOwnerPid) ≈ 24 bytes) only on exception path. Cumulative impact essentially zero.

### F-041 — `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` typo — should be `SaveToFile`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/JsonHelper.cs:42`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Resource lifecycle / Dispose (cosmetic)
- **Description:** Method name is `SafeToFile` (a typo of `SaveToFile`). It does not provide any "safety" guarantee — it's a plain `File.WriteAllText` with no atomicity. The misnamed method has spread to two consumers.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not, but the name actively misrepresents the function. A future reader looking for "safe" file IO will be misled.
- **Suggested fix:** Rename to `SaveToFile` and update both call sites (`Core.cs`, `PManager.cs`, `SettingsWindow.cs`).
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic.


### P/Invoke correctness

### F-031 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadMemoryArray` compares bytes-read to element count, missing partial reads

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 9744426
- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:120-153`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** P/Invoke correctness
- **Description:** `NativeWrapper.ReadProcessMemoryArray` wraps Win32 `ReadProcessMemory`. The `numBytesRead` out parameter (typed `IntPtr`) carries **bytes read**, not elements read. Code at line 140 compares it to `nsize`, which is the requested element count: `if (numBytesRead.ToInt32() < nsize) throw ...`.
- **Why it's a bug:** For any `T` larger than 1 byte (essentially every read in this codebase — `IntPtr`, `int`, `StdMapNode<,>`, `EntityNodeKey`, all the offset structs), `numBytesRead == nsize * sizeof(T)`. The comparison is therefore `(elements * sizeof(T)) < elements` which is false except for T-size 0. A partial read returning, say, 9 of 10 `int`s (36 bytes vs requested 40 bytes) compares 36 < 10, which is `false`, so the partial read is silently accepted and the caller sees stale `default(T)` data in the trailing slots of the buffer. The check only correctly fires when `T = byte`, where bytes-read == elements.
- **Suggested fix:** `if (numBytesRead.ToInt64() < (long)nsize * Marshal.SizeOf<T>()) throw ...`. (`ToInt64` is needed because for very large arrays the size could exceed `int.MaxValue`.) Bonus: hoist `Marshal.SizeOf<T>()` to the top of the method since it's already needed for the size calculation.
- **Risk if left:** Silent data corruption on every short read — the unread tail of the buffer remains zero-initialised (`new T[nsize]` is zero-init in C#), which manifests as null pointers / zero IDs / empty strings in any data structure that uses `ReadMemoryArray`. Most reads happen to succeed in full; this fires when the game has paged memory out, when the target address straddles an unreadable page, or during process teardown — exactly the scenarios where a robust check is most needed.

### F-039 — `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` non-atomic write — crash mid-write corrupts user settings

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit e2a91a3
- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/JsonHelper.cs:42-46`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** P/Invoke correctness (file IO atomicity)
- **Description:** `SafeToFile` calls `File.WriteAllText(file.FullName, content)` — a one-shot write that opens the file `Truncate|Write` and writes the JSON. If the process is killed (taskkill, OS shutdown, Battery loss, crash in `JsonConvert.SerializeObject` mid-stream) between `Truncate` and the final flush, the on-disk file is left zero-byte or partially-written. The next startup attempts to deserialize the corrupt content (see F-040) and crashes.
- **Why it's a bug:** Standard idiom for atomic settings save:
  1. Serialize to `<file>.tmp`.
  2. `File.Replace(<file>.tmp, <file>, <file>.bak)` (atomic on NTFS).
  3. Optionally delete `.bak` after success.
  This codebase saves settings on every overlay close, on `TimeToSaveAllSettings` events, and on user UI interactions — so the window is wide enough that a real-world crash will hit it.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `File.WriteAllText` with the temp-file-then-rename idiom. Use `File.Replace(tempPath, finalPath, backupPath)` or write to temp + `File.Move(temp, final, overwrite: true)`. Combine with F-040's exception handling for full robustness.
- **Risk if left:** Power loss / app crash during save causes user to lose all settings on next launch. Combined with F-040, the application also fails to start. Combined cost is high to a user.

### F-052 — `MiscHelper.KillTCPConnectionForProcess` ignores first `GetExtendedTcpTable` error code, allocates with potentially-zero buffer

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:148-156`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** P/Invoke correctness
- **Description:** First call: `var ret = GetExtendedTcpTable(IntPtr.Zero, ref buffSize, true, afInet, ...)`. The expected return is `ERROR_INSUFFICIENT_BUFFER (122)` so the OS fills `buffSize`. The code never checks `ret`. If the call fails for any other reason (e.g., `ERROR_INVALID_PARAMETER` — driver state issue), `buffSize` is left at zero, then `Marshal.AllocHGlobal(0)` is called (returns a small allocation), then `GetExtendedTcpTable` is called again with the same bad params, returns non-zero, the early-return fires — but the heap allocation and table walk above were wasted, and a buffer of unknown size is allocated.
- **Why it's a bug:** A correct caller checks both that `ret == ERROR_INSUFFICIENT_BUFFER` and that `buffSize > 0` before allocating. The current pattern leaks a tiny buffer in the success-on-second-try case (small) and silently swallows a real error in the bad-driver case.
- **Suggested fix:**
  ```csharp
  var ret = GetExtendedTcpTable(IntPtr.Zero, ref buffSize, true, afInet, ...);
  if (ret != 0 /* ERROR_SUCCESS */ && ret != 122 /* ERROR_INSUFFICIENT_BUFFER */) return;
  if (buffSize <= 0) return;
  var buffTable = Marshal.AllocHGlobal(buffSize);
  ```
- **Risk if left:** No live impact today; defensive hygiene only.

### F-067 — Win32 P/Invokes (`GetForegroundWindow`, `GetClientRect`, `ClientToScreen`) declared without `SetLastError = true`

- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:347-351`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** P/Invoke correctness
- **Description:** All three Win32 imports are declared with bare `[DllImport("user32.dll")]`. `GetClientRect` and `ClientToScreen` return `bool` — they fail (return `false`) when the target HWND is invalid (e.g. game process exited mid-call, racing `Monitor`'s checks). The error code is recoverable via `Marshal.GetLastWin32Error()`, but only if the import is annotated with `SetLastError = true`. Without that, `GetLastWin32Error()` returns whatever was on the thread before the P/Invoke, completely unrelated.
- **Why it's a bug:** `UpdateWindowRectangle` (line 335-345) ignores the return values and uses `out RECT size` and `out Point pos` regardless. If the call fails, `size` and `pos` contain zero/uninitialised data; `WindowArea` is then set to `Rectangle(0,0,0,0)` which the size-empty guard at line 340 skips — so live impact is benign by accident. But there's no diagnostic if the calls start failing systematically (hooked DLL, denial of access, target HWND closed).
- **Suggested fix:**
  ```csharp
  [DllImport("user32.dll", SetLastError = true)] private static extern IntPtr GetForegroundWindow();
  [DllImport("user32.dll", SetLastError = true)] [return: MarshalAs(UnmanagedType.Bool)] private static extern bool GetClientRect(IntPtr hWnd, out RECT lpRect);
  [DllImport("user32.dll", SetLastError = true)] [return: MarshalAs(UnmanagedType.Bool)] private static extern bool ClientToScreen(IntPtr hWnd, out Point lpPoint);
  ```
  Then check return values in `UpdateWindowRectangle` and log `Marshal.GetLastWin32Error()` on failure.
