The `[return: MarshalAs(UnmanagedType.Bool)]` is also recommended best practice — without it, .NET marshals `BOOL` (4-byte int) → `bool` (1 byte) using a default that, while it works, isn't explicit.
- **Risk if left:** No diagnostic for systematic Win32 failures; benign data corruption (zero rect) is silently accepted.

### F-102 — `LoadedFiles.ToImGui` Save button uses `File.WriteAllText` with no atomicity / try-catch — extension of F-039

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:74-76`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** P/Invoke correctness (file IO atomicity)
- **Description:** `File.WriteAllText(Path.Join(dir_name, this.filename), string.Join("\n", dataToWrite));` — same non-atomic write pattern as F-039 (`JsonHelper.SafeToFile`), and same lack of `try/catch` (an `IOException` from disk-full or `UnauthorizedAccessException` from a read-only dir crashes the render coroutine, see F-100).
- **Why it's a bug:** Less critical than F-039 because preload dumps are user-debug data (not application settings) — losing one is a minor inconvenience. But the pattern is identical, the consequence on exception is worse (kills the render coroutine via F-100), and the fix is one line.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap in try/catch and log the failure: `try { File.WriteAllText(...); this.areaAlreadyDone = true; } catch (Exception ex) { Console.WriteLine($"[LoadedFiles] Save failed: {ex.Message}"); }`. Atomicity is not required for debug dumps.
- **Risk if left:** A failed Save (read-only dir, disk full) crashes the render coroutine, cascading to F-100's "preload tracking permanently disabled" outcome.


### Logic bugs

### F-056 — `GameProcess.AskUserToSelectClient` Done button clears `clientSelected` before `FindAndOpen` consumes it — multi-instance selection is broken on the typical user timing

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 44c314d
- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:146-227`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** When more than one PoE process is running, `FindAndOpen` (line 148-184) is the consumer of the user's pick. Each iteration: `processesInfo.Clear()` → re-enumerate → if `count > 1` → `ShowSelectGameMenu()` → check `clientSelected > -1` → if so, `Open()` and `break`. `AskUserToSelectClient` (line 187-227) draws the popup. The user clicks a radio button (`clientSelected = i` line 204) and then clicks "Done" (line 209). The Done branch calls `HideSelectGameMenu()` (line 211) which **resets `clientSelected = -1`** (line 231) and clears `processesInfo` (line 232). The popup closes.
- **Why it's a bug:** The Coroutine library schedules cooperatively, single-threaded. Sequence:
  1. `FindAndOpen` body runs: count > 1 → ShowSelectGameMenu → check `clientSelected` (-1) → loop ends → `yield Wait(2d)`.
  2. Render frames fire every ~16 ms over the next ~2 s. `AskUserToSelectClient` draws the popup. User picks a radio (`clientSelected = 0`).
  3. User clicks **Done**. `HideSelectGameMenu()` runs: `clientSelected = -1`, `processesInfo.Clear()`, popup closes.
  4. `FindAndOpen` wakes after the 2 s wait. `clientSelected` is now `-1` — the user's selection was wiped by Done **before** `FindAndOpen` ever read it. `processesInfo.Clear()` → re-enumerate → count > 1 again → `ShowSelectGameMenu()` re-shows the popup → `clientSelected > -1` check fails → loop continues.
  
  The only timing under which Done "works" is if the 2 s tick happens to fire **between** the user clicking the radio and clicking Done — a sub-second window inside a multi-second user reaction time. Otherwise the user is stuck in an infinite popup-redisplay loop. The code does not even read `Information` directly from the popup callback — it relies on `FindAndOpen` to copy `processesInfo[clientSelected]` into `Information` (line 176), and that copy can never happen on the standard user flow.
  
  Additionally, the only flow that **does** work is "select radio → wait 2 s without clicking Done": `FindAndOpen` polls `clientSelected = 0`, copies `Information`, calls `Open()`, breaks. The popup is still on screen — and clicking Done at this point clears already-mooted state. So Done is functionally useless.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the consumption of the user's selection into the Done branch, not into `FindAndOpen`. For example: when Done is clicked, capture `Information = processesInfo[clientSelected]` *before* `HideSelectGameMenu`, set a `userPickedProcess` flag, and have `FindAndOpen` watch for that flag instead of `clientSelected`. Alternatively, `FindAndOpen` should read `clientSelected` immediately after `ShowSelectGameMenu()` *inside* a tighter wait loop (e.g., yield `OnRender` until `clientSelected > -1`, then proceed) rather than the 2 s tick. Either way, the order "user selects → Done captures → loop processes" must replace the current "user selects → Done discards → loop polls".
- **Risk if left:** Multi-instance PoE users (Hideout-warrior + main account, or test installations) cannot select which instance the overlay attaches to — they get caught in a popup that re-appears every 2 s, and their selection only takes effect by accident if they don't click Done.

### F-006 — Pattern without `^` marker silently sets `BytesToSkip = -1`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:73-82`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** The single-string `Pattern(string name, string arrayOfHexBytes)` constructor computes `BytesToSkip = arrayOfHexBytesList.FindIndex("^".Equals)`. `List<T>.FindIndex` returns `-1` when no element matches.
- **Why it's a bug:** If a future caller writes a pattern without a `^` marker, `BytesToSkip` becomes `-1`. `PatternFinder.cs:172` then computes `patternOffsets[i] + Patterns[i].BytesToSkip`, producing an address one byte before the actual match. The offset error is silent — no exception, no log — and shows up later as "wrong static address" with no obvious cause.
- **Suggested fix:** If `FindIndex` returns `-1`, either throw `ArgumentException("pattern must contain '^' marker")`, or fall back to `BytesToSkip = 0` and document the behavior. Today's all-six callers in `StaticOffsetsPatterns.cs` happen to include `^`, so no live bug, but the trap is loaded for the next pattern added.
- **Risk if left:** A pattern added without `^` resolves to a bad static-address offset that crashes downstream pattern-resolved reads, with no diagnostic pointing at the cause.

### F-023 — `VitalStruct.CurrentInPercent()` divides by `Unreserved` which can be 0 or negative

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Life.cs:56-64`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `CurrentInPercent()` guards `if (this.Total == 0) return 0;` then computes `(int)Math.Round(100d * this.Current / this.Unreserved)`. `Unreserved` is `this.Total - this.ReservedTotal` and `ReservedTotal = ceil(ReservedPercent/10000f * Total) + ReservedFlat`.
- **Why it's a bug:** The guard only handles `Total == 0`. When `ReservedTotal >= Total` (e.g. character reserves 100% via auras + a flat reservation, or `ReservedFlat >= Total`), `Unreserved` is `0` (DivideByZeroException) or negative (returns nonsensical negative percent that callers may render as a health bar). Real POE characters routinely reserve >90% of mana via auras, so `Unreserved == 0` for the Mana vital is not exotic. Same risk applies to `ReservedInPercent()` which divides by `Total` and is correctly guarded — but `CurrentInPercent` divides by `Unreserved` and is not. Consumers of this API in the host (`HealthBars`, vitals overlays) read this percent for every entity every frame.
- **Suggested fix:** `var unreserved = this.Unreserved; if (unreserved <= 0) return 0; return (int)Math.Round(100d * this.Current / unreserved);` Also clamp negative `Unreserved` to 0 in the property itself, since negative reservation is not physically meaningful.
- **Risk if left:** Live `DivideByZeroException` on any character whose ReservedFlat reaches Total (uncommon but possible mid-game) or on torn memory reads where `Total = 0` was the only guard.

### F-032 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdList` has no upper bound, will infinite-loop on cycle / torn read

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit 9744426
- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:366-387`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `ReadStdList<TValue>` walks the linked list by reading `currNode.Next` and stopping only when `currNodeAddress == nativeContainer.Head`. There is no max-iteration counter. If the in-game list contains a Next-pointer cycle that doesn't pass through Head (because of a torn read where Head's address shifted, or because the game patched the list during reading), the loop runs forever, blocking whatever coroutine called it.
- **Why it's a bug:** Memory reads against a moving target *will* tear occasionally. Every other read primitive in this file has a sanity bound (`StdVector` caps `length > 16_000_000`; `StdString` caps at 1000; `StdMap` caps via `maxSizeAllowed`). `ReadStdList` doesn't. The only safety net is the inline check `if (currNodeAddress == IntPtr.Zero) break` (line 374), which catches Next == null but not Next == garbage non-null pointer cycles.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a bound: `var maxIter = 100_000; var iter = 0; while (currNodeAddress != nativeContainer.Head && ++iter < maxIter) { ... }` and log/throw if maxIter reached.
- **Risk if left:** A single torn read on a game-list update could hang the entity-reader thread. POE's lists are small in practice (< 1000 elements), so a 100k cap is fine.

### F-037 — `PatternFinder.Find` computes `patternMaxLength` but never uses it; chunks have no overlap

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/PatternFinder.cs:63, 78-92`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 63 computes `var patternMaxLength = BiggestPatternLength();` with a comment block (lines 56-62) explaining the purpose: chunks should overlap by `patternMaxLength` bytes so a pattern that straddles a chunk boundary is still detected. But `patternMaxLength` is never read after assignment. The actual chunk read at line 80-82 is exactly `MaxBytesObject` bytes at offset `i * MaxBytesObject` — chunks are abutting, not overlapping. The inner loop at line 117 (`if (processDataLength - j < patternLength) continue;`) prevents reading past the end of a chunk, which means any pattern starting near the end of one chunk is skipped, not continued into the next.
- **Why it's a bug:** A pattern split across the boundary between chunk N and chunk N+1 will never match. With ~80 KB chunks and a typical pattern length of ~25 bytes, the boundary-loss probability per pattern per scan run is roughly `25 / 84_000 ≈ 0.03%`, multiplied by 6 patterns × ~50 chunks (for a ~4 MB module) = ~9% chance per run that *some* pattern lives in the dead zone. Failure surfaces as `throw new Exception("Couldn't find some patterns. kindly fix the patterns.")` at line 167 — flaky startup, not silent corruption. But the user sees no clue that retrying might work.
- **Suggested fix:** Make chunks overlap by `patternMaxLength`:
  ```csharp
  var actualReadSize = isLastIteration ? processSize - currentOffset
                       : Math.Min(MaxBytesObject + patternMaxLength, processSize - currentOffset);
  ```
  Then make the inner loop read up to `processDataLength - patternLength` (current behaviour) — patterns that straddle the boundary are now found in the chunk that starts before them, by virtue of the overlap.
- **Risk if left:** Flaky startup — `Couldn't find some patterns` thrown intermittently. User retries and it usually works the second time because the OS-paging happens to land patterns mid-chunk.

### F-115 — `Mods` and `ObjectMagicProperties` `UpdateData` append to mod lists without clearing — list grows forever on re-update

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit c76ccc0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Mods.cs:62-69`, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ObjectMagicProperties.cs:79-87`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Both components gate the mod-list refresh on `if (hasAddressChanged)` (Mods.cs:62, ObjectMagicProperties.cs:79). Inside that block they call `ObjectMagicProperties.AddToMods(this.<list>, reader.ReadStdVector<ModArrayStruct>(...))` for each mod source (Implicit, Explicit, Enchant, Hellscape, Crucible). `AddToMods` does `for (var i = 0; i < mods.Length; i++) collection.Add(...)` — a pure append. The lists are never cleared first.
- **Why it's a bug:** `hasAddressChanged` is `true` whenever the component's `Address` field changes value. That happens when:
  1. The component pointer is reassigned (item moved to a different inventory slot, item rerolled, item identified, vendor recycled).
  2. The entity is re-cached after a force-refresh (`Entity.UpdateData` rebuilds `componentAddresses` per F-100 in `UpdateComponentData(refreshComponentMap=true)`).
  In all those cases, the *old* mod list is still in the `Mods.ImplicitMods` (etc.) lists, and the *new* mods get appended. After N rerolls of the same item, the list contains all N versions concatenated. `ObjectMagicProperties.ModNames` HashSet is also never cleared — so it grows with every reroll, never shrinks. `ObjectMagicProperties.ModStats` Dictionary uses `StatUpdator` which does call `stats.Clear()` (line 70 of ComponentBase.cs) — so ModStats is consistent, but Mods/ModNames are not.
  Visible impact: in the debug widget, "ImplicitMods" tab shows duplicate mods. In any plugin that uses `ObjectMagicProperties.Mods` to display item state (NinjaPricer, item filters), the displayed mods accumulate over time. For long sessions, the lists could grow into thousands of entries per item.
- **Suggested fix:** Clear the lists at the top of the `if (hasAddressChanged)` block:
  ```csharp
  if (hasAddressChanged) {
      this.ImplicitMods.Clear(); this.ExplicitMods.Clear();
      this.EnchantMods.Clear(); this.HellscapeMods.Clear();
      ObjectMagicProperties.AddToMods(this.ImplicitMods, ...);
      // ... (same for others)
  }
  ```
  Same for `ObjectMagicProperties.UpdateData`: `this.Mods.Clear(); this.ModNames.Clear();` before the AddToMods calls. The current `_ = this.Mods.All(k => this.ModNames.Add(k.name));` line is also a candidate for replacement with a clean `foreach` (see F-128).
- **Risk if left:** Mod-list inflation across reroll events. Visible in debug UI; can corrupt plugin state that uses these lists for matching. Memory grows unbounded across long sessions.

### F-116 — `Actor.UpdateData` never clears `ActiveSkills` / `ActiveSkillCooldowns` dictionaries — stale entries persist across skill swaps

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit c76ccc0
- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Actor.cs:166, 173-221`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 166 clears `this.IsSkillUsable.Clear();` — the HashSet of usable skill names. The two dictionaries `ActiveSkills` (line 39, `Dictionary<string, ActiveSkillDetails>`) and `ActiveSkillCooldowns` (line 22, `Dictionary<uint, ActiveSkillCooldown>`) are *not* cleared. The for-loops at lines 174 and 180 overwrite each entry by key (`UnknownIdAndEquipmentInf0` for cooldowns, skill `name` for active skills). Old keys not present in the new read remain in the dictionary indefinitely.
- **Why it's a bug:** The player swaps a skill gem (e.g., removes "Vaal Lightning Strike" from a socket). The next `UpdateData` reads the new skill list which no longer contains "Vaal Lightning Strike". The for-loop iterates the new skills only — "Vaal Lightning Strike" stays in `ActiveSkills["Vaal Lightning Strike"]` with stale `ActiveSkillDetails` (cooldown counts, use stage, etc.) forever. Plugin code checking `actor.ActiveSkills.ContainsKey("Vaal Lightning Strike")` returns `true` after the gem is removed. Auto-skill plugins that scan `ActiveSkills` for usable skills then try to use "Vaal Lightning Strike" against a non-existent skill slot → input goes to wrong/random skill or to nothing. Also: the dictionaries grow monotonically (new gem swaps add new keys without removing old), so over a long session memory grows unbounded.
- **Suggested fix:** Clear both dictionaries at the top of `UpdateData` (alongside `IsSkillUsable.Clear()`):
  ```csharp
  this.IsSkillUsable.Clear();
  this.ActiveSkills.Clear();
  this.ActiveSkillCooldowns.Clear();
  ```
  Same as the existing `IsSkillUsable.Clear()` pattern. The for-loops then re-populate from the fresh memory read.
- **Risk if left:** Stale skill detection across skill swaps; auto-skill plugins target removed skills. Memory inflates with every gem swap. Exact contributing factor to "auto-attack hits wrong key" reports.

### F-120 — `StateMachine.UpdateData` has no upper bound on `statesCount` — torn read of StdVector triggers a 2 M-element loop and list allocation

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/StateMachine.cs:34-53`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 34: `var stateValues = reader.ReadStdVector<long>(data.StatesValues);` — bounded by `ReadStdVector`'s `length > 16_000_000` cap (F-12). For `T = long`, that maps to `16_000_000 / 8 = 2_000_000` elements max. Line 35: `var statesCount = stateValues.Length;` — up to 2 M. Line 44: `var statesList = new List<StateMachineState>(statesCount);` — list with capacity up to 2 M. Line 45-51: for-loop reads `stateNameAddr = statesPtr + i * StateStructSize` (StateStructSize = 0xC0) for `statesCount` iterations. Each iteration calls `reader.ReadMemory<StdString>` and `reader.ReadStdString`. With `i = 1_999_999`, the read address is `statesPtr + 0xC0 * 1_999_999 = statesPtr + ~239_999_880` — a huge offset that almost certainly fails (`addr > MaxUserModeAddress` check returns default).
- **Why it's a bug:** Even though the read fails for high indices, the *iteration* doesn't stop — the for-loop runs all 2 M iterations, calling `ReadMemory` and `ReadStdString` 2 M times. Each `ReadMemory<StdString>` does a P/Invoke call to `ReadProcessMemory`. The total cost: ~2 M × (Win32 syscall + branch). On modern hardware, ~2 M syscalls take seconds. The render thread / entity reader stalls for that duration. This is a denial-of-service attack vector if a malicious plugin or a torn read produces a `StatesValues.Last - StatesValues.First` of `15_999_999` bytes. POE's actual state machines have a small number of states (< 50 typical, maybe < 200 max for boss state machines).
- **Suggested fix:** Add a hard upper bound at line 35:
  ```csharp
  const int MaxStateMachineStates = 256;
  var statesCount = Math.Min(stateValues.Length, MaxStateMachineStates);
  if (stateValues.Length > MaxStateMachineStates) {
      Console.WriteLine($"[StateMachine] Suspicious state count {stateValues.Length} at {this.Address.ToInt64():X}; capping to {MaxStateMachineStates}");
  }
  ```
  Same defensive cap pattern as `MaxComponentsInAnEntity = 50` in `Entity.cs`. The list-capacity allocation also cleanly caps.
- **Risk if left:** Torn read of one entity's state machine stalls the entity reader for seconds. Symptom: "overlay freezes when I get near boss X". Hard to diagnose because it's a one-shot stall, not a permanent lockup.

### F-158 — `SettingsWindow` four widgets call `RemoveAt(i)` inside `for (var i = 0; i < Count; i++)` — skips the entry shifted into slot `i`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/SettingsWindow.cs:242-308, 375-383, 408-416, 449-457`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Four widgets render a settings list with a per-row delete button, all using the same broken pattern:
  - `DrawPoiWidget` lines 242-308: `for (var i = 0; i < Core.GHSettings.PoiMonstersCategories2.Count; i++) { ... if (ImGui.Button("delete##...")) Core.GHSettings.PoiMonstersCategories2.RemoveAt(i); }`
  - `DrawMonstersToIgnore` lines 375-383: same pattern on `MonstersPathsToIgnore`.
  - `DrawNPCWidget` lines 408-416: same pattern on `SpecialNPCPaths`.
  - `DrawMiscObjWidget` lines 449-457: same pattern on `SpecialMiscObjPaths`.
  
  After `RemoveAt(i)`, the next loop iteration is `i + 1`, but the entry that was at `i + 1` has shifted into slot `i` — that entry is *not* rendered for the rest of this frame. On the next frame, the loop starts from 0 again, so the user does see it again — but only after one missed frame.
- **Why it's a bug:** The visible symptom is mild: clicking "delete" on row N briefly hides row N+1 for one frame. But:
  1. If the loop body has any side effect that depends on iteration count (none currently, but a future audit might add one), the off-by-one becomes a real bug.
  2. If the user spam-clicks the delete button on rapid consecutive rows, multiple skipped entries pile up in a single frame.
  3. The pattern is well-known anti-pattern; this is exactly the same bug shape as F-187 below (`PerformanceStats` removes coroutines mid-iteration) and F-141 (`AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` `TryRemove` mid-Parallel.ForEach).
- **Suggested fix:** Standard pattern — iterate in reverse: `for (var i = list.Count - 1; i >= 0; i--)`. Or append the to-remove index to a side list and apply after the for loop. Reverse-iter is the simplest fix.
- **Risk if left:** Minor visual glitch on delete; latent risk for any future side-effect added to the loop body.

### F-174 — `KrangledPassiveDetector.Process Tree data` indexes `krangledSkillTree[pos]` with no `ContainsKey` guard after gathering "missing" lists

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:117-142`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 117-131 gather `skillMissingInKrangled` (positions in standard but not in krangled) and `skillMissingInStandard`. Then lines 133-142:
  ```csharp
  foreach (var (pos, skillId) in standardSkillTree) {
      var krangledSkillId = krangledSkillTree[pos];   // (!) no ContainsKey check
      if (skillConvertor.TryGetValue(skillId, out var value) && value != krangledSkillId) { ... }
      skillConvertor[skillId] = krangledSkillId;
  }
  ```
  The first `pos` in `standardSkillTree` that is *not* in `krangledSkillTree` (which is exactly what was gathered as "missingInKrangled" three lines earlier) hits `krangledSkillTree[pos]` with no `ContainsKey` check, throwing `KeyNotFoundException`.
- **Why it's a bug:** The earlier guard logic (lines 117-123) explicitly enumerated and tracked these missing positions, but the conversion loop doesn't use that data. The bug only fires when the standard and krangled trees diverge (the typical case the tool is built for) — *exactly* when the tool needs to work. The exception kills the entire `KrangledPassiveDetectorCoRoutine` (extension of F-100 / F-058), so the window vanishes silently with no error popup.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a guard:
  ```csharp
  foreach (var (pos, skillId) in standardSkillTree) {
      if (!krangledSkillTree.TryGetValue(pos, out var krangledSkillId)) continue;
      // ... rest unchanged
  }
  ```
  Or filter out missing positions earlier.
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only feature, but the *primary use case* of the tool — comparing differing trees — crashes the tool window. Tool is essentially broken when the user has any tree divergence.

### F-007 — Explicit-`bytesToSkip` constructor does not strip `^` from input

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:92-98`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** The two-argument `Pattern(string name, string arrayOfHexBytes, int bytesToSkip)` constructor passes the split tokens directly to `ParseArrayOfHexBytes` without filtering `^`. The string-only constructor does filter `^` (line 81: `.Where(hex => hex != "^")`).
- **Why it's a bug:** If a caller passes an `arrayOfHexBytes` that contains `^` along with an explicit `bytesToSkip`, `ParseArrayOfHexBytes` sees `^`, falls through the `?` branch, and calls `byte.Parse("^", NumberStyles.HexNumber)` which throws `FormatException`. The two constructors should be consistent — both should strip `^`.
- **Suggested fix:** In the explicit-bytesToSkip constructor, add `.Where(hex => hex != "^")` (or filter `^` once inside `ParseArrayOfHexBytes`).
- **Risk if left:** Mixing `^` with explicit `bytesToSkip` triggers a `FormatException` at type init with no obvious cause.

### F-012 — `StdVector.TotalElements` divides by caller-supplied size with no zero check

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/StdVector.cs:18-21`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `TotalElements(int elementSize)` returns `(Last - First) / elementSize` with no guard. `Marshal.SizeOf<T>` is the typical caller, which is normally non-zero, but defensive code paths or a misused empty/zero-sized struct produce `DivideByZeroException`.
- **Why it's a bug:** No defensive check; even though the caller-side `ReadStdVector` already gates on `length % typeSize`, callers using `TotalElements` directly (e.g. for diagnostics, `ToString()` itself passes `1` so it is safe) could still pass `0` from a buggy size calculation. Also: when `Last < First` (corrupted/torn read) the result is negative, but the consumer interprets it as a count.
- **Suggested fix:** `if (elementSize <= 0) return 0; var bytes = Last.ToInt64() - First.ToInt64(); return bytes <= 0 ? 0 : bytes / elementSize;`
- **Risk if left:** Misuse produces `DivideByZeroException` or negative element counts that crash downstream loops.

### F-033 — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdList` zero-pointer guard runs after the read

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/SafeMemoryHandle.cs:370-380`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Loop body:
  ```csharp
  var currNode = this.ReadMemory<StdListNode<TValue>>(currNodeAddress);
  if (currNodeAddress == IntPtr.Zero) { Console.WriteLine(...); break; }
  ```
  The zero-check happens *after* the read at the previous line.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not a real bug because `ReadMemory` itself early-returns `default` when `addr <= 0`, so reading from `IntPtr.Zero` is a safe no-op. But the code reads as if the author forgot to check before reading; clarity-wise the check should precede the read. Cost is one wasted read of zero per loop entry — negligible.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the check above the `ReadMemory` call. Or restructure: `while ((currNodeAddress != Head) && (currNodeAddress != IntPtr.Zero) && (++iter < maxIter)) { ... }` (combine with F-032 fix).
- **Risk if left:** Cosmetic; defensive logic still works.

### F-054 — `MiscHelper.TryConvertStringToImGuiGlyphRanges` returns `false` if last element is not `0x00`, even though parsing succeeded

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:51-74`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Method tries to parse comma-separated hex strings into `ushort[]`. It returns `false` if a `Convert.ToInt32` throws (line 67-70) — fine. But the final `return ranges[^1] == 0x00;` at line 73 returns `false` if the last element is not zero, even though all elements parsed cleanly. Caller `GameOverlay.cs:66` and `SettingsWindow.cs:210` interpret `false` as "parse failed" and skip applying the ranges.
- **Why it's a bug:** ImGui's glyph-range API is conventionally null-terminated (last `ushort` = 0), but the user's mistake of forgetting the trailing 0 is then conflated with a malformed input. The user's setting is silently dropped without log; they don't know whether they had a typo, a missing zero, or an unsupported character. Standard library convention: `TryParse` returns `true`/`false` only for parse success, with a separate validation pass for semantic checks.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) split into `TryConvert` (parse) + `IsValidGlyphRange` (semantic), or (b) auto-append a trailing `0x00` if it's missing (defensive), or (c) at minimum log the reason for the false return when validity fails post-parse.
- **Risk if left:** User-visible silent failure of custom font glyph ranges; user has no diagnostic.

### F-070 — `Core.version` is `null!`; `GetVersion().Trim()` NREs if `Initialize()` is skipped

- **File:** `GameHelper/Core.cs:30, 129-132`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `private static string version = null!;` — the field is null until `Initialize()` runs. `GetVersion()` returns `version.Trim()`. If any caller invokes `GetVersion()` before `Initialize()` (or if `Initialize()` itself throws — its `try/catch` catches all exceptions and assigns `"Dev"`, but a missing `Assembly.GetExecutingAssembly().Location` returning `null` could slip through), `version.Trim()` raises `NullReferenceException`.
- **Why it's a bug:** The control flow today is `Program.Main` → `new GameOverlay(...)` → coroutines started → `await Run()` → `Core.Initialize()` → `Core.InitializeCororutines()` → `await base.Run()` → first render frame. By the time anyone calls `GetVersion()` (the only consumer is `SettingsWindow.cs:699` inside the render loop), `version` is set. So no live bug.
  
  But the `null!` annotation is a footgun: any future caller, plugin, or static init path that touches `GetVersion()` *before* `Initialize` (e.g. a plugin static ctor running during `PManager.InitializePlugins` in `PostInitialized` — fine in current order, but a refactor could move it earlier) crashes with no diagnostic.
- **Suggested fix:** Initialize the field eagerly: `private static string version = "Unknown";`. Drop the `null!` suppression; the field is then always non-null. `Initialize()` overwrites with the correct version. Defensive reads are then natural. Optionally make `GetVersion()` return `version ?? "Unknown"` as belt-and-braces.
- **Risk if left:** Latent NRE if the init order changes; today: zero impact.

### F-082 — DEBUG `PManager.LoadPlugin(string name)` uses `Contains` substring match — picks wrong plugin when names share prefixes

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:91-116`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `var container = GetPluginsDirectories().Where(x => x.Name.Contains(name)).Select(LoadPlugin)...`. `Contains` matches anywhere in the directory name, not equality. Loading plugin "Test" matches directories "TestRunner", "MyTest", "Test", and "TestUtils" — all four get loaded. The code then takes `container[0]` and ignores the rest, so the user gets a non-deterministic load (depends on FS enumeration order).
- **Why it's a bug:** Despite being DEBUG-only, it's directly user-facing (the dev menu) and silently does the wrong thing. The same method is called in dev workflows where naming overlap is common (e.g., `Radar` vs `RadarPlus`). The "wrong plugin loaded" outcome is hard to diagnose because no log tells the developer which directory was selected.
- **Suggested fix:** Use exact match: `x.Name == name` (case-insensitive comparison via `string.Equals(x.Name, name, StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase)` if cross-FS consistency is desired). Alternatively, log a warning when multiple matches are found.
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only impact — affects plugin developers, not end users. Diagnosis-by-confusion when developing related plugins.

### F-083 — `PManager.ReadPluginFiles` glob `{DirName}*.dll` plus `FirstOrDefault` can pick wrong DLL; rename of dir without DLL silently fails

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:129-138`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `pluginDirectory.GetFiles($"{pluginDirectory.Name}*.dll", SearchOption.TopDirectoryOnly).FirstOrDefault()` — case 1: directory `Radar` containing both `Radar.dll` and `RadarPlus.dll` (e.g., a debug build artifact), `FirstOrDefault` picks one based on Windows directory-enumeration order, which is filesystem-dependent. Case 2: directory `Radar2` containing `Radar.dll` (forgotten to rename), the glob `Radar2*.dll` matches nothing, the "Couldn't find plugin dll" log fires — but the actual plugin DLL is right there. Case 3: directory `radar` (lowercase) containing `Radar.dll` — Windows is case-insensitive so `radar*.dll` matches `Radar.dll`; OK on Windows but breaks if the project ever ports to Linux/macOS via .NET cross-platform.
- **Why it's a bug:** The DLL-must-match-directory-name convention is implicit and the failure modes are silent. The glob pattern doesn't anchor to a single match; users with two DLLs in the same plugin folder get non-deterministic behavior.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) require exact match `$"{pluginDirectory.Name}.dll"` (drop the `*`) and document the convention loudly, or (b) require a `manifest.json` per plugin that names the entry DLL explicitly. Option (a) is the minimum-risk change. Update the error log to be explicit about the naming convention.
- **Risk if left:** Plugin developers debugging a non-loading plugin spend time tracking down the implicit naming rule. Edge cases produce silent wrong-DLL loads.

### F-085 — `PManager.LoadPlugin` derives plugin root via `string.Replace(PluginsDirectory.FullName, PluginsDirectory.Name)` — fragile if any path component duplicates the substring

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:151-162`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `var relativePluginDir = pluginDirectory.FullName.Replace(State.PluginsDirectory.FullName, State.PluginsDirectory.Name);` builds the relative path the plugin sees as its `DllDirectory` by string substitution. If `State.PluginsDirectory.FullName` is e.g. `C:\Apps\GameHelper\Plugins` and the plugin is at `C:\Apps\GameHelper\Plugins\Radar`, the result is `Plugins\Radar`. If the user installs to `C:\Plugins\GameHelper\Plugins\Radar` (a real-world Windows path with `Plugins` higher up), `Replace` finds the *first* occurrence — `C:\Plugins\GameHelper\Plugins\Radar`.Replace(`C:\Plugins\GameHelper\Plugins`, `Plugins`) → `Plugins\Radar`. OK in this case. But: `C:\Plugins\Plugins\Radar` (user mirrors the dir name) and `PluginsDirectory.FullName` = `C:\Plugins\Plugins`, then the Replace produces `Plugins\Radar` which is correct only because the longest match wins — but `Replace` is not greedy in general; in this specific case where both substrings are at the start, it works. The deeper issue is the use of string substitution where `Path.GetRelativePath(State.PluginsDirectory.FullName, pluginDirectory.FullName)` would do the right thing.
- **Why it's a bug:** Path manipulation via string Replace is the wrong tool. `Path.GetRelativePath` (.NET Core 2.0+, available in .NET 10) is purpose-built and handles edge cases (trailing separators, case-insensitive matching on Windows, normalisation). The current code happens to work for typical install paths but is a footgun for unusual paths and breaks symmetry with how the framework wants you to handle paths.
- **Suggested fix:** `var relativePluginDir = Path.Combine(State.PluginsDirectory.Name, Path.GetFileName(pluginDirectory.FullName));`. This produces e.g. `Plugins\Radar` deterministically.
- **Risk if left:** Edge-case paths produce wrong `DllDirectory`. Any plugin that uses `DllDirectory` to load resources from disk (typical for plugins with icons or templates) would fail. Today's user base apparently hasn't hit this — fragile.

### F-090 — `PManager.LoadPlugin(Assembly, ...)` requires plugin entry class to be `sealed`; missing `sealed` silently rejects plugin with confusing log

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:176-184`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Filter: `var iPluginClasses = types.Where(type => typeof(IPCore).IsAssignableFrom(type) && type.IsSealed).ToList();`. If the plugin author writes `public class MyPlugin : PCore<MySettings>` (no `sealed`), the type is excluded, the count is 0, and the log says: `"Plugin (in {dir}) {assembly} contains 0 sealed classes derived from CoreBase<TSettings>. It should have one sealed class derived from IPlugin."` Two problems with the message: (a) "CoreBase<TSettings>" is an old name — actual base is `PCore<TSettings>`; (b) "IPlugin" is also stale — actual interface is `IPCore`.
- **Why it's a bug:** Plugin authors copy templates that may or may not have `sealed`. Forgetting `sealed` produces an obscure error that mentions two type names that don't exist in the current codebase. Stale documentation in error messages causes search-fail on the actual class names. The `IsSealed` requirement itself is reasonable (prevents diamond-inheritance edge cases) but should be documented in `PCore`.
- **Suggested fix:** (a) Update the error message to use current names: "should have exactly one `sealed` class derived from `PCore<TSettings>`". (b) Document the `sealed` requirement in `PCore` XML doc. (c) Optional: split the diagnostic into "found 0 IPCore-derived classes (forgot to inherit?)" vs "found N derived classes but none are sealed (forgot `sealed` keyword?)" — different fix path for each.
- **Risk if left:** Plugin developers waste time on a confusing error message. Not user-facing.

### F-098 — `GameStates.UpdateData` magic constant `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 0x10` assumes 8-byte pointer (x64-only)

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:108`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `var cStateAddr = reader.ReadMemory<IntPtr>(data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 0x10); // Get 2nd-last ptr.` The comment says "Get 2nd-last ptr", and the offset `0x10` (16) is two pointers' worth assuming `sizeof(IntPtr) == 8` (x64). On x86 (`sizeof(IntPtr) == 4`), `0x10 = 16` would be 4 pointers back, not 2.
- **Why it's a bug:** The codebase appears to be x64-only (the rest of the offset structs assume 8-byte pointers; the project is compiled `AnyCPU` but practical operation requires x64 PoE process). However, the magic `0x10` hardcodes that assumption silently. A more defensive form is `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 2 * IntPtr.Size`, which scales correctly. Even better: a named constant `private const int SecondLastPointerOffset = 2 * IntPtr.Size;` (but `IntPtr.Size` is not a compile-time constant — would need a `static readonly`).
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 0x10` with `data.CurrentStatePtr.Last - 2 * IntPtr.Size`. Self-documenting and architecture-correct.
- **Risk if left:** Latent x64-only assumption; harmless under the current build target. Trip wire for any future port or for someone reading the comment "2nd-last ptr" and mentally computing `2 * 4 = 8` (wrong).

### F-099 — `GameStates.UpdateData` reads `data.States[i]` for `i < 12` then accesses `States[0]` and `States[4]` by hard-coded index — fragile coupling to enum ordering

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameStates.cs:97-103`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 97-100 build the `AllStates` dictionary by iterating `i = 0..TOTAL_STATES-1` and casting `i` to `GameStateTypes`. Lines 102-103 then directly dereference `data.States[0].X` and `data.States[4].X` to populate `AreaLoading` and `InGameStateObject` — relying on the unchecked invariant that the enum's index 0 is `AreaLoadingState` and index 4 is `InGameState`. The `GameStateTypes` enum is in `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/GameStateTypes.cs` and currently has those values at the right indices. Any future enum reordering — even adding a new state at the start — silently rewires `AreaLoading` and `InGameStateObject` to the wrong game memory addresses.
- **Why it's a bug:** The code assumes the game internally orders its state pointer array in the *same* order as the enum declaration, AND that the enum hasn't been reordered. Both assumptions are correct today, but neither is enforced. A safer form is to look up by enum name: `data.States[(int)GameStateTypes.AreaLoadingState].X` — at least the cast makes the dependency explicit (still implicitly couples to the enum's underlying integer values).
- **Suggested fix:** Use named enum values: `this.AreaLoading.Address = data.States[(int)GameStateTypes.AreaLoadingState].X; this.InGameStateObject.Address = data.States[(int)GameStateTypes.InGameState].X;`. Document in `GameStateTypes.cs` that the enum order is load-bearing for the array offset assumption. Optionally add a startup assertion that the enum has the expected values.
- **Risk if left:** A future enum-reorder PR (e.g., reorganizing for readability) silently breaks the overlay's ability to detect AreaLoadingState and InGameState. Failure mode: overlay never recognizes when the player is in-game — total functional loss.

### F-103 — `LoadedFiles.ToImGui` Save button uses user-controlled `filename` field with no path-traversal sanitization

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:64, 74-76`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 64: `ImGui.InputText("##filename", ref this.filename, 100);` — user types any string up to 100 chars. Line 75: `Path.Join(dir_name, this.filename)`. If the user types `../../../../etc/passwd` or `..\\..\\Configs\\config.json` and clicks Save, the file is written outside `preload_dumps/`. `Path.Join` does not normalize/reject `..` segments — that's `Path.GetFullPath` semantics on .NET 5+ with the optional `basePath` argument.
- **Why it's a bug:** The Save button is a debug feature; the user is presumed-trusted (they're running the host). But the lack of validation means a copy-paste of a filename containing `..` writes outside the dumps directory, potentially overwriting host config files. There's also no extension validation — the user could write `config.json` with the JSON-formatted Newline-joined preload list and confuse the host on next load.
- **Suggested fix:** Validate `this.filename` before save: `if (this.filename.Contains("..") || Path.IsPathRooted(this.filename) || this.filename.IndexOfAny(Path.GetInvalidFileNameChars()) >= 0) { /* show error */ return; }`. Alternatively, use `Path.GetFullPath(Path.Join(dir_name, filename))` and verify the result starts with the resolved `dir_name`. Or auto-construct the filename from area name + hash with no user input (already populated at line 185, just remove the `InputText`).
- **Risk if left:** User-typo writes preload data outside the intended directory; tiny security surface for "trusted user but accidental input" scenarios. Not a real attack vector.

### F-117 — `MinimapIcon.IconName` never reset when read fails — stale value retained when icon disappears or read errors

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:26, 55-75`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `IconName` is a `string?` property with private setter, defaulting to `null`. Inside `UpdateData`, the field is set only inside the success path: `this.IconName = this.TryReadUtf16String(namePtr);` (line 70). All early-exit paths — `ptr20 == IntPtr.Zero` (line 65), `(long)ptr20 <= 0x10000` (line 65), `namePtr == IntPtr.Zero` (line 68), `(long)namePtr <= 0x10000` (line 68), `TryReadUtf16String` returning `null` (line 50/51), the catch-all (line 74) — leave `IconName` at its previous value.
- **Why it's a bug:** When the underlying memory becomes unreadable mid-session (entity transitioning, torn read, game patched the icon), `IconName` retains the value from the previous successful read. Consumers checking `if (mi.IconName == "RewardChestExpedition")` for a chest that has now had its icon cleared still see the old name and process the chest as if the icon were live. Combined with F-114 (empty catches), there is no log to diagnose why an icon name is "stuck".
- **Suggested fix:** Reset to `null` at the top of `UpdateData` before any read:
  ```csharp
  this.IconName = null;
  // ... existing read logic ...
  ```
  Or reset inside each early-exit branch. The single top-of-method reset is simpler.
- **Risk if left:** Plugins using `MinimapIcon.IconName` for icon-based filtering see stale icons; debugging requires comparing memory state to reported name.

### F-118 — `Animated.UpdateData` only reads `Path`/`Id` when `hasAddressChanged` — stale data if AnimatedEntityPtr changes at the same component address

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Animated.cs:46-63`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** The body is wrapped in `if (!hasAddressChanged) return;` (lines 48-51). All actual reads — including the dereference of `data.AnimatedEntityPtr` — happen only when the *component* address (`this.Address`) changes. The `AnimatedEntityPtr` value at offset 0x280 inside the component, however, can change while the component address remains stable: e.g., a portal/transition entity that swaps its referenced animation between active/inactive states.
- **Why it's a bug:** When `AnimatedEntityPtr` changes at the same component address, `Path` and `Id` retain stale values. Consumers using `Animated.Path` for entity-class detection (e.g., "is this a Strongbox animated effect or a Boss spawner animation") see the old class long after the game has swapped to a different one. Less common than the Mods/Actor cases — most components have static class identity — but still incorrect for scenarios where the entity reuses a component slot for a different animated class.
  Note: the same pattern appears in `Charges`, `Chest` (F-119), `Mods`, `ObjectMagicProperties`, `Player` — but only `Mods/OMP` and `Chest` have meaningful in-game state changes that the gate prevents from updating. `Charges` writes `Current` outside the gate (line 49), `Player` writes `Xp/Level` outside (lines 61-62). So `Animated` is in the same "rare-change but real" category as `Chest`.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop the `hasAddressChanged` gate or — for performance — add a "did the AnimatedEntityPtr change" check: read the pointer cheaply, compare to the cached one, and only re-read Path/Id if it differs:
  ```csharp
  var data = reader.ReadMemory<AnimatedOffsets>(this.Address);
  this.OwnerEntityAddress = data.Header.EntityPtr;
  if (data.AnimatedEntityPtr == this.cachedAnimatedEntityPtr) return;
  this.cachedAnimatedEntityPtr = data.AnimatedEntityPtr;
  // ... rest of the read ...
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Stale animation class on entities that reuse the Animated component slot. Rarely user-visible but contributes to "this entity is reporting the wrong class" plugin bug reports.

### F-119 — `Chest.UpdateData` only reads `IsStrongbox`/`IsLabelVisible` when `hasAddressChanged` — strongbox/label-visibility transitions invisible to consumers

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Chest.cs:56-62`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `IsOpened` (line 56) is read on every UpdateData. `IsStrongbox` and `IsLabelVisible` are gated behind `if (hasAddressChanged)` (line 57). Both flags depend on the dereferenced internal struct (`ChestsStructInternal`).
- **Why it's a bug:** `IsLabelVisible` can change at runtime — e.g., Breach chests reveal their labels at certain phases of the breach event; some Legion chests reveal labels mid-encounter. `IsStrongbox` is more static (a chest is or isn't a strongbox by design) but the underlying internal pointer may transiently report otherwise during a torn read on the very first `UpdateData` (when `hasAddressChanged=true` includes the first attach). After the gate fires once with a torn read returning incorrect values, the wrong flags persist for the entire session.
- **Suggested fix:** Move `IsStrongbox` and `IsLabelVisible` outside the `if (hasAddressChanged)` block, accepting the per-frame extra `ReadMemory<ChestsStructInternal>` cost. Alternatively, re-read on first `IsOpened` change, since the chest UI typically updates label visibility around state transitions. Cost: one extra read per chest per frame — negligible compared to the entity scan cost.
- **Risk if left:** Label-visibility changes on Breach/Legion chests not detected by overlay plugins. Strongbox detection sticky on torn first-read.

### F-139 — `Entity.consecutiveInvalidFrames` is a non-atomic `int`, incremented from `Parallel.ForEach` entity loop

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:42, 138, 143`, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:296, 308-309`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `private int consecutiveInvalidFrames;` (line 42). Mutators: `IncrementInvalidFrames() => this.consecutiveInvalidFrames++;` (line 138), `ResetInvalidFrames() => this.consecutiveInvalidFrames = 0;` (line 143). Reader: `public int ConsecutiveInvalidFrames => this.consecutiveInvalidFrames;` (line 133). Caller: `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` `Parallel.ForEach(data, ...)` calls `kv.Value.IncrementInvalidFrames()` (line 296) and reads `kv.Value.ConsecutiveInvalidFrames >= staleThreshold` (line 308-309). Each entity is owned by one key in the parallel iteration (the key is the dictionary key, and each parallel worker handles a partition of distinct keys), so for a single Entity instance only one worker calls `IncrementInvalidFrames` — no race today.
  
  However: `Entity.IncrementInvalidFrames()` is `internal` (not `private`) and `int`-postfix-increment is not atomic. A future caller from a *different* parallel context (e.g., `Item.UpdateData` running from `Inventory.UpdateData`'s `Parallel.ForEach`, line 168 — Item inherits Entity) could race. More importantly, an `int` overflow at 2^31 frames (~414 days at 60 FPS — unrealistic in a single session, but possible in a long-running headless dev environment) wraps to `int.MinValue`, which makes the staleness check `consecutiveInvalidFrames >= staleThreshold` false until the counter wraps back up.
- **Why it's a bug:** Today: zero impact (single-worker per entity, sub-414-day session). Latent: an `Item` (which is an Entity subclass) rebinding to the same address from `Inventory.UpdateData`'s `Parallel.ForEach` while `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` iterates the parent dictionary could race the increment if the worker partitions overlap (they shouldn't, but the invariant isn't enforced). Plus: int overflow.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `Interlocked.Increment(ref this.consecutiveInvalidFrames)` and `Volatile.Read(ref this.consecutiveInvalidFrames)` for the read. Bound the increment: `if (this.consecutiveInvalidFrames < int.MaxValue - 1) Interlocked.Increment(...);` to prevent wrap.
- **Risk if left:** Latent overflow / latent race. No live impact today.

### F-140 — `Entity.componentCache.TryGetValue(name, out var comp); component = (T)comp;` — unchecked cast crashes if a component cache entry was inserted as a different `ComponentBase`-derived type with the same `typeof(T).Name`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Entity.cs:178-181`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 178-181:
  ```csharp
  if (this.componentCache.TryGetValue(componenName, out var comp))
  {
      component = (T)comp;
      return true;
  }
  ```
  The cast `(T)comp` succeeds if `comp` is a `T`, otherwise throws `InvalidCastException`. The cache key is `typeof(T).Name` — a string, not a `Type`. Two different `ComponentBase`-derived types in different namespaces with the same simple name (e.g., `MyPlugin.Stats` vs `GameHelper.RemoteObjects.Components.Stats`) collide at the cache key level. A plugin that defines its own component class named `Stats` and calls `TryGetComponent<MyPlugin.Stats>` would either (a) get back a `GameHelper.Stats` instance (cast crash) or (b) overwrite the cache with `MyPlugin.Stats` and break the host's subsequent lookup.
- **Why it's a bug:** Today, all component types are in `GameHelper.RemoteObjects.Components` and there are no name collisions. But the type-system guarantee is missing — the cache should key on `typeof(T)` (a `Type` reference, atomically equal) not `typeof(T).Name` (a string, vulnerable to namespace collisions). The same defect exists at line 184 (`componentAddresses.TryGetValue(componenName, ...)`) but that one only stores `IntPtr` so the cast is safe — the bug is specific to the *cache* path.
- **Suggested fix:** Change cache key to `Type`: `private readonly ConcurrentDictionary<Type, ComponentBase> componentCache;`. Lookup becomes `componentCache.TryGetValue(typeof(T), out var comp)`. Storage line 193 / line 459: `componentCache[typeof(T)] = component;`. The 1:1 relationship between component type and address slot is preserved by the existing `componentAddresses` (string-keyed by game-side name, which is the actual collision-free identifier).
- **Risk if left:** Plugin-defined components with names matching host components silently break.

### F-146 — `Item.UpdateData` sets `IsValid = true` unconditionally — even when item address is invalid

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Item.cs:24-41`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `Item.UpdateData` overrides `Entity.UpdateData`. Lines 33-34: `// this.Id will always be 0x00 because Items don't have / Id associated with them. / this.IsValid = true;` — the `IsValid` field is hardcoded to `true` regardless of whether `this.Address` is valid, whether `reader.ReadMemory<ItemStruct>(this.Address)` returned a populated struct, or whether `UpdateComponentData` succeeded. Compare with the parent `Entity.UpdateData` (line 360-368) which calls `EntityHelper.IsValidEntity(entityData.IsValid)` and short-circuits if invalid.
- **Why it's a bug:** `Inventory.UpdateData` checks `if (!item.Value.IsValid) Items.TryRemove(...)` at line 191-197 — items with `IsValid == false` are removed from the inventory. Since `Item.UpdateData` always sets `IsValid = true`, items are *never* removed by this check — they're only removed when their address transitions to Zero (line 165: `item.Value.IsValid = false;` inside the iteration, then line 168 the `Parallel.ForEach` re-sets to true if any address matches). The "stale items get removed" invariant only works for items whose `invItemPtr` doesn't appear in the new `itemsToInventorySlotMapping` snapshot.
  
  The reachability question: when does `item.Value.IsValid` end up `false` and survive to line 191? Only when `itemsToInventorySlotMapping` no longer references that item (line 165 sets `IsValid = false`; line 168 doesn't re-set it). In that case, removal is correct. So the visible behavior matches intent — but the implementation is fragile: a torn read of `invItem.Item` returning Zero would NOT remove the item (since `Item.UpdateData` would still set IsValid=true). Better defensive form: Item.UpdateData should set IsValid based on whether Address != Zero AND the component-data read succeeded.
- **Suggested fix:** 
  ```csharp
  this.IsValid = this.Address != IntPtr.Zero;
  if (!this.IsValid) return;
  this.EntityType = EntityTypes.Item;
  this.EntitySubtype = EntitySubtypes.InventoryItem;
  if (!this.UpdateComponentData(itemData, hasAddressChanged)) {
      this.UpdateComponentData(itemData, true);
  }
  ```
  Lock IsValid to "address is non-zero and component data was read".
- **Risk if left:** Items with torn-read addresses survive in `Inventory.Items` until the next clean snapshot. Plugin code using `Inventory.Items.Values` to iterate sees ghost items.

### F-147 — `ServerData.ToImGui` `(int)this.selectedInvName > this.PlayerInventories.Count` wrong comparison

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/ServerData.cs:58-61`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 58-61:
  ```csharp
  if ((int)this.selectedInvName > this.PlayerInventories.Count)
  {
      this.ClearCurrentlySelectedInventory();
  }
  ```
  `this.selectedInvName` is an `InventoryName` enum. The `int` value is the *enum value*, not an index into `PlayerInventories`. `PlayerInventories.Count` is the number of inventories the player currently has — say, 30. If the user selected `InventoryName.Cursor1` (`= 13`) but the player has 30 inventories where `InventoryName.Cursor1` is *not one of them* (e.g., `Cursor1 = 13` but `PlayerInventories` only contains keys for slots `1..12, 14..30`), the check `13 > 30` is `false`, so `ClearCurrentlySelectedInventory` is NOT called. Then line 76 (`this.SelectedInv.Address = this.PlayerInventories[this.selectedInvName];`) throws `KeyNotFoundException` because `Cursor1` isn't a key.
- **Why it's a bug:** The intended check is "is the selected enum value still a valid key in the dictionary", which is `this.PlayerInventories.ContainsKey(this.selectedInvName)`. The current check ("is the selected enum value greater than the dict count") was probably copy-pasted from a list-index pattern but enums and dictionary counts are unrelated. Latent crash any time a user selects an inventory and the underlying inventory list shrinks (e.g., area transition removes a special-area inventory).
- **Suggested fix:** Replace with the right semantic check:
  ```csharp
  if (this.selectedInvName != InventoryName.NoInvSelected &&
      !this.PlayerInventories.ContainsKey(this.selectedInvName))
  {
      this.ClearCurrentlySelectedInventory();
  }
  ```
  Also fix line 76 to use `TryGetValue` defensively in case of races.
- **Risk if left:** Debug-widget crash any time the user selects a special-area inventory and then transitions to an area where that inventory doesn't exist. Cascade with F-058 → render thread death.

### F-149 — `AreaLoadingState.UpdateData` only refreshes `CurrentAreaName` when `TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs > lastCache.TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs` — strictly-increasing check fails on game restart

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/AreaLoadingState.cs:60-80`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 66-74:
  ```csharp
  if (data.CurrentAreaDetailsPtr != IntPtr.Zero &&
      !this.IsLoading &&
      data.TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs > this.lastCache.TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs)
  {
      var areaName = reader.ReadUnicodeString(reader.ReadMemory<IntPtr>(data.CurrentAreaDetailsPtr));
      this.CurrentAreaName = areaName;
      this.lastCache = data;
      hasAreaChanged = true;
  }
  ```
  The check `TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs > lastCache.TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs` assumes the in-game timer is strictly increasing across the lifetime of a `AreaLoadingState` instance. It is — *until the game process restarts*. After PoE crashes and relaunches, the timer resets to 0 (or some small value), but `lastCache.TotalLoadingScreenTimeMs` retains the last-seen large value from the previous game session. The condition `0 > 1234567` is false, so `CurrentAreaName` is never updated — the overlay reports the previous game's area name.
  
  `CleanUpData` (line 53-57) does reset `lastCache = default;` and `CurrentAreaName = string.Empty;`, but only fires when `Address` transitions to `IntPtr.Zero` — which happens on `GameStates.CleanUpData` (game close), which happens on `GameProcess.Close()`. The standard sequence on PoE crash: (1) the OS reaps the PoE process, (2) `GameProcess.Monitor` detects via `HasExited`, (3) `Close()` fires, (4) `OnClose` event clears all RemoteObject addresses including `AreaLoading`, (5) `CleanUpData` runs — resets `lastCache`. So the bug doesn't fire on clean PoE close. It fires only if the overlay misses the close detection (F-060 documents this race) and the new PoE process is detected before `lastCache` resets. Narrow window.
- **Why it's a bug:** The same area entered after a fast-relaunch sequence reports the *previous* area's name. Overlay UI shows wrong area. Combined with F-060, the race window is real on every PoE relaunch.
  
  Also: the condition masks legitimate same-area-instant-reload — instant area change to the same area where loading time happens to round to a value < the previous one. Theoretically could happen if PoE's loading-time counter has a weird modulo behavior; in practice the counter is monotonic in a session.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) clear `lastCache` in `OnClose` event subscription explicitly so the reset happens regardless of `Address` transition; (b) compare `data.CurrentAreaDetailsPtr != lastCache.CurrentAreaDetailsPtr` instead of timer — pointer equality is the right "is this a new area" signal; (c) drop the timer check entirely and always re-read on `!IsLoading` (more reads but correct).
- **Risk if left:** Wrong area name on PoE-crash-and-relaunch sequence; rare, but presents as "overlay says I'm in Highgate when I'm actually in Lioneye's Watch" with no diagnostic.

### F-151 — `WorldAreaDat.Act` property declared but never assigned in `UpdateData` — always reports `0`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/FilesStructures/WorldAreaDat.cs:38, 87-97`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** The class exposes `public int Act { get; private set; }` (line 38). The offset struct has the field: `[FieldOffset(0x10)] public int Act;` in `WorldAreaDatOffsets.cs` (line 11). `UpdateData` (lines 87-97) reads `Id`, `Name`, `IsTown`, `HasWaypoint`, `IsHideout`, `IsBattleRoyale` — but never reads `data.Act` or assigns `this.Act`. `CleanUpData` does reset `this.Act = 0x00;` (line 79). So `Act` is always `0`.
- **Why it's a bug:** The property is exposed publicly, suggesting plugin authors are expected to read it. They get `0` for every area regardless of which Act it is. A plugin filtering "only show this widget in Act 1" would silently show in every act.
- **Suggested fix:** Add the read in `UpdateData`: `this.Act = data.Act;`. One line.
- **Risk if left:** Plugins relying on `WorldAreaDat.Act` get a wrong value silently. The property suggests the data is available; it isn't.

### F-152 — `ImportantUiElements.AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive` unbounded recursion may stack-overflow on torn read of UI tree

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/ImportantUiElements.cs:190-207`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive(UiElementBase uie)` recurses for each child via `this.AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive(uie[i]!);` (line 196). The `uie[i]` accessor (in `UiElementBase.cs:145-156`) constructs a fresh `UiElementBase(this.childrenAddresses[i], this.parents)` per call — that constructor calls `UpdateData(true)` which reads `data.ChildrensPtr` from memory. A torn read returning a child pointer that points back to a parent — or a UI tree update mid-iteration that produces a parent->child->parent cycle — recurses indefinitely. Render thread default stack 1 MB; ~50 stack frames per recursion level (each holds a fresh `UiElementBase` instance + locals + return address ≈ 200 bytes). That's ~5000 levels to SO; PoE skill trees are < 100 nodes deep, so a 50x cycle triggers SO.
- **Why it's a bug:** `StackOverflowException` is uncatchable in C# — the CLR aborts the thread. With F-058 unfixed, the render thread dies silently. The bug surface increases on UI tree corruption (game patch, rare race with `UiElementParents` cache).
  
  Same defect family as F-137 (`GetUnScaledPosition` parent-chain unbounded recursion) but on the descent side instead of ascent. Skill-tree-panel UI is dense (PoE has thousands of tree nodes), making this the highest-likelihood SO target in the UI traversal layer.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a depth bound: pass `int depth` parameter, bail at `depth > 64` (logging once). PoE skill trees are < 30 levels deep; 64 is generous. Or maintain a visited-addresses HashSet across the recursion.
- **Risk if left:** Hard-to-repro overlay crash when the user opens the skill tree panel during a UI-tree-update window. Cascade with F-058. Recovery: restart overlay.

### F-160 — `SettingsWindow.filterGroup` static field is shared between `DrawPoiWidget` and `DrawMiscObjWidget` — typing in one widget pre-fills the other

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/SettingsWindow.cs:34, 288, 337, 436`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 34 declares `private static int filterGroup = 0;`. Three widgets reference this same field:
  - `DrawPoiWidget` (lines 287-296, 337-339): `Group Number##` for the per-row monster category and `Group Number##addMonsterPoiWidget` for the "add new" form.
  - `DrawMiscObjWidget` (lines 436-447): `Group Number##MiscObjgroup` for the "add new" misc object.
  
  When the user types `42` in the Misc Objects "Group Number" field, then opens the Monster POI tracker and clicks the add-form, the input field starts pre-populated with `42`. Same issue in the other direction.
- **Why it's a bug:** The two widgets manage entirely independent group-number namespaces (Poi monster groups vs. MiscObj groups). Sharing a static field couples them in a way that confuses users who don't realize a stray group number from one screen leaks into another.
- **Suggested fix:** Split into two fields: `private static int poiFilterGroup = 0;` and `private static int miscObjFilterGroup = 0;`. Update each widget's reference.
- **Risk if left:** Confusing user experience; cosmetic.

### F-164 — `State.EntityReaderMaxDegreeOfParallelism` is a free `int` but the `SettingsWindow` UI only exposes `-1, 2, 4, 8, 16, 32, 64` radio buttons

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/State.cs:49`, `GameHelper/Settings/SettingsWindow.cs:553-572`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** `State.EntityReaderMaxDegreeOfParallelism` is a free `int` that gets serialized/deserialized verbatim. The radio-button row at `SettingsWindow` lines 553-572 enumerates only `i = -1, 2, 4, 8, 16, 32, 64` (the loop is `for (var i = 2; i < 128; i*=2)` plus a separate `-1` button). If a user (or a config migration) lands `EntityReaderMaxDegreeOfParallelism = 6`, all 7 radio buttons show unselected and the user has no way to see or change the current value short of editing JSON.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two failure modes:
  1. **Schema migration**: A future change adding e.g. `12` as an option, then reverted, leaves a `12` in user JSON. The UI then silently shows no selection.
  2. **Hand-edited JSON**: Power users who set `8` then later open the GUI to change to `4` see a confusing "no radio is highlighted" state.
  
  Defaults from the field initializer (`= 4`) match a radio button, so a fresh install behaves correctly.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) clamp the field on load to the nearest valid value (`if (!validSet.Contains(value)) value = 4;`), or (b) add a `Custom: ___` numeric input next to the radio strip so users with a custom value can see and edit it. Option (a) is simpler.
- **Risk if left:** Very narrow — only triggered by hand-edited JSON or schema migrations. Cosmetic.

### F-172 — `KrangledPassiveDetector` keys `standardSkillTree` / `krangledSkillTree` by `Vector2` (float) — slight float drift silently misses key matches

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:39-40, 78, 83, 98, 103, 117, 119, 125, 127, 133-135`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 39-40 declare `Dictionary<Vector2, int> standardSkillTree = new();` and `krangledSkillTree`. The keys come from `skillTreeNode.Position` (line 83, 103) — a `Vector2` of (presumably world-space) screen-grid floats read from the game's UI element. `Vector2.GetHashCode()` derives from float bit-patterns; two semantically-equal positions that differ in the lowest bit (e.g., from camera matrix re-orientation, FP recompute) hash differently and miss the lookup.
- **Why it's a bug:** The user-facing instructions ("Please be extra careful and do not move the tree around otherwise this tool will not work" — lines 71, 91) hint at this fragility. If the user pans the tree, scrolls slightly, or even resizes the window between recording standard and krangled trees, every position can shift by a fraction of a pixel — and every lookup at line 119 (`if (!krangledSkillTree.ContainsKey(posStandard))`) and line 127 misses, classifying every node as "missing in krangled" or "missing in standard". Output: the conversion map is empty or wildly wrong, the user gets a "data_krangled.json" that's unusable in PoB, and the only diagnostic is the two "Skill missing in ..." tree nodes showing all node IDs.
- **Suggested fix:** Round positions to integer grid: use `Dictionary<(int X, int Y), int>` keyed by `((int)Math.Round(node.Position.X), (int)Math.Round(node.Position.Y))`. Or use a custom `IEqualityComparer<Vector2>` with epsilon tolerance (`Math.Abs(a.X - b.X) < 0.5f && Math.Abs(a.Y - b.Y) < 0.5f`).
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only feature. The error mode is "tool produces empty conversion map and user has no idea why". Niche audience (PoB Krangled tool authors).

### F-173 — `KrangledPassiveDetector` "Duplicates found" branch logs the error message but still overwrites the dictionary entry

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:78-83, 98-103`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 78-83 (standard tree recording):
  ```csharp
  foreach (var skillTreeNode in skillTreeNodes) {
      if (standardSkillTree.ContainsKey(skillTreeNode.Position)) {
          message = "ERROR: Duplicates found.";
      }
      standardSkillTree[skillTreeNode.Position] = skillTreeNode.SkillGraphId;  // unconditional overwrite
  }
  ```
  The `if` only changes a string; line 83 always assigns. Same pattern at lines 98-103 for krangled. The user is told "ERROR: Duplicates found" but the dictionary actually holds the second-occurrence's `SkillGraphId`.
- **Why it's a bug:** If the user is told there's a duplicate, they expect the tool to refuse processing or at least to flag *which* skill was duplicated. Instead the tool silently picks the second-occurrence value, which may or may not be correct, and proceeds to the conversion stage — producing incorrect output.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) `continue` after detecting the duplicate (keep the first-seen value, skip subsequent), or (b) collect all duplicates into a list and surface them in a child tree node so the user can see what's clashing.
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only; user trust in the tool decreases on misleading error message.

### F-175 — `KrangledPassiveDetector` derives output path via `Replace(".json", "_krangled.json")` — substring-replace corrupts paths where ".json" appears earlier

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/KrangledPassiveDetector.cs:217, 219`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 217: `File.WriteAllText(dataJsonFilePath.Replace(".json", "_krangled.json"), ...)`. Same on line 219 for the success message. `string.Replace` substitutes *every* occurrence. If the user's path is `C:\.json-archive\data.json` (or any path containing `.json` earlier — e.g., a directory named after a JSON archive), the output becomes `C:\_krangled.json-archive\data_krangled.json`, writing to a non-existent directory.
- **Why it's a bug:** Even on benign paths, this is an unsafe pattern. The fix is `Path.ChangeExtension(...)` or `Path.Combine(Path.GetDirectoryName(...), Path.GetFileNameWithoutExtension(...) + "_krangled.json")`.
- **Suggested fix:** `var outPath = Path.Combine(Path.GetDirectoryName(dataJsonFilePath) ?? string.Empty, Path.GetFileNameWithoutExtension(dataJsonFilePath) + "_krangled.json");`. Same for line 219's user-facing path.
- **Risk if left:** DEBUG-only; failure mode is "writes to wrong location, possibly silently succeeds at writing to an unintended folder". Worst case, attacker-controlled input could traverse — but the input is typed by the developer themselves.

### F-187 — `PerformanceStats` calls `Core.CoroutinesRegistrar.Remove(coroutine)` inside `for (var i = 0; i < Count; i++)` — RemoveAt-in-for-loop pattern skips the next coroutine

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceStats.cs:99-104`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Lines 99-104:
  ```csharp
  for (var i = 0; i < Core.CoroutinesRegistrar.Count; i++) {
      var coroutine = Core.CoroutinesRegistrar[i];
      if (coroutine.IsFinished) {
          Core.CoroutinesRegistrar.Remove(coroutine);   // shifts all later entries down
      }
      // ... continues to use `coroutine` for MovingAverage update
  }
  ```
  After `Remove(coroutine)`, the entry at index `i+1` shifts into slot `i`, but the next iteration is `i + 1` — skipping it. If two consecutive coroutines finish in the same frame, the second is not pruned this frame (cosmetic, will be pruned next frame). Worse, the loop body continues to use the removed `coroutine` reference for the MovingAverage update on lines 107-117 — adding a sample for an already-finished coroutine.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same anti-pattern family as F-141 (`AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` TryRemove inside Parallel.ForEach) and F-158 above (`SettingsWindow` RemoveAt-in-for). The performance stats display jitters by one frame on coroutine-batch completion. The MovingAverage update for the just-removed coroutine briefly extends its sample window past coroutine end-of-life.
- **Suggested fix:** Iterate in reverse: `for (var i = Core.CoroutinesRegistrar.Count - 1; i >= 0; i--)`. Or collect to-remove items into a side list and apply after the loop. Skip the rest of the loop body when removed: `if (coroutine.IsFinished) { Remove(coroutine); i--; continue; }`.
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame minor inaccuracy in displayed performance stats; cosmetic.

### F-186 — `PerformanceStats` computes `(int)(1440 / fps)` with no zero-fps guard — first-frame `fps == 0` produces label "Average of last -2147483648 seconds"

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceStats.cs:92-98`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 92: `var fps = ImGui.GetIO().Framerate;`. Line 98: `ImGui.Text($"==Average of last {(int)(1440 / fps)} seconds==");`. `ImGuiIO.Framerate` is a `float`; `1440 / fps` is `float / float`. When `fps == 0` (first frame, before ImGui has accumulated any frame time), `1440 / 0f` returns `float.PositiveInfinity` (IEEE 754, no exception). `(int)Infinity` is `int.MinValue` (`-2147483648`) per CLR's float-to-int conversion rules.
- **Why it's a bug:** The user sees `==Average of last -2147483648 seconds==` for one frame at startup. Cosmetic — disappears on the next frame. Doesn't crash. But sloppy.
- **Suggested fix:** `var seconds = fps > 0.001f ? (int)(1440 / fps) : 10; ImGui.Text($"==Average of last {seconds} seconds==");`. Default to the moving-average windowSize design value (10s).
- **Risk if left:** One-frame visual glitch at startup. Cosmetic.

### F-188 — `PerformanceStats.MovingAverage.windowSize = 144 * 10` is hardcoded for 144 FPS — at 240 Hz the "10 second" average is actually 6 seconds

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceStats.cs:134`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Logic bugs
- **Description:** Line 134: `private readonly int windowSize = 144 * 10; // 10 seconds moving average @ 144 FPS.` The comment is honest about the assumption. With high-refresh monitors (240 Hz, 360 Hz now common), the same windowSize buffer holds only 6 / 4 seconds of data. With low-refresh (60 Hz), it holds 24 seconds.
- **Why it's a bug:** Display label at line 98 reads `"==Average of last {(int)(1440 / fps)} seconds=="` — that label is dynamic and adjusts for FPS, which means it correctly displays the actual average window in seconds. So the user sees the correct number — but at 240 Hz, a 6-second average is misleadingly short for stability analysis. At 60 Hz, a 24-second average is more sluggish than intended.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute `windowSize` from current FPS each frame: `var windowSize = (int)(fps * 10);` and resize the moving-average queue. Or store samples by elapsed-time stamp and prune by time rather than count.
- **Risk if left:** Stat-window length varies with FPS; the label is correct, but the underlying buffer behavior changes. Cosmetic.


### Culture / globalization

### F-002 — `ToLower()` without `Invariant` in process-name dictionary

- **File:** `GameOffsets/GameProcessName.cs:14-18`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** `"Path of Exile 2".ToLower()` is called five times in the dictionary initializer using the current culture. The matching call site in `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:156` also uses `process.MainWindowTitle.ToLower()` (current culture).
- **Why it's a bug:** In Turkish/Azeri locales, `'I'` lowercases to `'ı'` (dotless i), not `'i'`. Today both sides happen to use the same culture so they still match, but `ToLowerInvariant()` is the standard and removes any latent risk if either string is moved (e.g. dictionary cached from a different process culture, or refactored to a static field that runs before culture init).
- **Suggested fix:** Use `ToLowerInvariant()` in both this file and `GameProcess.cs:156`. Even better: precompute a `const string` of the lowercase title or compare with `StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase`.
- **Risk if left:** Hidden trap if cultures are crossed during refactor; pure code-hygiene cost otherwise.

### F-016 — `StdTuple2D`/`StdTuple3D` `ToString()` formatting is culture-dependent for floating `T`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/StdTuple2D.cs:17-20`, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdTuple3D.cs:12-15`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** `$"X: {this.X}, Y: {this.Y}"` uses the current culture's number format. With `T = float`/`double` and a culture using `,` as decimal separator (de-DE, ru-RU, fr-FR, ...), output becomes `"X: 1,5, Y: 2,5"` — ambiguous because the same `,` is the field separator.
- **Why it's a bug:** Logs and any code that re-parses the string become locale-dependent and visually confusing.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `string.Format(CultureInfo.InvariantCulture, "X: {0}, Y: {1}", this.X, this.Y)` or `FormattableString.Invariant($"X: {this.X}, Y: {this.Y}")`.
- **Risk if left:** Log output ambiguous in non-`en-US` locales; only diagnostic impact, no runtime error.

### F-029 — `StatusEffectStruct.ToString()` and `DeployedEntityStructure.ToString()` use culture-dependent number formatting

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Buffs.cs:33-38`, `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Actor.cs:105-108`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** Same shape as F-016 — both `ToString()` overrides use `$"..."` interpolation that picks up the current culture's number format for the embedded fields (`TotalTime`/`TimeLeft` are `float` in `StatusEffectStruct`; `int` fields in `DeployedEntityStructure`). The `float` case in `Buffs.cs` is the live concern (`"Total Time: 1,5"` in de-DE/ru-RU/...), the `int` case in `Actor.cs` is purely defensive.
- **Why it's a bug:** Diagnostic output from buff and skill logging becomes locale-dependent. No functional impact, only readability/parse-back.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap with `FormattableString.Invariant($"...")` or `string.Format(CultureInfo.InvariantCulture, ...)`. Alternatively, `EntityNodeKey.ToString()` (`GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:67-70`) and `EntityNodeValue.ToString()` (line 104-107) have the same concern, though they only emit `uint` and a hex `IntPtr` so the live impact is zero.
- **Risk if left:** Same as F-016 — log output ambiguous in non-`en-US` locales; only diagnostic impact.

### F-065 — `MainWindowTitle.ToLower()` culture-sensitive comparison — extension of F-002 in host code

- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:156`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** `process.MainWindowTitle.ToLower() == windowTitle` uses the current thread's culture to lowercase. Same defect family as F-002 (`GameProcessName.cs:14-18`); both sides happen to use the same culture today, masking the trap.
- **Why it's a bug:** In Turkish/Azeri locales, `'I'.ToLower() = 'ı'` (dotless i). If a future refactor caches `windowTitle` from one locale and reads `MainWindowTitle` in another (e.g. process culture override, or thread-pool work item), the equality fails and game attach silently breaks.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `string.Equals(process.MainWindowTitle, windowTitle, StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase)`. Combined with the F-002 fix (lowercasing the dictionary keys with `ToLowerInvariant`), the two sides become locale-independent.
