- **Risk if left:** Latent breakage in unusual locale configurations; no live impact today.

### F-101 — `LoadedFiles` debug UI uses `ToLower()` (current culture) on file paths and search text — extension of F-002

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:89, 103`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** Two sites: line 89 `this.searchTextSplit = this.searchText.ToLower().Split(...)` and line 103 `kv.Key.ToLower().Contains(this.searchTextSplit[i])`. Both use the current thread's culture for case folding. Same defect family as F-002 / F-065 — Turkish/Azeri locales lowercase `'I'` to `'ı'`, breaking search.
- **Why it's a bug:** Game preload paths contain mixed-case identifiers (`Metadata/Monsters/...`). User search input is whatever the user types. Under tr-TR, searching for `"INSTANCE"` (rare uppercase) lowercases to `"ınstance"` (with dotless ı) which doesn't match `"instance"` (with dotted i) in any path. Pure user-facing breakage in non-en culture.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `ToLowerInvariant()` on both sites. Or, more idiomatically, drop the lowercase entirely and use `string.Contains(searchTextSplit[i], StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase)` at line 103 — eliminates the per-key allocation of a lowercased string copy (also addresses a hot-loop allocation concern, since the loop runs over every loaded file every frame the search box has text).
- **Risk if left:** Search broken in Turkish/Azeri locale; allocation churn in en-US locale (the per-key `ToLower()` allocates a fresh string copy of every preload path on every render frame the search has text — typically 1000+ paths × ~30 chars × 60 FPS = ~2 MB/sec of Gen0 churn).

### F-142 — `AreaInstance.EntitiesWidget` filter compares `Path.ToLower().Contains(...)` — culture-dependent

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:622-624`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** Lines 622-624:
  ```csharp
  if (!(string.IsNullOrEmpty(this.entityPathFilter) ||
      entity.Value.Path.ToLower().Contains(this.entityPathFilter.ToLower())))
  {
      continue;
  }
  ```
  Two `.ToLower()` calls (current thread culture). Same defect family as F-002 / F-065 / F-101. Path strings contain mixed-case identifiers like `Metadata/Monsters/...`; user filter input is whatever the user types. Under tr-TR locale, `'I'.ToLower() = 'ı'` (dotless i) — a user typing `"INSTANCE"` lowercases to `"ınstance"` which doesn't match `"instance"` in any path.
  
  Additional issue: per-render-frame allocation. `Path.ToLower()` allocates a fresh string copy per entity per render frame the filter is non-empty. For 1000 entities × 60 FPS × ~30 chars/path = ~2 MB/sec of Gen0 churn (same family as F-101's terrain-search hot path).
- **Why it's a bug:** Same as F-002 / F-101. Search broken in Turkish/Azeri locale; allocation churn in en-US.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `entity.Value.Path.Contains(this.entityPathFilter, StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase)` — both correct and allocation-free. Same fix shape as F-101.
- **Risk if left:** Search broken in tr/az locales; allocation churn elsewhere.

### F-150 — `WorldAreaDat.UpdateData` `Id.ToLower().Contains(...)` culture-dependent — extension of F-002

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/FilesStructures/WorldAreaDat.cs:95-96`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Culture / globalization
- **Description:** Lines 95-96:
  ```csharp
  this.IsHideout = this.Id.ToLower().Contains("hideout") && !this.Id.ToLower().Contains("map");
  this.IsBattleRoyale = this.Id.ToLower().Contains("exileroyale");
  ```
  Three `.ToLower()` calls, current culture, on every `UpdateData` (i.e., every area change). The `Id` strings come from in-game `WorldArea.dat` — fixed identifiers like `"HeistHub"`, `"KalguuranSettlersLeague"`. They never contain `'I'` in upper case (PoE's identifier convention is PascalCase like `MapWorldsAtoll`), so the Turkish dotless-i case is dormant — but the principle applies.
  
  Also: each `this.Id.ToLower()` is called twice on line 95 (and once on 96) — three string allocations per area change. Minor but mechanical.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-002 / F-065 / F-101 / F-142. Latent locale-dependence; minor allocation churn.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `Contains` with `StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase`:
  ```csharp
  this.IsHideout = this.Id.Contains("hideout", StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase) &&
                   !this.Id.Contains("map", StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase);
  this.IsBattleRoyale = this.Id.Contains("exileroyale", StringComparison.OrdinalIgnoreCase);
  ```
  Or — cleaner — define const `string`s for the two patterns and use `IndexOf` with `Ordinal` comparison.
- **Risk if left:** Latent locale-dependence; minor per-area-change allocation. No live impact today.


### Performance in hot loops

### F-136 — `UiElementBase.this[int i]` allocates a fresh `UiElementBase` per indexer call; combined with recursive `GetUnScaledPosition`, total allocations are O(depth²)

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/UiElement/UiElementBase.cs:144-156, 252-282`
- **Severity:** medium
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Lines 145-156:
  ```csharp
  public UiElementBase? this[int i] {
      get {
          if (this.childrenAddresses.Length <= i) return null;
          return new UiElementBase(this.childrenAddresses[i], this.parents);
      }
  }
  ```
  Each `uie[i]` call allocates a fresh `UiElementBase`. The `UiElementBase` constructor (line 42-51) calls `this.UpdateData(true)` which reads `UiElementBaseOffset` from memory plus a child-pointers `StdVector` plus background color. Per-call cost is large: ~1 P/Invoke ReadProcessMemory + 1 StdVector read + 1 ImGuiHelper.Color allocation.
  
  Consumer hot paths:
  - `ImportantUiElements.AddOrUpdateSkillNodes` line 172: `currentChild.Address = this.passiveskilltreenodes[i]!.Address;` — allocates a fresh element, reads its address, throws it away. **Worse**: the `passiveskilltreenodes[i]!.Address` chain triggers `UpdateData(true)` on the throwaway instance — a full memory read for one address access.
  - `ImportantUiElements.AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive` line 196: `this.AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive(uie[i]!);` — recursion through the skill tree (PoE has 1300+ nodes). Each level allocates a fresh `UiElementBase` for every child, runs `UpdateData(true)`, descends. Total allocations per traversal = O(N nodes) = ~1300+ allocations per `AddOrUpdateSkillNodes` call. Combined with `GetUnScaledPosition` (line 252-282) which itself recurses through the parent chain calling `myParent.GetUnScaledPosition()` (line 260), the parent traversal is per-call (every visible widget per frame), and `myParent` is obtained via `TryGetParent` (cached lookup, OK).
  
  Per-render-frame total for an open skill tree: ~1300 allocations + 1300 P/Invokes + 1300 StdVector reads. At 60 Hz, ~78k allocations/sec.
- **Why it's a bug:** F-051 / F-122 / F-123 family — per-frame allocation in render hot path. Specifically severe for the skill tree traversal because the tree is dense and the indexer is called per child.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the indexer's allocation with an in-place `Address`-set on a *reused* `UiElementBase` instance. The existing `currentChild` pattern at `ImportantUiElements.cs:169-172` partially does this — `var currentChild = new UiElementBase(IntPtr.Zero, this.passiveSkillTreeCache);` then loop `currentChild.Address = this.passiveskilltreenodes[i]!.Address;`. But the right side `this.passiveskilltreenodes[i]` still allocates. Replace with a lower-level helper that returns just the child address (without constructing a full UiElementBase): `public IntPtr GetChildAddress(int i) => i < childrenAddresses.Length ? childrenAddresses[i] : IntPtr.Zero;`. The recursive consumer (`AddSkillTreeNodeUiElementRecursive`) needs a refactor: pass the reusable `UiElementBase` instance through the recursion, set its address per child, recurse. Or convert recursion to iteration with a stack of addresses.
- **Risk if left:** Visible Gen0 GC pressure when skill tree panel is open; periodic stutter. Same family as F-051 but at a higher allocation rate due to the recursion fan-out.

### F-038 — `PatternFinder.Find` writes shared bool/int arrays without synchronisation

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/PatternFinder.cs:73-74, 106, 144-148, 156`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops (concurrency micro-issue)
- **Description:** `isPatternFound[k]` is read without synchronisation at line 106 (`if (isPatternFound[k]) continue;`) and written without synchronisation at line 147. `patternOffsets[k] = currentOffset + j;` likewise (line 148). Multiple parallel chunks may simultaneously discover the same pattern (legitimate when patterns appear at multiple addresses) — they race to set the bool and write the offset.
- **Why it's a bug:** The `isPatternFound[k]` writes are idempotent (always `true`), and the `Interlocked.Increment(ref totalPatternsFound)` on line 146 correctly serialises the count. But the `patternOffsets[k]` write is non-atomic for `int` on x86 (atomic for aligned int on x64, which we are). So on x64, the only effect is non-determinism: which thread's offset wins is random. The "non-unique pattern" check at line 156 (`isPatternFound.All(k => k)`) inside a Parallel.For invocation is racy but harmless — multiple threads may throw the same exception, which gets aggregated.
  Performance angle: the inner `Parallel.For` at line 94 spawns a parallel iteration per byte position `j` of every chunk, which is gross over-parallelism. With 84_000 work items per chunk and `MaxDegreeOfParallelism = 4`, the partitioner overhead dominates. The outer Parallel.For over chunks with `MaxDegreeOfParallelism = 4` would be sufficient.
- **Suggested fix:** (a) Use `Volatile.Write`/`Volatile.Read` on the bool array (or `Interlocked.Exchange` for clarity), (b) drop the inner `Parallel.For` and replace with a sequential `for (var j = 0; ...)` loop — this restores predictable performance and eliminates the race. The outer Parallel.For still parallelises over chunks.
- **Risk if left:** None functional today (x64 + idempotent writes). Perf cost from inner Parallel.For overhead is real but only at startup once per session.

### F-051 — `ImGuiHelper.EnumComboBox` and `StatsWidget` allocate per frame in render hot path

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/ImGuiHelper.cs:177-181, 325-342`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** `EnumComboBox` calls `Enum.GetValues<T>()` on every invocation. This allocates a fresh array each time (the .NET 5+ generic version has a small fast path, but still allocates). `IEnumerableComboBox` then iterates and calls `item?.Equals(current)` per item — for value types, this boxes both `item` and `current` because `object.Equals(object)` is the resolved overload. `StatsWidget` snapshots a `Dictionary<GameStats, int>` to an array per frame inside its TreeNode block (whether or not the tree node is open the lock is taken; the `ToArray()` allocates).
- **Why it's a bug:** Render hot path. ComboBoxes are called per-render-frame (60+ Hz) for every settings widget that uses one. `StatsWidget` is in debug UI only. Per-frame allocations land in Gen0 and trigger frequent GC pauses, visible as stutter. Boxed value-type `Equals` doubles the allocation.
- **Suggested fix:**
  - `EnumComboBox`: cache `Enum.GetValues<T>()` per `T` in a `static class EnumValuesCache<T> { public static readonly T[] Values = Enum.GetValues<T>(); }`.
  - `IEnumerableComboBox`: use `EqualityComparer<T>.Default.Equals(item, current)` to avoid boxing for unconstrained `T`.
  - `StatsWidget`: take the snapshot only inside `if (ImGui.TreeNode(...))` so frames where the tree is closed don't allocate.
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame GC pressure when many combo boxes are visible; minor stutter on busy UIs.

### F-055 — `MiscHelper.KeyUp` uses non-thread-safe static `Random`; `Task.Run` exception is unobserved

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:20-22, 109-137`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops (also concurrency)
- **Description:** Two issues in one method:
  1. `private static readonly Random Rand = new();` plus `Rand.Next() % 10` at line 121. `Random` is documented as not thread-safe in .NET. `KeyUp` is `public static`, so any plugin can call from any thread — concurrent calls can leave `Rand` in a state that returns `0` for many subsequent calls (documented behaviour of pre-.NET-6 Random under contention; .NET 6+ Shared singleton is thread-safe but `new Random()` instance is not).
  2. `sendingMessage = Task.Run(() => SendMessage(...))` at line 132. The Task is fire-and-forget. If `SendMessage` throws (e.g., target window destroyed mid-call), the exception is captured in the Task and never observed → eventually surfaces as an `UnobservedTaskException` event with no useful stack.
- **Why it's a bug:** (1) Today, `KeyUp` is called from a single coroutine (`Rule.Execute` in AutoHotKey plugin), so Random contention doesn't manifest. But the public API surface invites multi-thread misuse. (2) Exception swallowing makes the rare "key send failed" case impossible to diagnose.
- **Suggested fix:**
  - Replace `Rand` with `Random.Shared` (.NET 6+) — thread-safe singleton, no allocation.
  - Add `.ContinueWith(t => Console.WriteLine(t.Exception), TaskContinuationOptions.OnlyOnFaulted)` after `Task.Run`, or `await` it (if the method becomes async). At minimum, log via `TaskScheduler.UnobservedTaskException`.
- **Risk if left:** Latent thread-safety hazard plus missing diagnostics for failed key sends.

### F-064 — `GameProcess.FindAndOpen` calls `Process.GetProcesses()` every 2 s — heavy enumeration of all OS processes

- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:148-185`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Every 2 seconds while no game is attached, `Process.GetProcesses()` enumerates **every** running OS process, allocating a `Process[]` array (typically 200-400 entries on a modern Windows desktop, each a Process object that holds a Win32 process snapshot). The matching loop then reads `process.MainWindowTitle` per element, which P/Invokes `GetWindowTextW` for every process with a window — heavy.
- **Why it's a bug:** Until the game is attached, this poll runs forever. On a busy machine, that's 1.4 KB of process objects allocated per 2 s plus dozens of P/Invokes — minor in absolute terms, but completely avoidable: `Process.GetProcessesByName(string)` filters at the kernel level by image name and avoids `MainWindowTitle` reads on processes that aren't even candidates. Since `GameProcessDetails.ProcessName` is keyed by process name, the lookup can be `foreach (var name in GameProcessDetails.ProcessName.Keys) Process.GetProcessesByName(name)` — typically zero results most of the time.
  
  Additionally, the enumeration leaks `Process` instances — the loop iterates the whole array but only `Add`s matching ones to `processesInfo`. The non-matching `Process` objects are not `Dispose()`d; they hold native snapshot data that's GC'd later. `Process.GetProcesses()` documentation explicitly recommends `Dispose` on each returned instance.
- **Suggested fix:**
  ```csharp
  this.processesInfo.Clear();
  foreach (var name in GameProcessDetails.ProcessName.Keys)
  {
      foreach (var p in Process.GetProcessesByName(name))
      {
          if (p.MainWindowTitle.ToLowerInvariant() == GameProcessDetails.ProcessName[name])
              this.processesInfo.Add(p);
          else p.Dispose();
      }
  }
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Minor CPU cost while waiting for game to launch; Process-instance leak (small, GC-collected eventually).

### F-071 — `Core.RemoteObjectsToImGuiCollapsingHeader` reflects over `Core` properties every frame the Debug widget is open

- **File:** `GameHelper/Core.cs:159-169`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Every render frame the Debug widget is visible, this method calls `RemoteObjectBase.GetToImGuiMethods(typeof(Core), propertyFlags, null)` (line 162). That method enumerates `Core`'s properties via `Type.GetProperties(BindingFlags)` (line 151 in `RemoteObjectBase.cs`), allocating a fresh `PropertyInfo[]` per call. Then for each non-skipped property it calls `property.GetValue(classObject)` (reflection-based getter) and `propertyType.GetMethod("ToImGui", methodFlags)` (reflection-based method lookup). All in a render-frame hot path.
- **Why it's a bug:** Reflection is slow; per-frame allocation churns Gen0; `GetMethod` is particularly heavy because it walks the type hierarchy. With ~10 `Core` properties, this is ~10 reflection ops per frame at ~60 FPS = 600 reflections per second per Debug-widget-open user. Result: minor CPU bump, more importantly Gen0 GC pressure visible as periodic frame stutters.
- **Suggested fix:** Cache the result. `RemoteObjectPropertyDetail` snapshots the `MethodInfo` and the `PropertyInfo` already; build the cache once and reuse:
  ```csharp
  private static RemoteObjectPropertyDetail[]? _cachedReflection;
  internal static void RemoteObjectsToImGuiCollapsingHeader()
  {
      _cachedReflection ??= RemoteObjectBase.GetToImGuiMethods(typeof(Core), flags, null).ToArray();
      foreach (var property in _cachedReflection) { ... }
  }
  ```
  But note: `property.Value` (`property.GetValue(classObject)`) needs to be re-fetched each frame because the underlying property values may change. Cache only the `MethodInfo`+`Name`, refetch `Value`. Net: 1 `GetValue` per property per frame, not 1 `GetProperties()` + 1 `GetValue` + 1 `GetMethod` per property per frame.
- **Risk if left:** Gen0 pressure; minor frame stutter when Debug widget is open. Most users never open it, so live impact small.

### F-094 — `RemoteObjectBase.GetToImGuiMethods` reflects via `Type.GetProperties` + `Type.GetMethod` per call — extension of F-071 at the base layer

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:144-180`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Each invocation of `GetToImGuiMethods(classType, propertyFlags, classObject)` calls `classType.GetProperties(propertyFlags).ToList()` (line 151) — allocating a fresh `PropertyInfo[]` plus a `List<PropertyInfo>` — and inside the loop calls `propertyType.GetMethod("ToImGui", methodFlags)` (line 177) — a name+flags dictionary lookup on the Type's internal method table — for every yielded property. Both calls are unmemoized. Every `RemoteObjectBase.ToImGui` invocation (the instance ToImGui at line 105) repeats this. The method runs in the render-frame hot path whenever the user has the Debug widget open — same call-graph concern as F-071 (which targets `Core.cs`'s use of the same helper), but at the per-instance layer rather than the static `Core` layer.
- **Why it's a bug:** F-071 documents the per-frame allocation/reflection cost for the static `Core` enumeration. The same helper is invoked from `RemoteObjectBase.ToImGui` (line 108) for every `RemoteObjectBase`-derived instance whose tree node is expanded. With ~20 remote object types and several being recursive (e.g., InGameState → AreaInstance → Player → components), per-frame reflection rapidly dominates Debug-widget rendering CPU. Same Gen0 GC pressure pattern.
- **Suggested fix:** Cache reflection results per `classType` keyed on `(classType, propertyFlags)`:
  ```csharp
  private static readonly Dictionary<(Type, BindingFlags), (PropertyInfo prop, MethodInfo? toImGui)[]> _reflectCache = new();
  // populate once via lock-on-miss
  ```
  Then `GetToImGuiMethods` only calls `property.GetValue(classObject)` per call — one reflection-getter per property per frame is unavoidable since the value can change, but the metadata is static.
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame Gen0 pressure proportional to the number of expanded debug tree nodes; minor frame stutter with the Debug widget open. Combined with F-071, the impact roughly doubles for users who keep both `Core` and any specific RemoteObject debug widget open.

### F-107 — `TerrainHeightHelper.ToImGui` `string.Join(' ', this.Values)` allocates a string proportional to terrain-height data per render frame

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/TerrainHeightHelper.cs:35`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** `ImGui.Text(string.Join(' ', this.Values));` — `string.Join` over a `byte[]` builds a string with each byte rendered as base-10 (`"0 0 0 1 ..."`) per render frame the widget is open. Terrain height data length is set in the ctor — likely tens of KB given the typical map terrain grid. With each byte producing 1-3 digits + 1 space ≈ 4 chars per byte, a 30 KB byte array produces a ~120 KB string per frame. At 60 FPS with the widget open, that's ~7 MB/sec of Gen0 allocation just for the debug widget.
- **Why it's a bug:** ImGui debug widget — only matters when the user opens it. Same family as F-051 (per-frame allocation in render hot path) and F-071 (per-frame reflection). Live impact: noticeable Gen0 GC pressure when this widget is open, possibly pausing the overlay for >1 frame at a time.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) cap the displayed length: `ImGui.Text(string.Join(' ', this.Values.Take(256))) + (this.Values.Length > 256 ? " ..." : "")`; (b) avoid recomputing every frame — cache the joined string and only rebuild when the data changes (a hash or a generation counter); (c) gate on `ImGui.IsItemVisible()` to skip computation if the widget is collapsed; or (d) use `ImGui.LabelText` with a static label and a generation-counter-controlled rebuild. (a) is the smallest-risk fix.
- **Risk if left:** Visible Gen0 GC pressure when a developer opens this debug widget; not user-facing.

### F-122 — `MinimapIcon.TryReadUtf16String` allocates a 512-byte buffer per call — extension of F-051 in entity hot path

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:36-52`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** `var bytes = reader.ReadMemoryArray<byte>(address, 512);` (line 40) allocates a fresh 512-byte array per invocation. `TryReadUtf16String` is called from `MinimapIcon.UpdateData` which fires once per frame per `MinimapIcon`-bearing entity. Maps with hundreds of icon-bearing entities (Breach, Expedition, Heist) trigger hundreds of `byte[512]` allocations per frame, plus an `Encoding.Unicode.GetString(bytes, 0, i)` allocation for the resulting string.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same defect family as F-051 (per-frame allocation in render hot path). Allocations land in Gen0; with a busy minimap-rich area the allocation pressure is significant. The codebase already has a `ReadUnicodeString(IntPtr)` primitive in `SafeMemoryHandle` (called from `Animated.UpdateData`, `ObjectMagicProperties.GetModName`, etc.) — `MinimapIcon` reimplements it inline because of the ad-hoc offset arithmetic (see F-121).
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `TryReadUtf16String` with `Core.Process.Handle.ReadUnicodeString(namePtr)`. Drop the manual byte buffer + string scan. Same primitive used elsewhere in this batch, single allocation for the result string.
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame Gen0 pressure proportional to icon-bearing entity count; minor stutter in icon-rich content.

### F-123 — `StateMachine.UpdateData` allocates fresh `List<StateMachineState>` and string copies per update — extension of F-051 in entity hot path

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/StateMachine.cs:44, 48-51`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Every `UpdateData` (per-frame, per `StateMachine`-bearing entity — bosses and complex monsters): line 44 `new List<StateMachineState>(statesCount)` allocates a fresh list. Lines 48-51 then for each state read a `StdString` and a `string` (via `ReadStdString`) and `new StateMachineState(...)` allocates a new wrapper class. Lines 53 `this.States = statesList;` swaps the property (which is `IReadOnlyList<StateMachineState>`).
- **Why it's a bug:** Same defect family as F-051 / F-122. For a typical boss with ~30 states updating at 60 Hz, this is 1800 allocations/sec just for one entity. Maps with 5-10 simultaneous bosses (Delirium, Simulacrum) compound the cost. Allocations land in Gen0 and trigger frequent GC pauses, visible as stutter.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) reuse a single `List<StateMachineState>` field, `Clear()`-ing and re-filling each update; (b) reuse `StateMachineState` class instances by mapping by index (mutable Name/Value) — but the class is `init`-set via primary constructor so this requires refactor; (c) pool the list via `ArrayPool<StateMachineState>` or a per-instance `List<StateMachineState>` reused across updates. Option (a) is the smallest change. Combined with F-120's bound, the per-update cost becomes O(1) allocation + O(N≤256) string allocations (the `ReadStdString` calls — those are unavoidable without further refactor).
- **Risk if left:** Visible Gen0 GC pressure on boss-heavy maps; minor stutter on Simulacrum/Delirium content.

### F-144 — `Inventory.this[y, x]` allocates `new Item(IntPtr.Zero)` on every miss path

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Inventory.cs:67-94`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Lines 67-94: the `this[y, x]` indexer returns `new Item(IntPtr.Zero)` on four early-exit paths (out-of-bounds, mapping miss, zero address, dictionary miss) and a real `Item` from the dictionary on the hit path. Each `new Item(IntPtr.Zero)` allocates a new `Item` (which inherits from `Entity`) — and the `Item(IntPtr)` ctor calls `Entity()` which allocates two `ConcurrentDictionary` instances (`componentAddresses`, `componentCache`, line 61-62 of `Entity.cs`). Three allocations per miss.
  
  The indexer is called from plugin code that inspects inventory grids. The `[y, x]` access pattern of "iterate every slot to find an item" allocates `(rows × cols)` Item-zero instances per call. For a 12×5 standard inventory or larger stash tab grids, that's 60-300 Item allocations per scan. Plugin code that scans inventory each frame compounds the cost.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-051 / F-122 / F-123 / F-136 — per-frame allocation in render hot path. The "return a sentinel `Item(IntPtr.Zero)` and let the caller check `IsValid`" pattern is well-intentioned (avoids null-check ergonomics) but pays for it in allocations.
- **Suggested fix:** Cache a single static-readonly `Item` representing the empty/invalid sentinel:
  ```csharp
  private static readonly Item EmptySlot = new(IntPtr.Zero);
  public Item this[int y, int x] {
      get {
          // ... existing checks ...
          return EmptySlot; // miss path
      }
  }
  ```
  Or change the API to return `Item?` and let the caller use null-conditional. The static-sentinel approach preserves the API.
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame allocation churn proportional to inventory grid size × plugins-using-this. Minor stutter under heavy plugin load.

### F-145 — `Inventory.UpdateData` `this.itemsToInventorySlotMapping.Distinct()` allocates a `HashSet<IntPtr>` per 50 Hz tick

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/Inventory.cs:168`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Line 168: `Parallel.ForEach(this.itemsToInventorySlotMapping.Distinct(), invItemPtr => { ... });`. `Enumerable.Distinct()` over an `IntPtr[]` materializes a `HashSet<IntPtr>` internally to deduplicate, then yields elements. Allocation cost: one HashSet + bucket arrays. For a 60-slot inventory snapshot, the HashSet has ~60 entries.
  
  `OnTimeTick` runs at 50 Hz (line 204: `yield return new Wait(0.02d);`). 50 × 1 HashSet/sec = 50 HashSet allocations/sec, plus the underlying bucket arrays. Same concern in `ServerData.UpdateData` (no Distinct, just `inventoryData[i]` linear iter — fine). `Inventory` is the only hot-loop call site for `Distinct`.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-051. Per-tick allocation; modest in absolute terms (50 Hz × 60 slots × ~1 KB HashSet = 3 MB/sec churn), but easily avoidable. The Distinct exists because `itemsToInventorySlotMapping` can contain duplicate addresses (one item occupying multiple slots, e.g., 2x4 tier-3 maps); without Distinct, `Parallel.ForEach` would process the same `invItemPtr` multiple times.
- **Suggested fix:** Cache a HashSet field on the class and reuse: `private readonly HashSet<IntPtr> distinctScratch = new(); ... distinctScratch.Clear(); for (var i = 0; i < this.itemsToInventorySlotMapping.Length; i++) distinctScratch.Add(this.itemsToInventorySlotMapping[i]); Parallel.ForEach(distinctScratch, ...);`. Reuses the bucket arrays across ticks. Or: skip duplicate work via `ConcurrentDictionary`'s `TryAdd` already guarding (already implicit in line 173-186 — duplicates would just hit `Items.ContainsKey`).
- **Risk if left:** Per-tick Gen0 churn proportional to inventory size; minor.

### F-159 — `SettingsWindow.SaveCoroutine` calls `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` on the render thread — settings serialize+disk-write blocks the UI frame

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/SettingsWindow.cs:730-737`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** `SaveCoroutine` (lines 730-737):
  ```csharp
  while (true) {
      yield return new Wait(GameHelperEvents.TimeToSaveAllSettings);
      JsonHelper.SafeToFile(Core.GHSettings, State.CoreSettingFile);
  }
  ```
  Fires on `TimeToSaveAllSettings` event (raised when user toggles settings hotkey, lines 688, 711). Coroutines are scheduled by the render-event handler (`OnRender` / `TimeToSaveAllSettings` are both raised from the render loop), so the `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` call executes synchronously on the render thread. The settings JSON serialize a `State` object with ~40 fields including a list of POI categories — at user growth (5-50 entries), the serializer + disk write can take 5-50 ms.
- **Why it's a bug:** The user toggles the F12 settings window and expects the next frame to render normally. Instead, the frame stutters by however long `JsonConvert.SerializeObject` + `File.WriteAllText` take. With F-039 (non-atomic write) compounded — a `File.WriteAllText` on a slow disk (Windows Defender scan, anti-virus) can take 100+ ms.
- **Suggested fix:** Marshal the save off the render thread: `Task.Run(() => JsonHelper.SafeToFile(Core.GHSettings, State.CoreSettingFile));`. Combined with F-039 fix (atomic temp+rename), the off-thread save is safe to fail without corrupting in-flight settings.
- **Risk if left:** Single-frame stutter on settings save (every F12 hide). User-perceptible on slow disks.

### F-169 — `DataVisualization` reflects `Core.GHSettings.GetType().GetFields()` per frame — extension of F-071 / F-094 in the DV widget

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/DataVisualization.cs:46-51`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Lines 46-51 inside the `Settings` collapsing-header branch:
  ```csharp
  var fields = Core.GHSettings.GetType().GetFields().ToList();
  for (var i = 0; i < fields.Count; i++) {
      var field = fields[i];
      ImGui.Text($"{field.Name}: {field.GetValue(Core.GHSettings)}");
  }
  ```
  - `Core.GHSettings.GetType().GetFields()` allocates a `FieldInfo[]` of all ~40 public instance fields per frame.
  - `.ToList()` allocates a `List<FieldInfo>` per frame.
  - For each field, `field.GetValue(Core.GHSettings)` boxes the value (every value-type field — `int`, `bool`, `VK`, etc. — boxes to `object`).
  - `$"{field.Name}: {field.GetValue(...)}"` allocates the interpolated string.
  
  Same pattern family as F-071 (`Core.RemoteObjectsToImGuiCollapsingHeader`) and F-094 (`RemoteObjectBase.GetToImGuiMethods`).
- **Why it's a bug:** When the user opens "Data Visualization → Settings", the widget is rendered every frame (no caching). Per-frame: 1 `FieldInfo[]` + 1 `List<FieldInfo>` + ~40 boxed values + ~40 interpolated strings. At 144 Hz × 40 fields = ~6000 boxed values/sec, ~6000 interpolated strings/sec. Gen0 churn proportional to GHSettings field count.
- **Suggested fix:** Cache `FieldInfo[]` once in a `private static readonly FieldInfo[] CachedFields = typeof(State).GetFields();` and reuse. Cannot avoid the `GetValue` boxing, but skipping the reflection allocation cuts ~50% of the alloc cost.
- **Risk if left:** Modest Gen0 churn when DV → Settings widget is visible. DV is a debug feature.

### F-177 — `NearbyVisualization.DrawNearbyRange` `Span<Vector2> points = new Vector2[totalLines]` heap-allocates per frame instead of `stackalloc`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/NearbyVisualization.cs:60`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Line 60: `Span<Vector2> points = new Vector2[totalLines];`. The `new Vector2[40]` clause heap-allocates a 320-byte array, then implicitly converts to `Span<Vector2>`. `DrawNearbyRange` is called up to 2 times per frame (inner + outer circle). At 144 Hz with both circles enabled: 144 × 2 = 288 array allocations per second × 320 bytes ≈ 92 KB/sec Gen0 churn. Per F-051 family.
- **Why it's a bug:** `totalLines` is a constant `40`, well within `stackalloc` limits (~1 KB recommended). Heap allocation is unnecessary.
- **Suggested fix:** `Span<Vector2> points = stackalloc Vector2[totalLines];`. Eliminates the allocation entirely. Note the `ImGui.GetBackgroundDrawList().AddPolyline(ref points[0], totalLines, color, ...)` call (line 75) takes a `ref` to the first element — works with `stackalloc` since the span lives for the function lifetime.
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame Gen0 churn proportional to number of visible circles; minor (~92 KB/sec).

### F-184 — `PerformanceProfiler.Profile()` allocates a fresh `ProfileDisposable` reference object per call when the profiler is enabled

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceProfiler.cs:37-46, 254-276`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** `Profile(namespaceName, methodName)` (line 37) returns a `new ProfileDisposable(...)` (line 45) when `Core.GHSettings.ShowPerfProfiler` is true. `ProfileDisposable` is declared `class`, so each `using (PerformanceProfiler.Profile(...))` block allocates a new heap object. The constructor also captures the `Stopwatch` (which is `class` and was just allocated at line 44) plus three `ConcurrentDictionary` references.
  
  The expected use is "wrap every hot-loop method": each call site is `using var _ = PerformanceProfiler.Profile(...)` at the top of frequently-called methods. Per-frame call count can reach hundreds (entity update loops, per-component reads, etc.).
- **Why it's a bug:** When the profiler is enabled, the act of measuring hurts performance: 2 heap allocations per Profile call (`ProfileDisposable` + `Stopwatch`) × hundreds/frame × 144 Hz = tens of thousands of allocations/sec. The profiler artifact distorts the very measurement it's recording (Heisenbug — hot path's measured cost includes its own allocator overhead).
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `class ProfileDisposable` with a `ref struct` or `struct` returning `IDisposable`-like via custom `Dispose` pattern (C# `using` works with non-interface `Dispose`). Or pool the ProfileDisposable instances via a `ThreadLocal<Stack<ProfileDisposable>>`. The `Stopwatch.StartNew()` allocation can be avoided by using `Stopwatch.GetTimestamp()` directly and storing the start tick in the struct.
- **Risk if left:** Profiler distorts measurements. Profiler is debug-only, but anyone trying to use it to optimize hot paths sees inflated numbers caused by the profiler itself.

### F-185 — `PerformanceStats` calls `Process.GetCurrentProcess()` every render frame the perf-stats window is in non-minimum mode

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/PerformanceStats.cs:73-78`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Lines 73-78:
  ```csharp
  using (var proc = Process.GetCurrentProcess()) {
      ImGui.Text($"Total Used Memory: {proc.PrivateMemorySize64 / (1024 * 1024)} (MB)");
  }
  ```
  Inside the per-frame render loop. `Process.GetCurrentProcess()` allocates a fresh `Process` wrapper (which holds an OS handle internally), reads the process info. The `using` Dispose closes the handle. At 144 Hz with non-minimum perf stats visible: 144 Process objects allocated and disposed per second.
- **Why it's a bug:** `PrivateMemorySize64` only changes meaningfully on the order of seconds (memory allocations and GCs aren't visible at frame granularity). Reading it every frame is wasteful — a once-per-second cache would lose nothing user-visible. The `Process.GetCurrentProcess()` call is documented as relatively cheap, but it does allocate a Process object and trigger an internal `Refresh()`-equivalent.
- **Suggested fix:** Cache the value with a Stopwatch:
  ```csharp
  private static readonly Stopwatch memCacheSw = Stopwatch.StartNew();
  private static long cachedPrivateBytesMb;
  // in render loop:
  if (memCacheSw.ElapsedMilliseconds > 1000) {
      memCacheSw.Restart();
      using var proc = Process.GetCurrentProcess();
      cachedPrivateBytesMb = proc.PrivateMemorySize64 / (1024 * 1024);
  }
  ImGui.Text($"Total Used Memory: {cachedPrivateBytesMb} (MB)");
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Per-frame OS-handle allocation when perf stats window is in non-minimum mode; minor.

### F-050 — `ImGuiHelper.Color(Vector4)` casts truncate instead of rounding

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/ImGuiHelper.cs:66-70`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops (correctness corollary)
- **Description:** `color *= 255f; return ((uint)color.W << 24) | ((uint)color.Z << 16) | ((uint)color.Y << 8) | (uint)color.X;`. Casting `float` to `uint` truncates toward zero; e.g., `0.5f * 255 = 127.5 → cast → 127`, but `Math.Round(127.5) = 128`. The error per channel is up to 0.5/255 ≈ 0.2%.
- **Why it's a bug:** Conversion isn't symmetric with `Color(uint)` (line 77-88) which divides by `255f` exactly. Round-tripping a Vector4 through `Color(Vector4) → Color(uint) → Vector4` loses up to 0.5/255 per channel due to the truncation. Visually imperceptible.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace each `(uint)color.X` with `(uint)MathF.Round(color.X)` (and clamp to `[0, 255]` if the source could over/undershoot). Negligible perf cost.
- **Risk if left:** None practically; minor color drift if anyone round-trips colors.

### F-162 — `SettingsWindow.RenderCoroutine` allocates `new Vector2(800, 600)` and `Vector2.One * float.MaxValue` per frame

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/SettingsWindow.cs:697`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Performance in hot loops
- **Description:** Line 697: `ImGui.SetNextWindowSizeConstraints(new Vector2(800, 600), Vector2.One * float.MaxValue);`. `Vector2` is a `struct`, so allocation is on the stack — but `Vector2.One * float.MaxValue` creates an intermediate `Vector2` via the operator. The whole expression runs every frame the settings window is visible.
- **Why it's a bug:** Negligible allocation cost (struct, zero heap). However, the values are constants that could be cached as `private static readonly Vector2 SizeMin = new(800, 600);` and `private static readonly Vector2 SizeMax = Vector2.One * float.MaxValue;`. Eliminates the per-frame operator call and improves readability.
- **Suggested fix:** Hoist into static readonly fields. Same shape as F-051's caching guidance.
- **Risk if left:** Cosmetic; no measurable cost.


### API misuse

### F-003 — `static readonly Dictionary` is mutable

- **File:** `GameOffsets/GameProcessName.cs:12-19`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `public static readonly Dictionary<string, string> ProcessName = new() { ... }`. The reference is `readonly`, but the dictionary contents are not — anyone with a reference can `ProcessName["foo"] = "bar"`, mutating shared state.
- **Why it's a bug:** This collection is read every 2 seconds inside `GameProcess.FindAndOpen()` from a worker coroutine. A buggy plugin or future refactor that mutates it would race the reader and silently change scanning behavior.
- **Suggested fix:** Expose as `IReadOnlyDictionary<string, string>` (or `FrozenDictionary<,>` in .NET 8+) and keep the mutable `Dictionary` private.
- **Risk if left:** Latent multi-threaded mutation hazard; no live bug today.

### F-009 — `static readonly Pattern[]` array is mutable

- **File:** `GameOffsets/StaticOffsetsPatterns.cs:8-105`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `public static readonly Pattern[] Patterns = { ... };`. `readonly` on an array reference does not prevent element-level mutation. `Patterns[0] = new Pattern("evil", "00", 0)` is legal from any caller.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-003. The array is consumed by `PatternFinder` during process-attach scanning. A plugin or test could clobber slot data.
- **Suggested fix:** Expose as `ImmutableArray<Pattern>` or `IReadOnlyList<Pattern>`. Keep the storage private.
- **Risk if left:** Latent tampering hazard; no live bug today.

### F-017 — `LoadedFilesRootObject.TotalCount` is mutable `public static int`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/LoadedFilesOffset.cs:8-12`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `public struct LoadedFilesRootObject { public StdBucket LoadedFiles; public static int TotalCount = 0x10; }`. The static field has no `readonly` modifier and no `const` keyword, so any caller can write `LoadedFilesRootObject.TotalCount = 0;` from anywhere.
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-003 and F-009 — public mutable shared state. The value is read inside `GetAllPointers()` (`GameHelper/RemoteObjects/LoadedFiles.cs:141`) on every area change to size a `ReadMemoryArray<LoadedFilesRootObject>` call. A buggy plugin or test that clobbers `TotalCount` to `0` would silently disable file scanning (preloaded-file detection used to identify boss arenas etc.); a value larger than the native array would over-read past the array bounds, producing garbage `StdBucket`s with attacker-controlled pointers (then used in `ScanForFilesParallel` as `IntPtr` dereferences).
- **Suggested fix:** Convert to `public const int TotalCount = 0x10;` (preferred — compile-time constant, no possibility of mutation) or `public static readonly int TotalCount = 0x10;`.
- **Risk if left:** Latent tampering hazard. `const` would be a one-line zero-risk fix.

### F-025 — Public static mutable `Func` fields across helper classes — extension of F-011

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/EntityOffsets.cs:29-31` (`EntityHelper.IsValidEntity`, `IsFriendly`), `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:38-44` (`EntityFilter.IgnoreVisualsAndDecorations`), `GameOffsets/Objects/UiElement/UiElementBaseOffset.cs:49-57` (`UiElementBaseFuncs.IsVisibleChecker`, `ShouldModifyPos`)
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Same defect pattern as F-011 (`Util.isBitSetByte`/`isBitSetUint`). Each of these is a `public static Func<...>` field initialized inline; none are `readonly` or `const`, so any caller can reassign them globally, changing entity-validity, friendliness, network-bubble filtering, and UI visibility checks process-wide. These five funcs fire on every entity/UI element on every frame (the host calls `EntityHelper.IsValidEntity` per entity in `AddOrGetExisting` per area-update; `UiElementBaseFuncs.IsVisibleChecker` is called per UI element in `UiElementBase.IsVisible` per render frame).
- **Why it's a bug:** Same family as F-011 — tampering hazard plus an unnecessary delegate-invoke indirection on a hot path.
- **Suggested fix:** Convert each to a `public static bool IsXxx(...)` method, or at minimum mark the field `readonly`. Method form also restores standard PascalCase naming.
- **Risk if left:** Latent tampering; minor per-call perf cost (delegate invoke vs. direct method call) on every-frame hot paths.

### F-026 — Public static mutable fields that should be `const` or `readonly` — extension of F-017

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:128` (`TerrainStruct.TileHeightFinalMultiplier`), `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:141-142` (`TileStructure.TileToGridConversion`, `TileToWorldConversion`), `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/ImportantUiElementsOffsets.cs:31` (`PassiveSkillTreeStruct.ChildNumber`)
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Same defect family as F-017. Four `public static` fields without `readonly`/`const` modifier:
  - `TerrainStruct.TileHeightFinalMultiplier = 7.8125f;` — used in walkable-grid height conversions
  - `TileStructure.TileToGridConversion = 0x17;` — terrain tile-to-grid coordinate conversion
  - `TileStructure.TileToWorldConversion = 250f;` — terrain tile-to-world coordinate conversion
  - `PassiveSkillTreeStruct.ChildNumber = (3 - 1) * 0x08;` — passive-tree UI traversal offset
- **Why it's a bug:** Public mutable shared state. Anyone can reassign these from anywhere, silently breaking terrain reads (radar walkability) or passive-tree node traversal. Only `int`/`float` constants — perfect candidates for `const`. The expression `(3 - 1) * 0x08` is constant-foldable so `const int ChildNumber = 0x10;` works.
- **Suggested fix:** Convert each to `public const`. For the `float` (`TileHeightFinalMultiplier`, `TileToWorldConversion`), `const float` is allowed.
- **Risk if left:** Latent tampering hazard; same shape as F-017.

### F-048 — `GameHelperEvents.PostPerFrameDataUpdate` is mutable (no `readonly`) — extension of F-017 in host code

- **File:** `GameHelper/CoroutineEvents/GameHelperEvents.cs:59`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** All other events in this file are `public/internal static readonly Event` — `OnMoved`, `OnForegroundChanged`, `OnClose`, `PerFrameDataUpdate`, `OnRender`, `OnPostRender`, `OnOpened`, `TimeToSaveAllSettings`. `PostPerFrameDataUpdate` (line 59) is `internal static Event` (no `readonly`).
- **Why it's a bug:** Same defect family as F-017 / F-026 — public mutable shared state. Anyone with `internal` access can do `GameHelperEvents.PostPerFrameDataUpdate = new();`, which would orphan all coroutines that yielded on the original Event (they would never fire again). Also breaks the symmetry with the rest of the file — clearly an oversight.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `readonly`: `internal static readonly Event PostPerFrameDataUpdate = new();`.
- **Risk if left:** Same shape as F-017. One-line zero-risk fix.

### F-066 — `Core.cs:166` `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(property.Value, null)` masks a contract violation; `?.` should be `!`

- **File:** `GameHelper/Core.cs:166`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `RemoteObjectsToImGuiCollapsingHeader` calls `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(property.Value, null)`. `RemoteObjectPropertyDetail.ToImGui` is filled by `RemoteObjectBase.GetToImGuiMethods` (`RemoteObjectBase.cs:177`), which only yields properties whose runtime type derives from `RemoteObjectBase` (line 168 filter). `RemoteObjectBase` declares an `internal virtual void ToImGui()` (line 105). Therefore *every* property yielded by `GetToImGuiMethods` is guaranteed to have a `ToImGui` method — the only way `GetMethod("ToImGui", methodFlags)` returns `null` is a contract violation (e.g. a derived class that hides `ToImGui` with a different signature, or a runtime where `RemoteObjectBase.ToImGui` was reflection-stripped).
- **Why it's a bug:** The Phase 1 reviewer flagged this site explicitly. `?.` masks the contract violation: when ToImGui is null, the call silently does nothing and the user sees an empty CollapsingHeader with no diagnostic. The correct annotation is `property.ToImGui!.Invoke(...)` — preserving the NRE so the contract violation crashes loudly during dev rather than silently producing no output.
  
  Same pattern at `RemoteObjectBase.cs:114` (out of scope for this task, see Task 13) — both sites should use `!`.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(...)` with `property.ToImGui!.Invoke(...)`. Optionally tighten `RemoteObjectPropertyDetail.ToImGui` to a non-nullable `MethodInfo` so the type system prevents the regression.
- **Risk if left:** Today: zero, because the contract holds. Future: a derived type that diverges from the base ToImGui signature silently disappears from the debug widget instead of crashing during testing.

### F-069 — `MiscHelper.GenerateRandomString` allocates a fresh `new Random()` per call; output is the overlay window title — predictability + low entropy

- **File:** `GameHelper/Utils/MiscHelper.cs:80-100`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Used at `Program.cs:29` as the overlay window title. The character pool is `"qwertyuiopasdfghjklzxcvbnm" + "eioadfc"` (33 chars, weighted toward vowels). Each "word" is `[A-Z][a-z]{4-9}`, joined by space, 1-3 words total. Total entropy: roughly `log2(33) * (avg 7 chars * 2 words) ≈ 70 bits` per call. *However*: `new Random()` with no seed in .NET 6+ uses a thread-static `Random.Shared` seed, which is itself derived from a per-thread state seeded with the wall-clock at thread start. Two GameHelper instances launched within the same millisecond on the same machine can share a seed. (.NET 5 and earlier: time-of-day seed at ms granularity — worse.)
- **Why it's a bug:** The window title is presumably randomised to avoid trivial detection by signature scanners (other tools / overlays / streamers' OBS profiles). For that purpose:
  1. Predictable seeding under .NET 6+ is mostly fine because each `new Random()` instance is reseeded uniquely per call from the thread-static, but the surface should be `Random.Shared` directly to make this guarantee explicit.
  2. The character pool is small; with only 33 chars and a vowel bias, automated string-similarity scanners can identify "looks like GameHelper title" trivially.
  3. The function name `GenerateRandomString` makes the predictability concern invisible to reviewers — its only caller depends on it for adversarial-environment unpredictability.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `Random.Shared` (.NET 6+ thread-safe shared instance) instead of `new Random()`. For the window-title use case, prefer `RandomNumberGenerator.GetString(...)` (cryptographically strong) — overkill but safer signaling. At minimum, document the call site in `Program.cs` so reviewers know the entropy expectation.
- **Risk if left:** Marginal — title still varies per launch. Adversarial-detection robustness is weaker than implied by the function name.

### F-086 — `PCore<TSettings>.DllDirectory` and `.Settings` are public mutable fields, not properties — violates encapsulation; external mutation possible

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PCore.cs:11-22`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `public string DllDirectory = null!;` and `public TSettings Settings = new();` are public fields. Any external code holding a `PCore<...>` reference can write to them. The `null!` initialiser hides that the field is required to be set via `SetPluginDllLocation` before use; external write breaks that invariant.
- **Why it's a bug:** Three issues. (a) Public fields cannot be made virtual or interface members — if `IPCore` later wants `string DllDirectory { get; }` as a contract, the existing fields can't fulfil it without a breaking change. (b) Public fields skip property-style invariants — no setter validation, no `OnDllDirectoryChanged` hook. (c) The convention in the rest of the codebase (e.g., `State.cs`, `Core.cs`) is to use properties with `{ get; set; }` or readonly fields; PCore departs from this without reason.
- **Suggested fix:** `public string DllDirectory { get; private set; } = null!;` and `public TSettings Settings { get; protected set; } = new();`. Change `SetPluginDllLocation` to assign via the private setter. Plugin authors that already write `this.Settings = new();` in OnEnable would need `protected set` to keep working — `protected` is correct since `PCore` is the contract owner.
- **Risk if left:** Encapsulation hole. External `Plugins[i].Plugin.DllDirectory = "garbage"` is legal C# today. Cosmetic but inconsistent with the rest of the codebase.

### F-087 — `IPCore` defines no lifecycle hook for game close, render-loop teardown, or `IDisposable` — plugins cannot reliably release native resources

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/IPCore.cs:10-50`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** The interface declares `SetPluginDllLocation`, `OnEnable(bool isGameOpened)`, `OnDisable`, `DrawSettings`, `DrawUI`, `SaveSettings`. There is no `OnGameClose`, no `OnGameOpen`, no `OnDispose`/`IDisposable`. The host fires `GameHelperEvents.OnClose` and `OnOpened` on `Core.Process` events, but plugins receive only an `OnEnable(bool isGameOpened)` once at enable time — they have to subscribe to events themselves to track game lifecycle.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two consequences. (a) When the host shuts down, there's no signal to the plugin that it should flush state or release native resources (D3D textures, file handles, native threads). The host's `Plugins.ForEach(SaveSettings)` is the only fan-out, and it's only triggered by `TimeToSaveAllSettings` — not by genuine shutdown. If the host process is killed without that event firing, plugins lose work. (b) Plugins must independently subscribe to `Core.Process.OnClose`/`OnOpened` to react to game launch/exit, leading to event-handler boilerplate replicated across every plugin.
- **Suggested fix:** Extend `IPCore` with optional virtual/default-implemented members (default-interface-method support in C# 8+):
  ```csharp
  public virtual void OnGameOpen() { }
  public virtual void OnGameClose() { }
  public virtual void OnHostShutdown() { }
  ```
  Wire `PManager` to fan these out from `GameHelperEvents.OnOpened`/`OnClose` and host shutdown. Optionally inherit `IDisposable` and have the host call `Dispose` during unload.
- **Risk if left:** Plugin authors forget to subscribe to game-close events, leak native resources, or flush settings only on the next periodic save (which may not happen if the user immediately Alt+F4s the host). Lifecycle coupling is replicated across every plugin.

### F-092 — `RemoteObjectBase.cs:114` `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(...)` masks contract violation; `?.` should be `!`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:112-117`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Inside the `foreach (var property in properties)` loop, the call site is `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(property.Value, null);`. The `properties` enumerable is produced by `GetToImGuiMethods` (line 144-180) which only yields `RemoteObjectPropertyDetail` for property values whose runtime type is assignable to `RemoteObjectBase` (line 168 filter) and reflects `propertyType.GetMethod("ToImGui", methodFlags)` (line 177). `RemoteObjectBase` declares `internal virtual void ToImGui()` (line 105), so every type that survives the filter has a `ToImGui` method. `GetMethod` therefore can return `null` only on a contract violation (e.g., a derived class hides `ToImGui` with a different signature, or the runtime aggressively trims metadata).
- **Why it's a bug:** The Phase 1 reviewer explicitly flagged this site (paired with the F-066 site at `Core.cs:166`). `?.` masks the contract violation: when `ToImGui` is null, the call silently does nothing — the user sees an empty TreeNode tree with no diagnostic. The correct annotation is `property.ToImGui!.Invoke(...)`, which preserves the NRE so the contract violation crashes loudly during dev rather than silently producing no output. Same pattern as F-066, just at the instance call site instead of the static call site.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `property.ToImGui?.Invoke(property.Value, null);` with `property.ToImGui!.Invoke(property.Value, null);`. Optionally tighten `RemoteObjectPropertyDetail.ToImGui` to non-nullable `MethodInfo` so the type system prevents the regression. The two sites (here + `Core.cs:166`) should change in lockstep.
- **Risk if left:** Today: zero, because the contract holds. Future: a derived type that diverges from the base `ToImGui` signature silently disappears from every debug widget instead of crashing during testing. The bug surfaces only as "the debug tree is missing entries", with no log to chase.

### F-093 — `RemoteObjectBase` parameterless constructor throws `NotImplementedException` — dead code with no diagnostic value

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/RemoteObjectBase.cs:29-32`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `internal RemoteObjectBase() { throw new NotImplementedException(); }`. The class is `abstract`, so the only consumers are derived classes' constructors. No derived class chains `: base()` (verified — the only invocation site shape is `: base(address, ...)` from each remote object class). The parameterless ctor is dead code that exists only to throw.
- **Why it's a bug:** The pattern looks like an attempt to "ban" the parameterless ctor, but C# offers cleaner ways: omit the parameterless ctor entirely (it isn't auto-generated for classes with another ctor; though for `abstract` classes a parameterless ctor IS auto-generated for derived chaining), or mark it `private`. Throwing `NotImplementedException` at runtime delays the failure to the moment any future caller chains `: base()`, with a misleading exception name (it's not "not implemented", it's "intentionally banned"). A `private` ctor would produce a compile-time error with a clear diagnostic.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) delete the parameterless ctor entirely — derived classes will be forced to chain to `RemoteObjectBase(IntPtr, bool, bool)`, or (b) make it `private` if some inheritance edge case requires it to exist, or (c) throw `InvalidOperationException("Use RemoteObjectBase(IntPtr address, ...) instead.")` with a useful message. Option (a) is the minimum-risk change.
- **Risk if left:** A future derived class that accidentally chains `: base()` (or omits chaining and triggers the implicit base call) crashes at construction with an exception name that misrepresents the cause.

### F-121 — `MinimapIcon` performs ad-hoc offset arithmetic (`Address + 0x20`) instead of using a typed offset struct

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs:62-72`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Every other component in this batch reads memory through a typed struct in `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/` (e.g., `BuffsOffsets`, `LifeOffset`, `ChestOffsets`). `MinimapIcon` has no corresponding offset struct in `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/`. The `UpdateData` method (lines 62-74) reads via raw arithmetic: `reader.ReadMemory<IntPtr>(this.Address + 0x20);` and a chained dereference. Two magic numbers: `0x20` (the offset) and `0x10000` (the "valid pointer" sentinel at line 65/68).
- **Why it's a bug:** Inconsistent with the codebase convention. Future GameOffsets refresh via the IDA Pro / Cheat Engine offset finder (`tools/UPDATE_OFFSETS_IDA.md`) regenerates typed structs for all components — `MinimapIcon` would be missed. The `0x10000` "valid pointer" check is also not idiomatic — `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadMemory` already gates on `addr <= 0 || addr > MaxUserModeAddress`. The custom guard is duplicative and the constant is undocumented (probably "below this is null page / kernel descriptor").
- **Suggested fix:** Add `MinimapIconOffsets` struct in `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/MinimapIcon.cs`:
  ```csharp
  [StructLayout(LayoutKind.Explicit, Pack = 1)]
  public struct MinimapIconOffsets {
      [FieldOffset(0x00)] public ComponentHeader Header;
      [FieldOffset(0x20)] public IntPtr DatRowPtr; // -> +0x00 -> UTF-16 string
  }
  ```
  Then `MinimapIcon.UpdateData` becomes consistent with the rest:
  ```csharp
  var data = reader.ReadMemory<MinimapIconOffsets>(this.Address);
  this.OwnerEntityAddress = data.Header.EntityPtr;
  this.IconName = null;
  if (data.DatRowPtr == IntPtr.Zero) return;
  var namePtr = reader.ReadMemory<IntPtr>(data.DatRowPtr);
  if (namePtr == IntPtr.Zero) return;
  this.IconName = reader.ReadUnicodeString(namePtr);
  ```
  This also subsumes F-114 (drop empty catches), F-117 (reset to null), F-122 (use ReadUnicodeString primitive).
- **Risk if left:** Future offset refreshes don't touch `MinimapIcon`; field offset drifts undetected. Codebase convention violated.

### F-127 — Component public mutable fields (`Stats.StatsChangedByItems`, `ObjectMagicProperties.Mods`/`ModNames`/`ModStats`) — encapsulation hole + invites unsynchronized iteration

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Stats.cs:22, 27, 32, 37`, `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ObjectMagicProperties.cs:38, 43, 48`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Both classes expose collections as public mutable fields (not properties):
  - `Stats.StatsChangedByItems`, `StatsChangedByBuffAndActions` (Dictionary fields, line 22 and 27)
  - `Stats.CurrentWeaponIndex`, `IsInShapeshiftedForm` (primitive fields, line 32 and 37)
  - `ObjectMagicProperties.Mods` (List field, line 38), `ModNames` (HashSet, line 43), `ModStats` (Dictionary, line 48)
  
  Same defect family as F-086 (`PCore<TSettings>.DllDirectory` and `Settings`). External code can replace the entire collection (`actor.Mods = null;`) or iterate without lock (the `StatUpdator` pattern locks the dictionary; an external caller iterating `actor.StatsChangedByItems` directly does not).
- **Why it's a bug:** Three issues. (a) Public fields cannot be made virtual or interface members. (b) External replacement breaks the lock invariant — `StatUpdator` locks on `stats` (the parameter alias), but if a third party reassigns `actor.StatsChangedByItems = new();`, an in-flight `StatUpdator` is locked on the old reference and the writer is locked on the new one — same key, different locks → race. (c) Convention in the rest of the codebase is `{ get; private set; }` properties for collections; the components depart without reason.
- **Suggested fix:** Convert each field to a `{ get; }` auto-property: `public Dictionary<GameStats, int> StatsChangedByItems { get; } = new();`. The collection contents remain mutable (lock-protected via `StatUpdator`); the reference itself becomes immutable. Same for `Mods`, `ModNames`, `ModStats`.
- **Risk if left:** Encapsulation hole. External `comp.Mods = null` is legal C# today and would crash subsequent reads. No live consumer does this — but the pattern is fragile.

### F-141 — `AreaInstance.UpdateEntities` calls `data.TryRemove(kv.Key, out _)` inside `Parallel.ForEach(data, ...)` enumeration of the same dictionary

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/AreaInstance.cs:284-325`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Lines 284-325: `Parallel.ForEach(data, (kv) => { ... if (shouldRemove) data.TryRemove(kv.Key, out _); ... });`. `data` is a `ConcurrentDictionary<EntityNodeKey, Entity>`. The `Parallel.ForEach(IEnumerable, ...)` overload uses `data`'s default enumerator, which for `ConcurrentDictionary` returns a moment-in-time snapshot — *enumeration is documented as safe even with concurrent mutation*. So `TryRemove` while enumerating is technically allowed.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — `ConcurrentDictionary.TryRemove` while enumerating is officially safe. But the pattern is fragile because:
  1. The enumerator's snapshot semantics differ from `Dictionary<K,V>` (which throws `InvalidOperationException` on mutation-during-enumeration), so future refactors that swap to a non-concurrent collection will introduce a hard crash.
  2. The same `data` dictionary is also mutated by `kv.Value.Address = value.EntityPtr;` (line 336) inside the `ReadStdMap` callback at line 327-357 — which runs *concurrently with* the `Parallel.ForEach` since the two operations are queued on the same `data` reference and the second one fires after the first kicks off. The interaction depends on subtle scheduling: today `Parallel.ForEach` blocks until done, so by the time `ReadStdMap` starts, the iteration is complete. But this requires reading the source carefully — a future async-ification or task-pipelined refactor would race.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) collect keys-to-remove into a local `ConcurrentBag<EntityNodeKey>` during the parallel iteration, then remove them after the iteration completes; (b) document the concurrent-enumerate-and-mutate dependency in the source comment so future maintainers know not to swap the collection type. Option (a) decouples and is more robust against refactors.
- **Risk if left:** Future refactor that swaps to `Dictionary<K,V>` or async-iterates triggers a hard crash. Today: zero impact, because `ConcurrentDictionary` officially supports it.

### F-148 — `InGameState.UpdateData` mutates `Core.GHSettings.EnableControllerMode` from a data-read path

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameState.cs:75-83`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Lines 75-83:
  ```csharp
  if (uiRootStruct.GameUiPtr == IntPtr.Zero) {
      Core.GHSettings.EnableControllerMode = true;
      this.GameUi.Address = uiRootStruct.GameUiControllerPtr;
  } else {
      Core.GHSettings.EnableControllerMode = false;
      this.GameUi.Address = uiRootStruct.GameUiPtr;
  }
  ```
  `Core.GHSettings.EnableControllerMode` is a settings field (intended to be user-toggleable in the Settings window). Writing to it from `UpdateData` (a data-read coroutine fired per-frame) overrides the user's choice every frame based on the in-game state — and means the settings "Save" button never sees a stable value to write.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two issues. (a) The settings file's `EnableControllerMode` value rotates every frame depending on whether PoE has GameUiPtr or GameUiControllerPtr set. The user can never persist a preference; the next launch re-reads game state and overrides. (b) The naming `EnableControllerMode` implies user intent ("I want controller mode"), but the actual semantic is "is the game currently using controller mode". Two different concepts conflated in one field.
  
  The right model: a read-only `IsControllerMode` exposed on `InGameState`/`Core.States` for the data-driven case, and a separate `EnableControllerModeOverride` setting for explicit user intent. The current code merges them into one mutable settings field.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) remove the writes and add a read-only computed property: `public bool IsControllerMode { get; private set; }` updated alongside the GameUi address; (b) leave `EnableControllerMode` as a true user setting and consume it instead of the auto-detected value; (c) split into two fields. Option (a) is the smallest change.
- **Risk if left:** User cannot persist a controller-mode preference; settings file reflects last-frame state, not user intent.

### F-167 — `State.SpecialMiscObjPaths` and `MonstersPathsToIgnore` field initializers carry default entries that the deserializer always overwrites — once cleared, defaults are gone forever

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/State.cs:209-223`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Lines 209-214 declare `SpecialMiscObjPaths` with three default entries (Expedition markers/relic and ExpeditionRelic terrain). Lines 220-223 declare `MonstersPathsToIgnore` with one default ("VaalTrainingDummy"). These initializers run only when the *field initializer* fires — i.e., on a fresh `State()` instance. Newtonsoft.Json deserialization, when populating an existing instance, *replaces* `List<T>` fields with the deserialized list (or, depending on `ObjectCreationHandling`, *appends to it* — but the default behavior is replace).
  
  Effect: First launch creates `core_settings.json` with the three Expedition entries (from the initializer). User opens the GUI, clicks "Delete" on each entry (using F-158's RemoveAt-in-for, but functionally still Delete works), and the JSON is saved with an empty list. Next launch deserializes `[]` into `SpecialMiscObjPaths`, the field initializer never runs (constructor invoked with `JsonConstructorAttribute`-equivalent), and the user's "deleted" defaults are now permanently gone unless they manually delete `core_settings.json` to reset.
- **Why it's a bug:** No mechanism to "restore defaults" in the UI. Power users may want to remove a default they don't care about (e.g., user doesn't run Expedition), but if they later change their mind, there's no UI button — they must edit JSON or wipe config. Not strictly a bug since explicit user-deletion is honored, but the semantics are surprising.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a "Restore defaults" button next to each list (in `DrawMonstersToIgnore` and `DrawMiscObjWidget`) that resets the list to the field initializer's default. Or store defaults in a separate readonly field and merge them in on load if missing.
- **Risk if left:** Mild user friction; no data loss.

### F-168 — `State` exposes ~40 public mutable fields — no encapsulation, no per-write change notification, every UI field can be mutated without triggering the save coroutine

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/State.cs:42-252`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** The class declares ~40 public fields with no `set` accessor (since they're fields, not properties). Every UI mutation in `SettingsWindow.cs` writes directly to e.g. `Core.GHSettings.Vsync`, `Core.GHSettings.FPSLimit`, `Core.GHSettings.HidePerfStatsWhenBg`. The save coroutine fires only on `TimeToSaveAllSettings` event (raised when settings window hides via F12, or on `IsOverlayRunning = false`). Between hide-events, all in-flight changes are unsaved — a process crash drops them.
  
  Same encapsulation-hole concern as F-127 (`Stats.StatsChangedByItems` etc. are public mutable fields) but applied to the settings layer. Specifically:
  - No invariants are enforced on assignment (e.g., `FPSLimit = -5` is accepted; `KeyPressTimeout = -1` ignored at-set, only validated by UI clamps).
  - No PropertyChanged notification, so a feature wanting to react to a setting change (e.g., "FPSLimit changed → tell `Core.Overlay`") must poll, not subscribe.
  - External code (plugins) can mutate any setting without going through a single chokepoint.
- **Why it's a bug:** Combined with F-159 (sync save on render thread), F-039 (non-atomic save), F-167 (cleared-defaults loss), and F-058 (no top-level try/catch), the settings layer has compound failure modes: a render-thread crash mid-frame → unsaved changes lost; a plugin sets `FPSLimit = 0` → save fires only at next hide, and meanwhile `Core.Overlay.FPSLimit = 0` is propagated.
- **Suggested fix:** Convert fields to properties with validation and per-set save trigger (debounced). Or wrap settings in a transactional `SaveOnChange` proxy. At minimum, validate ranges in setters: `set { _fpsLimit = Math.Max(0, value); }`.
- **Risk if left:** Settings can be in an invalid state for arbitrarily long. Crash mid-edit loses all changes. No reactive notification for cross-cutting setting changes.

### F-047 — `UiElementParents.AddIfNotExists` has empty `if` block on line 53 — confusing control flow

- **File:** `GameHelper/Cache/UiElementParents.cs:51-72`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse (code quality)
- **Description:** The control flow reads:
  ```csharp
  if (this.grandparent != null && this.grandparent.cache.ContainsKey(address))
  {
      // empty
  }
  else
  {
      lock (this.cache) { ... add ... }
  }
  ```
  The "if exists in grandparent, do nothing" branch is empty. The `else` does the actual work.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not, but it inverts the natural reading of the code. Standard pattern is early-return: `if (grandparent?.cache.ContainsKey(address) == true) return; lock (this.cache) { ... }`.
- **Suggested fix:** Invert with `return`. Also see F-044 for the lock concern.
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic, but contributes to reviewer confusion that obscures F-044.

### F-063 — `GameProcess.Address` has an empty `private set { }` — confusing dead code

- **File:** `GameHelper/GameProcess.cs:74-95`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse (code quality)
- **Description:** The `Address` property has a getter that computes the base address from `Information.MainModule?.BaseAddress` and a `private set { }` with an empty body (line 94). The setter is unreachable from outside the class, and even from inside it's a no-op.
- **Why it's a bug:** Dead code that misleads readers. A reviewer might assume the setter caches the address; it does not. The property is effectively read-only — make it so.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop `private set { }`. Use `internal IntPtr Address { get { ... } }`.
- **Risk if left:** Reader confusion; the getter recomputes from `Information.MainModule` on every call, producing minor allocation churn (Process.MainModule probes loaded modules), but that's already the case regardless of the empty setter.

### F-072 — `Core` is `static class`; testability and lifecycle footgun

- **File:** `GameHelper/Core.cs:25`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse (architecture)
- **Description:** `Core` is `public static class` with public static properties initialised inline (`Process { get; } = new()`, `States { get; } = new(IntPtr.Zero)`, etc.). This couples every consumer in the codebase to a single global instance, makes unit-testing impossible without process attach, and makes "two simultaneous game attach" or "test harness" workflows undoable. The static singleton design is the upstream pattern — not a bug — but it's worth noting because it locks the architecture.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not, but four consequences cascade through the audit:
  1. F-061's `Environment.Exit` skips `Core.Dispose` because the static singleton has no destructor; the `using` on `Overlay` (single instance) is the only Dispose hook.
  2. F-070's `version = null!` exists because static-class initialization order is fragile — `Initialize()` is the dependency-injected lifecycle hook.
  3. F-049 (existing): caches like `GgpkAddresses` only work *because* they are accessed via the static singleton — if they were instance, the eternal coroutines they start would leak.
  4. Plugins access `Core.Process.Handle` directly, with no abstraction — refactoring requires touching every plugin.
- **Suggested fix:** Out of scope for the .NET migration. Note in audit and leave for future architectural work.
- **Risk if left:** Architectural debt; not actionable here.

### F-089 — `PManager.UnloadPlugin` (DEBUG) calls `Plugins.Remove(plugin)` inside `foreach (var plugin in Plugins)` — works only because of immediate `return true`; brittle

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:75-89`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** The loop is:
  ```csharp
  foreach (var plugin in Plugins)
  {
      if (plugin.Name == name)
      {
          plugin.Plugin.SaveSettings();
          plugin.Plugin.OnDisable();
          Plugins.Remove(plugin);
          return true;
      }
  }
  ```
  `List<T>.Remove` mutates the list during enumeration, which would normally throw `InvalidOperationException` from the next `MoveNext`. The code escapes the bug only because `return true;` exits the foreach immediately, before the enumerator's invariant is rechecked.
- **Why it's a bug:** A future maintainer who adds a "remove all matching" or post-remove cleanup line below `Plugins.Remove(plugin)` (and removes the `return`) would silently introduce `InvalidOperationException`. The pattern is brittle; the right form is `var match = Plugins.FirstOrDefault(p => p.Name == name); if (match != null) { ... Plugins.Remove(match); return true; }`.
- **Suggested fix:** Refactor as above — find first, then remove, no enumerator involved. Or use `RemoveAll(p => p.Name == name) > 0`.
- **Risk if left:** Latent — works today, breaks the moment someone adds another statement after `Plugins.Remove`.

### F-091 — `Activator.CreateInstance(iPluginClasses[0])` requires a parameterless constructor; a plugin with a parameterized ctor fails with no targeted log

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:187-192`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `var pluginCore = Activator.CreateInstance(iPluginClasses[0]) as IPCore;`. This calls the parameterless constructor. If the plugin author declares only a parameterized ctor (e.g., `public MyPlugin(string name) { ... }`), `Activator.CreateInstance` throws `MissingMethodException`, which is caught by the outer `catch (Exception e)` (line 197) and logged generically — no hint that the cause is "missing parameterless ctor".
- **Why it's a bug:** The contract "plugin must have a parameterless ctor" is implicit. Plugin authors with experience in DI frameworks may instinctively add a constructor parameter (e.g., `IServiceProvider`) and find their plugin silently fails to load. The generic `catch` exacerbates the diagnosis problem.
- **Suggested fix:** (a) Document the parameterless-ctor requirement on `PCore`/`IPCore`. (b) Add an explicit catch for `MissingMethodException` with a targeted message: `"Plugin {dir} class {className} requires a parameterless constructor"`. (c) Optionally support a constructor that takes `PluginContext` (mirror of how `IPlugin` works in the C++ host described in CLAUDE.md) to give plugins access to host services without static lookups.
- **Risk if left:** Plugin authors hit obscure load failures. Diagnosis-by-confusion.

### F-126 — `Stats.IsInShapeshiftedForm = data.ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr != 0x00` compares `IntPtr` to integer literal — should be `IntPtr.Zero`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/Stats.cs:63`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** `this.IsInShapeshiftedForm = data.ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr != 0x00;`. `ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr` is presumably an `IntPtr` (or `long` for the offset); comparing to integer literal `0x00` works due to implicit conversion (or operator overload on `IntPtr`), but is semantically odd. The standard idiom is `data.ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr != IntPtr.Zero` or, if it's `long`/`int`, use a typed zero literal.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but `0x00` is a value-equals-zero compare that masks the type. A reviewer can't tell from this line whether `ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr` is a pointer (where `IntPtr.Zero` is the right comparand) or an integer flag. Other components in this batch consistently use `IntPtr.Zero`: `Animated.cs:56` `data.AnimatedEntityPtr != IntPtr.Zero`, `Buffs.cs:74` `BuffDefinationPtr == IntPtr.Zero`, etc.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace with `data.ShapeshiftFormsRowPtr != IntPtr.Zero`. Verify the underlying field type in `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Stats.cs`. Codebase convention.
- **Risk if left:** Code-style inconsistency; reviewer confusion.

### F-128 — `ObjectMagicProperties.UpdateData` uses `_ = this.Mods.All(k => this.ModNames.Add(k.name))` for side-effect — abuse of LINQ predicate as iteration

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/Components/ObjectMagicProperties.cs:86`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Line 86: `_ = this.Mods.All(k => this.ModNames.Add(k.name));`. `Enumerable.All<T>` short-circuits on the first `false`. `HashSet<string>.Add` returns `false` if the item was already present. So `All` iterates until it finds a duplicate-name entry, then stops — *and the `_ = ` discards the result*. The intent is "for each mod, add its name to ModNames". The implementation is "add names to ModNames until you find a duplicate".
