- **Why it's a bug:** The intent and the behavior diverge for any case where a mod name already exists in ModNames (which combined with F-115's no-Clear behavior is *every* update after the first). After the first update, `ModNames` already contains all names from the previous update; the very first `Add` returns false; `All` stops. So new mod names from new mods are never added. Subtle data-correctness bug, not just style.
  
  Combined with F-115's no-Clear bug, the visible effect is: ModNames is the *union of names from all reroll events ever seen* but stops growing as soon as the first mod name repeats. After F-115 is fixed (Clear() before AddToMods), ModNames will be empty at the top of UpdateData; the `All` then iterates *all* mods and `Add` returns true for each, populating ModNames correctly — but only because F-115 was fixed. The current `All` pattern *depends on* the broken F-115 to mostly work.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace with explicit foreach: `foreach (var k in this.Mods) this.ModNames.Add(k.name);`. Or `this.ModNames.UnionWith(this.Mods.Select(k => k.name));`. Either makes the iteration intent explicit.
- **Risk if left:** Once F-115 is fixed, this line still subtly works because ModNames is cleared first. But the LINQ-as-side-effect pattern is fragile and a reviewer could rightly flag it.

### F-154 — `ServerData.OnTimeTick` is fully commented-out dead code

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/ServerData.cs:29-32, 140-150`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Lines 29-32 inside the constructor:
  ```csharp
  // Feel free to uncomment this if we ever add stuff like latency.
  //Core.CoroutinesRegistrar.Add(CoroutineHandler.Start(
  //    this.OnTimeTick(), "[ServerData] Update ServerData", int.MaxValue - 3));
  ```
  Plus the entire `OnTimeTick` method (lines 140-150) is defined but never invoked. `private IEnumerable<Wait> OnTimeTick() { while (true) { yield return new Wait(0.2d); if (this.Address != IntPtr.Zero) this.UpdateData(false); } }`.
- **Why it's a bug:** Dead code clutters the file and confuses readers. The method exists, looks like it should be called, but isn't. A reader investigating "why doesn't ServerData update?" reads `OnTimeTick`, assumes it runs, and is surprised. The `UpdateData` is called only via `RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter — i.e., when `AreaInstance.UpdateData` reassigns `this.ServerDataObject.Address = data.PlayerInfo.ServerDataPtr;` (line 236). On address-stable runs (no area change), `ServerData.UpdateData` doesn't fire. The commented-out coroutine *would* fix that if a use case arose.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) delete the commented coroutine and `OnTimeTick` method entirely — if a future need arises, reintroduce; or (b) uncomment it now if there's a known need for periodic updates. The current half-state is the worst option.
- **Risk if left:** Reader confusion. No runtime impact.

### F-155 — `ImportantUiElements.UpdateData` `Core.GHSettings.IsTaiwanClient ? this.Address - 0x08 : this.Address` undocumented magic offset

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/ImportantUiElements.cs:123`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Line 123: `var data1 = reader.ReadMemory<ImportantUiElementsOffsets>(Core.GHSettings.IsTaiwanClient ? this.Address - 0x08 : this.Address);`. The conditional offset `- 0x08` for the Taiwan client has no source comment explaining why or what game-build difference produces the 8-byte shift. A reader investigating Taiwan-client compatibility, or an offset-finder script regenerating offsets per league, has no clue what the 0x08 represents.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but offset comments are critical infrastructure, and "Taiwan client is shifted -8 bytes for ImportantUiElements only" is exactly the kind of fact that gets lost on engineer rotation. Other Taiwan-specific shifts in the codebase would benefit from being collected (probably in `ServerConfig.h`-equivalent or in a `TaiwanClientOffsets` helper class).
- **Suggested fix:** Add a comment explaining the 0x08 shift and link to the source (which league/build introduced it, what game struct difference produces it). Optionally extract to a constant: `private const int TaiwanClientShift = 0x08; // GameUI base shifted -8 bytes per [date/build]`.
- **Risk if left:** Future Taiwan-client breakage on game patch — the 0x08 may need to change. Without a comment, a maintainer doesn't know where to look.

### F-156 — `WorldData.WorldToScreen` has two near-identical overloads (3D-tuple, 2D) duplicating the entire matrix multiplication body

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/WorldData.cs:38-77, 85-115`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse (code quality)
- **Description:** Two overloads:
  - `WorldToScreen(StdTuple3D<float> worldPosition, float height)` (lines 47-77)
  - `WorldToScreen(Vector2 worldPosition, float height)` (lines 85-115)
  
  The bodies are byte-for-byte identical except for `temp0[0] = worldPosition.X; temp0[1] = worldPosition.Y` — the X and Y access. Everything else (matrix multiply, perspective divide, viewport mapping, rounding) is duplicated. Plus a third overload `WorldToScreen(StdTuple3D<float>)` (line 38-39) that delegates to the first.
- **Why it's a bug:** Code duplication is a maintenance hazard — F-148 fixes (per-frame allocation of `double[4]` arrays, see F-147 below) need to be applied in two places. The second overload was probably added without refactoring, copying the first.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract the common body into a private method:
  ```csharp
  private Vector2 WorldToScreenInternal(float wx, float wy, float height) {
      // ... common matrix math ...
  }
  public Vector2 WorldToScreen(StdTuple3D<float> p, float h) => WorldToScreenInternal(p.X, p.Y, h);
  public Vector2 WorldToScreen(Vector2 p, float h) => WorldToScreenInternal(p.X, p.Y, h);
  ```
  Eliminates ~30 lines of duplication.
- **Risk if left:** Future fixes diverge between the two overloads.

### F-157 — `ChatParentUiElement.IsChatActive` uses magic threshold `>= 0x8C` (140 / 255 ≈ 55% alpha) with no documentation of why that threshold means "active"

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/UiElement/ChatParentUiElement.cs:20`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Line 20: `public bool IsChatActive => this.backgroundColor.W * 255 >= 0x8C;`. The threshold `0x8C = 140` represents an alpha-channel value (the "is the chat box visible above ~55% opacity?" check). The constant has no comment explaining why 140 was chosen as the threshold — empirical observation of PoE's chat UI's alpha behavior, presumably. A future game patch that changes the chat-box alpha animation breaks this check silently.
  
  Also: `this.backgroundColor.W * 255 >= 0x8C` mixes float math (`* 255`) with an integer compare (`>= 140`). Conversion `float >= int` promotes the int to float, fine — but the float-compare is still one of the small set of "comparing floats with ==/>=" cases that could miss the boundary by one bit. If `backgroundColor.W` is read as `0x8B / 255.0f = 0.5490196f`, then `* 255 = 139.99999f`, then `>= 140f` is `false`. That's fine — but the inverse case `0x8C / 255.0f = 0.5529412f, * 255 = 141.00001f`, `>= 140f` is `true`. So the threshold effectively rounds to 0x8C (140), but an edge-case torn read of `W = 0x8C / 255.0f` exact could drift a bit either way.
- **Why it's a bug:** Magic threshold + no comment; latent failure on game patch. Float comparison fragility.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a comment: `// PoE chat box visible alpha threshold; chat is interactive when bg-alpha > ~55%. Verified empirically against [date/version].` Replace the float multiply with an int compare on the byte: `var alphaByte = (byte)(this.backgroundColor.W * 255 + 0.5f); return alphaByte >= 0x8C;` — eliminates the float-compare quirk.
- **Risk if left:** Threshold drift on game patch; subtle ChatActive state misreports. No live impact.

### F-170 — `GameUiExplorer` writes `current.Element.Address = current.Element.Address;` four times — intentional re-trigger of the `Address` setter masquerades as no-op self-assignment

- **File:** `GameHelper/Ui/GameUiExplorer.cs:147, 201, 257`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** API misuse
- **Description:** Three sites assign `Address` to itself:
  - Line 147: `current.Element.Address = current.Element.Address;`
  - Line 201: `child.Address = child.Address;`
  - Line 257: `child.Address = child.Address;`
  
  Per F-095 (`RemoteObjectBase.Address` setter holds `updateLock` for the entire `UpdateData` call) and the implementation at `RemoteObjectBase.cs`, the setter triggers a full re-read of the underlying memory. The self-assignment is a deliberate invocation of the side-effect: "re-read this UI element's data from memory so the values shown in this frame are fresh." But the syntax `x.Address = x.Address` looks indistinguishable from a pointless no-op; a reader (or a static-analysis tool) is likely to suggest deleting it as dead code.
- **Why it's a bug:** Future maintainer reads "x = x", deletes the line as a no-op, and silently breaks the UI element refresh — the explorer now displays stale data from the original `CreateUiElement` time. The behavior contract relies on a non-obvious side-effect of property assignment.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace each call with an explicit `current.Element.Refresh()` (or `current.Element.UpdateData(true)`) method. Document why the re-read is needed at this point in the render loop.
- **Risk if left:** Latent — a future refactor or static-analysis "dead code" suggestion deletes the lines and silently breaks the UI explorer. Cosmetic / maintainability.


### Coroutine semantics

### F-073 — `Core.Overlay = new GameOverlay(...)` happens before `Core.Initialize()` — `version` is null while overlay coroutines are starting

- **File:** `GameHelper/Program.cs:29`, `GameHelper/Core.cs:102-123, 137-146`, `GameHelper/GameOverlay.cs:24-50`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Coroutine semantics
- **Description:** Initialization sequence:
  1. `Program.Main` line 29: `Core.Overlay = new GameOverlay(MiscHelper.GenerateRandomString())`. This invokes the GameOverlay ctor, which:
     - Calls base `Overlay` ctor (allocates window).
     - Calls `CoroutineHandler.Start(this.UpdateOverlayBounds(), priority: int.MaxValue)`.
     - Calls `SettingsWindow.InitializeCoroutines()`, `PerformanceStats.InitializeCoroutines()`, etc. — eight sub-system coroutine bootstraps.
  2. `Program.Main` line 31: `await Core.Overlay.Run()`. `Run()` calls `Core.Initialize()` (sets `version`) then `Core.InitializeCororutines()` then `await base.Run()` (starts the render loop).
  
  Between steps (1) and (2), `Core.version` is `null`, but coroutines started in step (1) are running. Each `CoroutineHandler.Start` call schedules the coroutine, which then waits for its first event. The render loop hasn't started yet, so `Tick` isn't called and no coroutine has actually executed past its first `yield`. So in practice no coroutine reads `version` before it's set.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but the ordering is a load-bearing accident. A future refactor that:
  - Makes any subsystem `InitializeCoroutines` do work synchronously (e.g. read settings that contain version-dependent fields), OR
  - Moves the `Tick` startup earlier (e.g. a debug-mode warmup tick before `Run()`)
  
  ...will hit `Core.GetVersion()` returning `null.Trim()` → NRE. The current code happens to work because of cooperative-only coroutines plus pre-Tick startup ordering.
- **Suggested fix:** Move `Core.Initialize()` to *before* `new GameOverlay(...)`:
  ```csharp
  Core.Initialize();
  using (Core.Overlay = new GameOverlay(MiscHelper.GenerateRandomString()))
      await Core.Overlay.Run();
  ```
  And drop the `Core.Initialize()` call inside `GameOverlay.Run()` (or make it idempotent). This eliminates the ordering trap. Combined with F-070 (eager initialisation of `version`), the trap is fully closed.
- **Risk if left:** Latent ordering trap; one refactor away from a cryptic NRE at startup.


### Settings / IO

### F-084 — `PManager.LoadPluginMetadata` / `SavePluginMetadata` use `JsonHelper.SafeToFile` — non-atomic, no exception handling

- **Status:** ✅ Fixed in commit e2a91a3
- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PManager.cs:204-217, 227-230, 232-239`
- **Severity:** high
- **Category:** Settings / IO
- **Description:** Both methods funnel through `JsonHelper.CreateOrLoadJsonFile<Dictionary<string, PluginMetadata>>(State.PluginsMetadataFile)` (line 206) and `JsonHelper.SafeToFile(...)` (line 229). Per F-039 and F-040: `SafeToFile` is `File.WriteAllText` with no atomicity, and `CreateOrLoadJsonFile` has no exception handling around `JsonConvert.DeserializeObject`. The plugin metadata file `configs/plugins.json` is therefore at the same risk as core settings: a crash mid-write zeroes the file, and a corrupt file crashes startup.
- **Why it's a bug:** The save coroutine `SavePluginMetadataCoroutine` (line 232) writes on every `TimeToSaveAllSettings` event. The window for crash-during-write is wide. If the file is corrupted, the next launch fails inside `LoadPluginMetadata` → all plugin enable/disable state is lost (every plugin defaults to `Enable = true` per `PluginMetadata.Enable`). A user who carefully disabled some plugins to manage performance loses that configuration on every settings-file corruption event.
- **Suggested fix:** Same fix as F-039 (atomic temp-then-rename) and F-040 (try/catch around deserialize, fall back to fresh metadata with a console warning). Both fixes are upstream of this file — no change needed here once those are fixed. Severity ranking matches F-039 = high.
- **Risk if left:** Inherits F-039 + F-040 risk for plugin enable state. User-facing impact: enabled plugins re-enable on next run (default `Enable = true`), so the *bad* outcome is "plugins re-enable themselves" — possibly *enabling* something the user disabled for stability. That's a behavior regression at minimum and could re-enable a buggy plugin.

### F-068 — `Program.Main` writes `Error.log` to a relative path that depends on CWD

- **File:** `GameHelper/Program.cs:25`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Settings / IO
- **Description:** `File.AppendAllText("Error.log", ...)` uses a relative filename. The resolved path is `Environment.CurrentDirectory + "Error.log"` — wherever the OS launched the process from. If the user double-clicks the exe in Explorer, CWD is the exe folder. If launched from the Launcher project, CWD is the Launcher's directory. If launched from a Steam shortcut or `dotnet run`, CWD can be anywhere (Steam: typically Steam's install dir, which is not writable without elevation).
- **Why it's a bug:** The error log lands in different folders for different launchers; users who hit a crash can't find it. If CWD is non-writable (Program Files, Steam directory), the `AppendAllText` itself throws — recursing into the unhandled-exception handler if not caught — silent loss of the log.
- **Suggested fix:** Resolve the path against the assembly directory:
  ```csharp
  var logPath = Path.Combine(AppContext.BaseDirectory, "Error.log");
  File.AppendAllText(logPath, ...);
  ```
  Wrap in `try/catch` to handle the read-only-directory case. Better still, write to `%LOCALAPPDATA%\GameHelper\Error.log` (the user's profile, always writable).
- **Risk if left:** Crash diagnostics scattered or lost; user can't find the log; nested crash if CWD non-writable.

### F-163 — `State.FontPathName` defaults to a Windows-specific hardcoded path — fresh install with the font missing fails first font load

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/State.cs:90`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Settings / IO
- **Description:** Line 90: `public string FontPathName = @"C:\Windows\Fonts\msyh.ttc";`. This is the Microsoft YaHei font, distributed only with Chinese-language Windows installations (and some other east-Asian SKUs). On English / European Windows, the file is absent, and `Core.Overlay.ReplaceFont(...)` (per F-161) throws `FileNotFoundException`. The default `FontLanguage = ChineseSimplifiedCommon` (line 100) compounds the issue — a non-Chinese user would prefer English glyph ranges and a Latin font like Tahoma or Segoe UI.
- **Why it's a bug:** On a fresh install with no `core_settings.json`, the field initializer fires, the user clicks "Apply Changes" in the font widget, and the font load fails, killing the settings render coroutine (F-161). The user has no way to recover without editing JSON. The default seems to assume a Chinese-language target audience, which may be intentional — but the comment on the field gives no indication of why this specific font was chosen.
- **Suggested fix:** Default to a font that ships with all Windows SKUs: `@"C:\Windows\Fonts\segoeui.ttf"` (Segoe UI). Or use a font *bundled* with GameHelper2 in `Resources/fonts/` (like the existing C++ POEFixer pattern). Default `FontLanguage` to `English` to match. Add a try/file-exists check at startup that falls back to a known-good font if the saved path is missing.
- **Risk if left:** Non-Chinese-Windows users hit a font-load error on first font customization attempt. Recoverable only via manual JSON edit.

### F-165 — `State.CoreSettingFile` / `PluginsMetadataFile` / `PluginsDirectory` use CWD-relative `FileInfo` / `DirectoryInfo` — extension of F-068 across the settings layer

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/State.cs:24, 30, 36`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** Settings / IO
- **Description:** Lines 24, 30, 36:
  ```csharp
  public static readonly FileInfo CoreSettingFile = new("configs/core_settings.json");
  public static readonly FileInfo PluginsMetadataFile = new("configs/plugins.json");
  public static readonly DirectoryInfo PluginsDirectory = new("Plugins");
  ```
  All three are constructed with relative paths. `FileInfo("configs/...")` resolves against the *current working directory* (CWD), not the executable's directory. If GameHelper2 is launched via shortcut with a different "Start in" folder, or via `Process.Start` from another tool, or the CWD changes via `Directory.SetCurrentDirectory`, the settings/plugins paths point to the wrong location.
  
  Same pattern as F-068 (`Program.Main` writes `Error.log` to a CWD-relative path) and F-143 (`AreaInstance.EntitiesWidget` Dump button uses CWD-relative `entity_dumps/`).
- **Why it's a bug:** A Steam-launched GameHelper2 with a working dir set by Steam's launcher (typically the install directory) will work. A power-user wrapper that launches from a different directory will silently fail to load settings (file not found → defaults used → user's customizations appear lost) and silently fail to load plugins (Plugins dir not found → no plugins).
- **Suggested fix:** Resolve all paths against `AppContext.BaseDirectory`:
  ```csharp
  private static readonly string BaseDir = AppContext.BaseDirectory;
  public static readonly FileInfo CoreSettingFile = new(Path.Combine(BaseDir, "configs", "core_settings.json"));
  // ... same for the other two
  ```
- **Risk if left:** Settings invisibly drop on launches with non-default CWD. Common symptom: "my settings reset themselves".

### F-088 — `PluginMetadata` has no schema version field — future schema changes will fail silently or break user metadata

- **File:** `GameHelper/Plugin/PluginMetadata.cs:6-12`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Settings / IO
- **Description:** `internal class PluginMetadata { public bool Enable { get; set; } = true; }`. Single field. The on-disk JSON for `configs/plugins.json` is `Dictionary<string, PluginMetadata>`. There's no schema version. If a future version adds `LastEnabledAt`, `MinHostVersion`, or `Pinned`, old metadata files lack those fields — Newtonsoft will use the property's default value, which is fine until a default-of-default conflict (e.g., new `bool Pinned { get; set; } = false;` — but if the policy is "all loaded plugins should be Pinned by default unless user opted out", silent default-to-false is wrong).
- **Why it's a bug:** Standard hygiene for any persisted schema is a version field. The cost is one int property; the upside is graceful migration. Combined with F-040 (no try/catch on deserialize), schema changes that change a property type (`bool` → `enum`) silently corrupt user metadata.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `public int SchemaVersion { get; set; } = 1;` and check it in `LoadPluginMetadata`. If the loaded version is older, run a migration; if newer (downgrade), warn and reset.
- **Risk if left:** Latent. Schema changes today require a "delete configs/plugins.json on version bump" workaround that nobody has needed yet — but the first time someone needs to migrate metadata, the absence of a version field forces a destructive reset.

### F-166 — `State.PoiMonstersCategories2` field name carries an undocumented schema-migration `2` suffix — no schema version field, no `[JsonProperty]` rename, no migration log

- **File:** `GameHelper/Settings/State.cs:204`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** Settings / IO
- **Description:** Line 204: `public List<(EntityFilterType filtertype, string filter, Rarity rarity, GameStats stat, int group)> PoiMonstersCategories2 = new();`. The `2` suffix on the field name suggests a previous version (`PoiMonstersCategories`) existed with a different shape (different tuple, different name) and was migrated to the current shape. The migration path is undocumented:
  - No `[JsonProperty("PoiMonstersCategoriesV2")]` to clarify the schema name.
  - No corresponding `[JsonIgnore]` field for the legacy `PoiMonstersCategories` to allow auto-migration.
  - No schema-version field on `State` to enable version-aware migration logic.
  - No CHANGELOG entry referencing the migration.
  
  Same pattern as F-088 (`PluginMetadata` has no schema version field).
- **Why it's a bug:** Future schema changes will repeat the pattern: rename to `PoiMonstersCategories3`, lose old user data silently. A user who hasn't launched GameHelper2 in a year and had categories saved under the old shape sees them silently dropped.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a `public int SchemaVersion = 2;` field on `State`. On `JsonHelper.CreateOrLoadJsonFile`, if `SchemaVersion < currentVersion`, run a migration function. Document the schema in a `docs/schema/state-v{N}.md` file.
- **Risk if left:** Latent — silent data loss on next major schema change. Same family as F-088.


### GameOffsets struct correctness

### F-004 — Default-constructed `Pattern` NPEs in `ToString()` and consumers

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:8-122`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** `Pattern` is a `public struct` with reference-type fields `Data` (`byte[]`) and `Mask` (`bool[]`). The default value (`default(Pattern)`) has both arrays `null`. `ToString()` then calls `this.Data.Length`, throwing `NullReferenceException`.
- **Why it's a bug:** Structs in C# always have an implicit parameterless constructor that produces a zero-initialized instance. Anyone who allocates an empty `Pattern[]` and assigns the default value (or fails to fill a slot) gets an unusable struct that crashes on `ToString` or pattern-matching.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) change `Pattern` to a `class` (it is logically immutable reference data), or (b) make `ToString()` and other consumers tolerate `null` arrays, or (c) add an `IsValid` property that callers must check.
- **Risk if left:** Unlikely in current code (all `Pattern` instances are constructed inline in `StaticOffsetsPatterns`), but a real trap for anyone building patterns dynamically.

### F-010 — `1 << pos` is `int` shift, not `uint`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/Util.cs:10-15`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** `(x & (1 << pos)) != 0` shifts the literal `1` (typed `int`) by `pos`. The XML comment for `isBitSetUint` says "Pos can be any number from 0 to 31". For `pos = 31`, `1 << 31` is `int.MinValue` (`0x80000000` reinterpreted as signed = `-2_147_483_648`).
- **Why it's a bug:** When the operand types are mixed (`uint x` and `int (1 << 31)`), the C# spec promotes both to `long` for `&`, so the result happens to come out correct. But the code is fragile: a future refactor that, for instance, changes `x` to `int`, or extends `isBitSetUint` to handle 64-bit values, would silently break. Today's known callers only pass `pos = 0` (`IS_VISIBLE_BINARY_POS`, `SHOULD_MODIFY_BINARY_POS`), so the issue is dormant.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `(x & (1u << pos)) != 0` for `isBitSetUint` and document/guard `pos` range.
- **Risk if left:** Latent footgun for any future caller passing `pos >= 31`.

### F-011 — Public static mutable `Func` fields

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/Util.cs:5-16`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** `isBitSetByte` and `isBitSetUint` are `public static Func<...>` (not `readonly`). Any caller can reassign them globally.
- **Why it's a bug:** Tampering hazard; also forces an indirection (delegate invoke) on every call. A static method would be both safer and faster.
- **Suggested fix:** Convert to `public static bool IsBitSet(byte x, int pos) => ...;` (also fixing the casing convention — these look like field names because they are fields, but they are effectively functions).
- **Risk if left:** Latent tampering; minor perf cost in hot paths (entity-flag checks fire often).

### F-013 — `Size` as `int` silently truncates 64-bit length in `StdList`/`StdMap`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/StdList.cs:13-18`, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdMap.cs:13-18`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** Both structs declare `public int Size; public int PAD_C;` with the comment `"according to debugger this is long but for now int is working fine."` The native field is 64-bit (`size_t`); the upper 32 bits land in `PAD_C` and are silently dropped.
- **Why it's a bug:** A POE container with > 2^31 elements would be observed as a small/negative `Size`. In practice, no in-game container reaches 2^31 elements, so this is a documented behavioral limit, not a live bug.
- **Suggested fix:** Promote to `public long Size;` and remove `PAD_C`. The traversal code in `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdMap`/`ReadStdList` uses sentinel/parent pointers and a counter, so `Size` from the struct is mostly informational — the change is low-risk.
- **Risk if left:** None today; documents a known correctness gap.

### F-014 — `Length`/`Capacity` as `int` silently truncates 64-bit length in `StdString`/`StdWString`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/StdString.cs:7-27`, `GameOffsets/Natives/StdWString.cs:11-31`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** Same shape as F-013: `Length` and `Capacity` are 32-bit; the upper 32 bits go into `PAD_14`/`PAD_1C`. Comment in `StdWString.cs` explicitly notes `"according to debugger this is long but for now int is working fine."`
- **Why it's a bug:** A string longer than 2^31 bytes would be misread. Strings of that size do not appear in POE, so this is a documented behavioral limit.
- **Suggested fix:** Promote to `long`. Adjust the SSO offset arithmetic in `SafeMemoryHandle.ReadStdString`/`ReadStdWString` if needed.
- **Risk if left:** None today.

### F-024 — `WorldDataOffset.CameraStructurePtr` is misnamed — embedded struct, not a pointer

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/WorldDataOffset.cs:15`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** `[FieldOffset(0xA0)] public CameraStructure CameraStructurePtr;` — the field type is the inline `CameraStructure` value (~0x100+ bytes including the embedded `Matrix4x4 WorldToScreenMatrix`), not an `IntPtr`. The `Ptr` suffix is a holdover from earlier offset versions where this slot held a pointer.
- **Why it's a bug:** A reader scanning the struct definition will assume they need to deref a pointer at `WorldData+0xA0` to reach the camera; in fact the camera lives at `WorldData+0xA0` directly, with the world-to-screen matrix at `WorldData+0x1A0`. The misnomer has already caused confusion in the C++/POE2Fixer codebase per its CLAUDE.md (the project has documented a special note: `CameraStructure is EMBEDDED at WorldData+0xA0 (not a pointer!) — matrix at WorldData+0x1A0`). Renaming the field eliminates the trap.
- **Suggested fix:** Rename `CameraStructurePtr` → `Camera` (or `CameraStructure`). Update the consumer in `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/States/InGameStateObjects/WorldData.cs` (single reference).
- **Risk if left:** Continuing developer confusion; high risk that someone "fixes" the read path to dereference a pointer that isn't there, producing a torn read or NPE.

### F-110 — `GameStats` enum members use snake_case — violates PascalCase, generated by sed pipeline; cast `(GameStats)newStat.key` relies on a fragile +1 offset contract documented only in a NOTE comment

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/GameStats.cs:16-24884`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Two concerns in one enum:
  1. **Naming**: All ~24,880 members are snake_case (`level`, `item_drop_slots`, `main_hand_weapon_type`). This violates PascalCase. The header comment shows the snake_case is generated by a sed script from the .dat-file's Id column. Renaming would break a source-of-truth contract with the dat file.
  2. **+1 offset contract**: The pattern is `level = 0 + 1, item_drop_slots = 1 + 1, ...`, with a NOTE at line 13 reading `"flask_charges_used_+% whatever you read in _rid, add +1 to it."` and at line 12 `"Do not forget to add '= 1' on the first enum."` This means the enum value is `(dat_id) + 1`, and the consumer cast `(GameStats)newStat.key` at `ComponentBase.cs:73` requires `newStat.key` to also be in the +1 form (game stores stat IDs as `dat_id + 1`, presumably). The contract is documented only in the source comment, not in any test, runtime assertion, or the cast site itself.
- **Why it's a bug:** (a) Naming violates conventions but is locked by the sed pipeline. (b) The +1 contract is fragile: if the upstream dat schema changes (adds a stat at the start, removes one in the middle), regenerating the enum via sed silently shifts every ID by one — every consumer of `GameStats` (e.g., `ComponentBase.cs:73` which builds a per-entity stats dictionary) is now reading the wrong stat. There's no compile-time check, no runtime sanity probe (e.g., "the stat ID for `level` should always be 1; if not, dat schema changed").
- **Suggested fix:** (a) Naming: leave snake_case but add a `[CLSCompliant(false)]` style suppression document so reviewers don't keep re-flagging; or rewrite as PascalCase + an `EnumMemberAttribute` on each (impractical for 24k entries). Recommendation: leave as-is, document the convention exception in a header comment. (b) +1 contract: add a runtime startup assertion in `Core.Initialize` (or a unit test) that probes a known-stable stat ID at a known position, and emit a clear log if the assertion fails: `if ((int)GameStats.level != 1) Console.WriteLine("[GameStats] Schema drift detected — regenerate enum from latest Stats.dat.");`. The assertion need only check 2-3 known-stable IDs; if those drift, the user knows to regenerate.
- **Risk if left:** Naming concern is cosmetic. The +1 contract risk is latent — silent stat misclassification on game patch — and the only diagnostic is "stats look weird".

### F-111 — `InventoryName` mixes real slots, `DONOTUSE5`, `UNUSED1` placeholders — silent index alignment to .dat file with no compile-time enforcement of the off-by-one comment-documented invariant

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/InventoryName.cs:13-124`
- **Severity:** low
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** The XML doc says: *"in the game, inventory index starts from 0x01. In the Inventories.dat file, inventory index starts from 0x00."* The enum starts with `NoInvSelected = 0` (implicit), then `MainInventory1 = 1`, etc. This means the enum value matches the in-game index (game's `0x01` → enum `1`, not the dat-file `0x00`). The cast `(InventoryName)inventoryData[i].InventoryId` at `ServerData.cs:122` works only if `InventoryId` is the in-game index (1-based), per the doc. The enum also contains `DONOTUSE5, DONOTUSE1, DONOTUSE2, ..., DONOTUSE7, DONOTUSE6, UNUSED1, UNUSED2` — placeholder slots inserted to keep enum values aligned with dat-file indices when slots were removed in past game patches.
- **Why it's a bug:** Two concerns:
  1. The 1-based-vs-0-based contract is documented only in an XML comment (lines 7-11). A future maintainer regenerating the enum from a fresh Inventories.dat (which is 0-based) would naturally start at `MainInventory1 = 0`, breaking every consumer cast silently.
  2. The `DONOTUSE` / `UNUSED` placeholders are necessary scaffolding but visible to plugin authors via IntelliSense. A plugin checking `if (inv == InventoryName.DONOTUSE5) ...` would compile clean but be obviously wrong; there's no compile-time hint that these are non-functional.
- **Suggested fix:** (a) Make the off-by-one explicit by adding `= 1` to `MainInventory1` (line 16) so a future regeneration cannot silently miss it: `MainInventory1 = 1, BodyArmour1, /* ... */`. (b) Mark the placeholders with `[Obsolete("Reserved/unused slot — do not consume.", error: true)]` to make consumption a compile-time error. The `error: true` flag would force any code referencing `DONOTUSE5` to fail compilation, leaving the enum value as a silent index-alignment placeholder only. (c) Add a unit-test-style runtime assertion in `Core.Initialize` similar to the F-110 fix.
- **Risk if left:** Latent — the comment-documented invariant is the only line of defense against a regeneration mistake. Same family as F-110 (offset enum drift on dat schema change).

### F-005 — `Pattern.ToString` string concatenation in loop

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Pattern.cs:104-121`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** `data += $"0x{this.Data[i]:X} ";` inside a `for (var i = 0; i < this.Data.Length; i++)` loop — quadratic allocation pattern.
- **Why it's a bug:** Patterns are short (< 30 bytes) and `ToString` is called only for diagnostics, so impact is negligible. Still, `StringBuilder` is the idiomatic approach.
- **Suggested fix:** Switch to `StringBuilder`.
- **Risk if left:** None practically; pure hygiene.

### F-015 — `StdTuple3D` missing constructor (asymmetry with `StdTuple2D`)

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Natives/StdTuple3D.cs:6-16`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness
- **Description:** `StdTuple2D<T>` has a `(T x, T y)` constructor; `StdTuple3D<T>` does not have a `(T x, T y, T z)` constructor. Callers that want a non-default `StdTuple3D` must use object-initializer syntax or an aggregate-init.
- **Why it's a bug:** Inconsistent API surface; not a defect.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a `public StdTuple3D(T x, T y, T z) { ... }` constructor for symmetry.
- **Risk if left:** None.

### F-018 — `IGNORE_FIRST_X_AREAS` comment "Feel free to set it to 0" misleads — field is `readonly`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/LoadedFilesOffset.cs:32-34`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** `public static readonly int IGNORE_FIRST_X_AREAS = 2;` is preceded by the comment `// This saves a hell lot of memory but for debugging purposes / Feel free to set it to 0.` But because the field is `readonly`, only the field initializer (or static constructor) can assign it — a runtime caller cannot set it to `0` without recompiling.
- **Why it's a bug:** The comment is actively misleading to any developer reading it. They'd try `FileInfoValueStruct.IGNORE_FIRST_X_AREAS = 0;` from a Debug menu and get a compile error.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) change the comment to "Recompile with this set to 0 to disable filtering" or (b) drop `readonly` and accept it as a debug-only mutable knob (with the F-017-class trade-off acknowledged).
- **Risk if left:** Developer time wasted; no runtime impact.

### F-019 — `[StructLayout(Explicit, Pack = 1)]` — `Pack` is ignored under `Explicit` layout

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/GameStateOffsets.cs:13,19`, `GameOffsets/Objects/LoadedFilesOffset.cs:22`, `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameStateOffset.cs:7,15`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Multiple structs in these files are decorated with `[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Explicit, Pack = 1)]`. Per the Microsoft .NET documentation: "The `Pack` field affects the placement of fields when the layout is `Sequential` or `Auto`. It has no effect on `Explicit` layout." All field positions are determined by `[FieldOffset(...)]` directly.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but the `Pack = 1` is dead annotation noise that suggests the author expected it to do something. A future reader could mis-interpret it as load-bearing.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop `Pack = 1` from all `Explicit`-layout structs. Keep it only on `Sequential` structs where it actually controls field alignment.
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic.

### F-020 — `[StructLayout(Sequential, Pack = 1)]` redundant on `[InlineArray]` struct

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/GameStateOffsets.cs:26-31`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** `GameStateBuffer` is decorated with both `[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Pack = 1)]` AND `[InlineArray(GameStateHelper.TOTAL_STATES)]`. With `[InlineArray]`, the runtime treats the struct as `N` repetitions of its single field, and the resulting layout is fully determined by the inline-array attribute and the field's natural size (16 bytes for `StdTuple2D<IntPtr>`, so 192 bytes total for `N=12`). The `[StructLayout]` attribute is not required and `Pack = 1` has no effect because `StdTuple2D<IntPtr>` is naturally aligned.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but it's confusing. A reader has to verify that the explicit `Sequential, Pack = 1` doesn't conflict with `[InlineArray]` semantics.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop `[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Pack = 1)]` from `GameStateBuffer`. Rely solely on `[InlineArray(N)]`.
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic.

### F-021 — `AreaChangeOffset.counter` field name violates PascalCase convention

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/AreaChangeOffset.cs:8`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** `public struct AreaChangeOffset { public int counter; }` — the field name `counter` is lowercase. Every other public field in the offset structs in this directory uses `PascalCase` (e.g. `LoadedFiles`, `FilesPointer`, `AreaChangeCount`, `Name`, `GameState`, `States`).
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but inconsistent naming hurts readability and would trip a CodeAnalysis style rule (CA1707/IDExxx) if enabled. The matching consumer `AreaChangeCounter.cs:54` reads it as `.counter` so renaming requires a one-line consumer fix.
- **Suggested fix:** Rename to `Counter` and update the single consumer reference.
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic.

### F-022 — `[StructLayout(Explicit, Pack = 1)]` `Pack` is ignored — extension of F-019 across all 32 audited Component/State/UiElement structs

- **File:** Every `[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Explicit, Pack = 1)]` in this batch:
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Actor.cs:7,25,54,81` (4 structs)
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Animated.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Buffs.cs:7,14`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Charges.cs:6,14`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Chest.cs:6,14`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/ComponentHeader.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Life.cs:6,15`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/ModsAndObjectMagicProperties.cs:7,14,21,39`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Player.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Positioned.cs:5`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Render.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Shrine.cs:5`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/StackOffsets.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/StateMachine.cs:7`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Stats.cs:7,17`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Targetable.cs:5`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Transitionable.cs:5`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/TriggerableBlockage.cs:5`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/FilesStructures/BuffDefinitionsOffset.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/FilesStructures/GrantedEffectsDatOffset.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/FilesStructures/GrantedEffectsPerLevelDatOffset.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/FilesStructures/WorldAreaDatOffsets.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/AreaLoadingStateOffset.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:7,47,110,131`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/EntityOffsets.cs:7,16,34,42`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/ImportantUiElementsOffsets.cs:9,18,25`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/InventoryOffset.cs:7,13,46`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/ServerDataOffset.cs:7,13,19`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/WorldDataOffset.cs:11,18,24`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/UiElement/MapUiElement.cs:6`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/UiElement/SkillTreeNodeUiElement.cs:6,13,19`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/UiElement/UiElementBaseOffset.cs:7`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Same defect as F-019. `Pack` only affects `Sequential` and `Auto` layout — it has no effect under `Explicit`. Every offset struct in this batch (~50 declarations across 32 files) carries `Pack = 1` redundantly.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not, but it's misleading boilerplate. New offset structs inherit the cargo-culted attribute, suggesting `Pack = 1` is doing something here.
- **Suggested fix:** Bulk-strip `, Pack = 1` from every `[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Explicit, ...)]` in `GameOffsets/Objects/`. Keep `Pack = 1` only on `Sequential` and `Auto` structs that genuinely need it (e.g. `[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Pack = 1)]` on `ActiveSkillStructure`, `EnvironmentStruct`, `EntityListStruct`, `EntityNodeKey/Value`, `SubTileStruct`, `TgtFileStruct`, `ItemHashKey/Value`, `ComponentNameAndIndexStruct`, `DeployedEntityStructure`, `AllModsType`, `StatArrayStruct` — all use `Sequential` and there `Pack = 1` matters).
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic. Mass code change with mechanical regex; recommend a single sed pass.

### F-027 — Lowercase / mixed-case public field names violate PascalCase convention — extension of F-021

- **File:** Every non-PascalCase public field across the audited offset structs:
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Charges.cs:11` — `current`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Stats.cs:26-27` — `key`, `value`
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Targetable.cs:17` — `HiddenfromPlayer` (should be `HiddenFromPlayer`)
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:64-65` — `id`, `pad_0x24` (in `EntityNodeKey`)
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/AreaInstanceOffsets.cs:137-138` — `tileIdX`, `tileIdY` (in `TileStructure`)
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/EntityOffsets.cs:37` — `name` (in `EntityDetails`)
  - `GameOffsets/Objects/States/InGameState/InventoryOffset.cs:10` — `ptr` (in `PreInventoryStruct`)
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Same defect family as F-021. `Pack`-style padding fields in this codebase consistently use `PAD_` prefix + hex byte index (`PAD_0x18`, `PAD_8`, `PAD_C`), so the lowercase `pad_0x24` is the inconsistency, not the prefix idea. The other lowercase fields (`current`, `key`, `value`, `id`, `name`, `ptr`, `tileIdX`, `tileIdY`) violate PascalCase outright. `HiddenfromPlayer` is partial PascalCase ("from" should be capitalized).
- **Why it's a bug:** Inconsistent naming; would trip CA1707/IDE1006 if enabled. Each rename requires touching the matching consumer (typically 1-3 references each in `GameHelper/`).
- **Suggested fix:** Rename to PascalCase: `Current`, `Key`, `Value`, `Id`, `PAD_0x24`, `TileIdX`, `TileIdY`, `Name`, `Ptr`, `HiddenFromPlayer`. Update consumers in tandem.
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic.

### F-028 — `RenderOffsets.CharactorModelBounds` typo (should be `CharacterModelBounds`)

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Render.cs:19`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Field is spelled `CharactorModelBounds` (with `o`); should be `CharacterModelBounds` (with `e`). Typo predates the .NET migration.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but typo'd identifiers leak into IntelliSense and any string-based reflection.
- **Suggested fix:** Rename. Single consumer reference (if any) updates trivially; the field comment notes "This might be useless" so it may have no consumers at all.
- **Risk if left:** None.

### F-030 — `ActiveSkillCooldown.TotalActiveCooldowns()` uses magic-number element size `0x10`

- **File:** `GameOffsets/Objects/Components/Actor.cs:70-73`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** `(int)this.CooldownsList.TotalElements(0x10)` — the `0x10` is the size of a per-cooldown entry (likely `IntPtr + IntPtr` = 16 bytes, but that struct isn't named here). Other call sites in this codebase use `Marshal.SizeOf<T>()` or a named const for this purpose.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but if the per-cooldown entry shape ever grows (e.g. a 24-byte entry per league), the call site silently miscounts elements. A named struct + `Marshal.SizeOf<CooldownEntry>()` makes the dependency explicit.
- **Suggested fix:** Define a `CooldownEntry` struct (or repurpose an existing one) and switch to `(int)this.CooldownsList.TotalElements(Marshal.SizeOf<CooldownEntry>())`. Even a `const int CooldownEntrySize = 0x10;` next to the call site would document intent.
- **Risk if left:** Hidden coupling to a 0x10-byte stride; will silently produce wrong cooldown counts if game struct grows.

### F-105 — `GameWindowScale.UpdateData` redundant `- 0` and `Cull.Value - Cull.Value` instead of `2 * Cull.Value`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteObjects/GameWindowScale.cs:92-93`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Line 92: `(Core.Process.WindowArea.Width - Core.GameCull.Value - Core.GameCull.Value) / UiElementBaseFuncs.BaseResolution.X`. Line 93: `(Core.Process.WindowArea.Height - 0) / UiElementBaseFuncs.BaseResolution.Y`. The `- Core.GameCull.Value - Core.GameCull.Value` is `- 2 * Core.GameCull.Value` (left + right black-bar cull). The `- 0` on line 93 is dead code from a prior refactor where vertical cull existed.
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but the form `- a - a` reads as a typo of `- a + b` and forces a reviewer to verify whether two different cull values were intended. The `- 0` is just noise.
- **Suggested fix:** `(Core.Process.WindowArea.Width - 2 * Core.GameCull.Value) / UiElementBaseFuncs.BaseResolution.X` and `Core.Process.WindowArea.Height / UiElementBaseFuncs.BaseResolution.Y`. Self-documenting.
- **Risk if left:** None — purely cosmetic.

### F-108 — `EntitySubtypes.ChestWithRareRarity` doc comment is a copy-paste of `ChestWithMagicRarity`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/Entity/EntitySubtypes.cs:32-40`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Both `ChestWithMagicRarity` (line 35) and `ChestWithRareRarity` (line 40) carry the docstring `"A <see cref="EntityTypes.Chest"/> that have magic or above rarity on them."`. The latter should describe rare rarity ("A Chest entity that has rare or above rarity on it") — the comment was copy-pasted and not updated.
- **Why it's a bug:** Docstring inaccuracy. IntelliSense shows the wrong description for `ChestWithRareRarity`. Plugin authors reading the docstring will mis-categorize.
- **Suggested fix:** Update line 38: `/// A <see cref="EntityTypes.Chest"/> that has rare or above rarity on it.` Verify the docstring matches the corresponding rarity threshold in the entity-classification logic that uses these enum values.
- **Risk if left:** Minor reader confusion; no runtime impact.

### F-109 — `EntityFilterType` member names use ALLCAPS — violates PascalCase + serializes to JSON in that form via `StringEnumConverter`

- **File:** `GameHelper/RemoteEnums/Entity/EntityFilterType.cs:11-18`
- **Severity:** nit
- **Category:** GameOffsets struct correctness (code quality)
- **Description:** Members are `PATH, PATHANDRARITY, MOD, MODANDRARITY, PATHANDSTAT`. The enum is `[JsonConverter(typeof(StringEnumConverter))]`, so values serialize as `"PATH"`, `"PATHANDRARITY"`, etc. into user settings JSON (`SettingsWindow.cs:30, 259` are the live consumers). The naming violates .NET PascalCase convention (`Path`, `PathAndRarity`, ...).
- **Why it's a bug:** It's not — but the persistent-storage form is locked to ALLCAPS. Renaming for style would break user setting files (deserialization fails on `"PATH"` if the enum is renamed to `Path`). The naming is therefore intentionally frozen, but the convention violation propagates wherever `EntityFilterType.PATH` is referenced in code (e.g., `Entity.cs:687-697`) — every call site reads as a SHOUTING constant.
- **Suggested fix:** Two options. (a) Leave as-is — the persistence cost of renaming is real. (b) Rename to PascalCase (`Path`, `PathAndRarity`, `Mod`, `ModAndRarity`, `PathAndStat`) and add an `EnumMemberAttribute` to each that pins the JSON serialization name to the old ALLCAPS form for backward compatibility:
  ```csharp
  [System.Runtime.Serialization.EnumMember(Value = "PATH")]
  Path,
  ```
  Option (b) restores convention without breaking user data. Lowest-risk path forward.
- **Risk if left:** Cosmetic; consistent SHOUTING constants in source. No runtime impact.
